\section{Finite-Audit Reformulation of the Remaining TECT Microscopic Program}

\subsection{Goal}

The correct next step is not to introduce a new qualitative mechanism,
but to rewrite the remaining open microscopic questions as a finite operator audit
for the actual linearized Bloch operator of the refined locked TECT branch.

Let
\[
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
P_0=z_0 z_0^\dagger,
\qquad
\chi\gg 1,
\]
and let the full microscopic linearization around the chosen defect/background be denoted by
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}(p).
\]
Fix the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and let
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}
=
\mathcal H_D \oplus \mathcal H_R,
\qquad
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
where \(\mathcal H_D\) is the shell-relevant doubled local block and \(\mathcal H_R\) is the remote sector.

The purpose of this section is to reduce all remaining open tasks to finite checks on
\[
\Pi_D \mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)\Pi_D,
\qquad
\Pi_D \mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}(0)\Pi_R,
\qquad
\Pi_R \mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)\Pi_R,
\]
where \(\Pi_D,\Pi_R\) are the corresponding spectral/projected block projectors.

\subsection{Step A. Actual witness carrier audit}

The first question is whether the actual microscopic TECT linearization contains
a nontrivial shell-relevant \((i,a)\)-carrier channel.

Let the shell-relevant enriched tensor space be
\[
V_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
\{N^a_{ij}\ \text{surviving the actual microscopic linearization}\}.
\]
For each transverse shell direction \(e_\alpha\), \(\alpha=1,2\), define
\[
C^\alpha_j(N)=e_{\alpha i}N^{a_\alpha}_{ij},
\qquad
L_\alpha(N)=G_{*j}C^\alpha_j(N)=G_{*j}e_{\alpha i}N^{a_\alpha}_{ij}.
\]
Then the witness condition is
\[
L_1(N)\neq 0,
\qquad
L_2(N)\neq 0.
\]

The key theorem-level fact is the following dichotomy:
either \(L_\alpha\equiv 0\) on \(V_{\mathrm{enr}}\) by an exact symmetry prohibition,
or else \(L_\alpha\neq 0\) on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{\mathrm{enr}}\).
Therefore the actual carrier audit reduces to constructing a single admissible witness
\[
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\in V_{\mathrm{enr}}
\]
such that
\[
L_\alpha\bigl(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\alpha)}\bigr)\neq 0.
\]

Hence the completion criterion for Step A is:
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,N^{(1)}_{\mathrm{seed}},N^{(2)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\in V_{\mathrm{enr}}
\ \text{with}\
L_1(N^{(1)}_{\mathrm{seed}})\neq 0,\quad
L_2(N^{(2)}_{\mathrm{seed}})\neq 0.
}
\]

\subsection{Step B. Opposite-valley survival and matching}

Let
\[
W^\pm=(W^\pm_\parallel,W^\pm_I,W^\pm_J)
\]
denote the shell witness triples extracted from the projected \(+\) and \(-\) valleys
in matched opposite-valley frames.

The actual Dirac pairing condition is
\[
\boxed{
W^- = W^+.
}
\]
This is not a conceptual problem any more; it is an explicit finite comparison problem:
one must project the actual microscopic operator to both shell blocks and compare the three coefficients.

The completion criterion for Step B is the explicit equality
\[
\boxed{
W_\parallel^- = W_\parallel^+,
\qquad
W_I^- = W_I^+,
\qquad
W_J^- = W_J^+.
}
\]

\subsection{Step C. Zero constant mixing as a finite label audit}

At \(p=0\), the full operator has block form
\[
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
If the residual symmetry group at the crossing is \(H_*\), then equivariance implies
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Therefore a sufficient and exact theorem-level criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

In the present TECT setting, the correct practical version is not an abstract
``ordinary cubic 2D irrep'' statement.
Rather, \(\mathcal H_D\) is the shell-relevant carrier
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
and each remote sector \(K_a\subset \mathcal H_R\) must differ from \(\mathcal H_D\)
in at least one shell-relevant label:
\[
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{additional conserved microscopic labels}.
\]

Thus Step C reduces to the finite table audit:
for every remote sector \(K_a\), check whether it matches \(\mathcal H_D\) in all labels.
If not, then
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]
If this holds for all \(a\), then
\[
V(0)=0.
\]

\subsection{Step D. Remote-gap audit}

The remote gap is an independent spectral property of the remote block:
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\qquad
\text{for }|p|\le p_*.
\]
This is not implied by the shell determinant.
Hence the correct theorem-level route is either:

\paragraph{Route D1: direct finite lower bound}
Split
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\]
where \(D_R\) is the diagonal or benchmark part and \(R_R\) the residual mixing.
Define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p))\bigr),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Route D2: bounded perturbation from a gapped benchmark}
If
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
\]
and
\[
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|<\Delta_0,
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta=\Delta_0-\sup\|\delta H_R\|>0.
}
\]

Hence Step D is a finite Bloch-spectral inequality problem.

\subsection{Step E. Mass-protection audit}

The doubled local Dirac block has the form
\[
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i).
\]
The space of genuine constant Dirac masses is
\[
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
\]
Therefore mass protection is exactly the finite operator-algebra condition
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
}
\]
where \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\) is the algebra of residual-symmetry-allowed constant Hermitian operators
on the isolated doubled block.

A sufficient mechanism is an exact residual valley symmetry.
If
\[
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
generates an exact \(U(1)_V\), then
\[
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0,
\]
while
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
transform nontrivially and are therefore forbidden.
The weaker discrete remnant \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) also suffices.

Hence Step E reduces to computing the residual constant operator algebra
\(A_{\mathrm{res}}\) from the actual microscopic symmetry realization
and checking its intersection with \(\mathcal M_D\).

\subsection{Step F. Combined finite-audit theorem}

Assume the actual microscopic realization satisfies:

\begin{enumerate}
\item there exist two admissible enriched witnesses with
\[
L_1\neq 0,\qquad L_2\neq 0;
\]
\item the opposite-valley witness triples match:
\[
W^- = W^+;
\]
\item the remote sectors satisfy the shell-relevant mismatch audit, hence
\[
V(0)=0;
\]
\item the remote block satisfies one of the gap inequalities above, hence
\[
\Delta>0;
\]
\item the residual constant operator algebra satisfies
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then, for \(|E|<\Delta/2\),
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)-\Sigma(E,p),
\qquad
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger,
\]
with
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i \Gamma_i
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
}
\]
with no allowed constant Dirac mass term.

Thus the complete remaining TECT microscopic frontier is reduced to a finite,
explicitly checkable operator audit on the actual projected Bloch linearization.

\subsection{Normalization constants and what they do not affect}

The overlap constants \(\nu_\parallel,\nu_\perp\) enter the dictionary
between the microscopic Class II parameters and the reduced witness coefficients:
\[
g_c=\nu_\parallel \Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\nu_\perp \Gamma c_I,
\qquad
g_O=\nu_\perp \Gamma c_J.
\]
They are needed for absolute normalization and quantitative matching,
but not for the purely existential Weyl/Dirac statement as long as they are finite and nonzero.
Therefore their determination is a calibration problem, not an existence obstruction.

\section{Final Summary}

The strongest honest current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the TECT local Dirac problem is not yet fully unconditionally closed,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{it has been reduced to a finite explicit microscopic audit problem.}
}
\]

The remaining finite audits are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(I) actual witness carrier realization,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(II) opposite-valley survival and matching,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(III) zero constant mixing } V(0)=0,}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(IV) positive remote gap } \Delta>0,}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(V) mass protection } A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.}
\]

More explicitly:

\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0,
\]
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho>0,
\]
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}
=
\{0\}
\Longrightarrow
\text{no constant Dirac mass.}
\]

Therefore, once the actual microscopic linearized Bloch operator passes these finite audits,

\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i \Gamma_i
+
O(|p|^2/\Delta),
}
\]
so the theory contains a spectrally isolated massless local Dirac cone.

Finally, the constants \(\nu_\parallel,\nu_\perp\) affect only the absolute normalization of the
microscopic-to-reduced dictionary, not the existential form of the Dirac/Weyl theorem.

\section{Actual Microscopic Carrier Audit}

\subsection{Goal}

The remaining microscopic question after the explicit Class II witness theorem is not whether
the shell-level witness logic is correct.
That part is already closed inside the concrete Class II truncation.

The actual remaining question is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the true microscopic TECT linearization contain a nontrivial shell-relevant }(i,a)\text{-carrier sector?}
}
\label{eq:actual_carrier_goal}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the issue is whether the full linearized transport operator, after projection to the relevant defect/shell sector, contains a nonzero component in the explicit seed space that generates the reduced witness coefficients
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\subsection{What the witness actually needs}

The shell-level Weyl/Dirac witness is controlled by the enriched tensor
\[
N^a_{ij},
\]
through the shell-adapted coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta,
\]
or equivalently
\[
A,\qquad B,\qquad C.
\]

The minimal shell-adapted tensor family is
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_minimal_family}
\end{equation}

Therefore the microscopic carrier must simultaneously supply:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index \(i\) or \(j\),
\item one reduced internal / shell-tangent index \(a\).
\end{enumerate}

This is the structural meaning of an \((i,a)\)-carrier.

\subsection{Finite-dimensional witness functionals}

Let \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) be the finite-dimensional vector space of symmetry-allowed microscopic enriched tensors surviving the linearization around the chosen defect background.

The shell witness functionals are:
\begin{equation}
W_\parallel(N):=g_c(N),
\qquad
W_E(N):=g_E(N),
\qquad
W_O(N):=g_O(N).
\label{eq:actual_carrier_W_def}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel(N)=c_\parallel W_\parallel(N),
\qquad
\alpha(N)=c_\perp W_E(N),
\qquad
\beta(N)=c_\perp W_O(N),
\label{eq:actual_carrier_lambda_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
with nonzero defect-overlap constants \(c_\parallel,c_\perp\).

Define the longitudinal and transverse witness conditions by
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak W_\parallel(N):=\lambda_\parallel(N)\neq 0,
\qquad
\det T_\perp(N):=\alpha(N)^2+\beta(N)^2\neq 0.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_two_witnesses}
\end{equation}

Since \(W_\parallel\) is linear and \(W_E^2+W_O^2\) is polynomial on \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\),
the witness problem is finite-dimensional from the start.

\subsection{Exact dichotomy: symmetry-forbidden versus generic nonvanishing}

Let \(V\subset W\) be the symmetry-allowed microscopic tensor space inside the ambient tensor space \(W\).
For each shell channel \(\alpha\), define the target covector
\[
T^{(\alpha)}_{ija}=e_i^\alpha G_*^{\,j}u_a^{(\alpha)}.
\]
Then the corresponding shell contraction is
\begin{equation}
L_\alpha(N)=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_Lalpha}
\end{equation}

If \(P_V:W\to V\) denotes the orthogonal projection onto the allowed tensor space, then
\begin{equation}
L_\alpha|_V\equiv 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_projectioncriterion}
\end{equation}

Hence exactly one of the following holds:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0\): the channel is symmetry-forbidden;
\item \(P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0\): the channel is generically nonvanishing on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore, to prove that a witness channel survives, it is enough to exhibit one admissible seed tensor with nonzero projection.

\subsection{Minimal UV classification of admissible carriers}

At lowest derivative order, any local microscopic extension capable of producing the reduced shell tensor must effectively introduce an \((i,a)\)-carrier.
The minimal viable classes are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Class I: direct shell--projector derivative couplings,
\item Class II: heavy auxiliary internal vector mediators \(X_i^a\),
\item Class III: connection-like mediators \(A_i^a\).
\end{enumerate}

Among these, Class II is the strongest current explicit class, because it dynamically generates the carrier rather than inserting it by hand.

\subsection{Explicit Class II carrier mechanism}

The explicit Class II UV structure is
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha\,X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta\,X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:actual_carrier_classII_UV}
\end{equation}

After elimination of the heavy mediator \(X_i^a\), the shell-relevant quadratic mixing takes the form
\begin{equation}
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^a X_i^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X X_i^a C^{ab}_{ij}(D_j\psi)\xi^b
+\mathrm{h.c.},
\label{eq:actual_carrier_classII_quad}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m^aC^{ab}_{ij}.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_deltaN}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\Gamma:=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_Gamma}
\end{equation}
For the shell-adapted seed family
\[
m^a=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
C^{31}_{ij}
=
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}
=
-\,c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_deltaABC}
\end{equation}

Thus the reduced witness coordinates satisfy
\begin{equation}
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_gc_gE_gO}
\end{equation}

This shows that the three Class II mediator directions correspond exactly to the three shell-reduced invariant coordinates:
\[
X_i^3 \leftrightarrow \text{longitudinal seed},
\qquad
X_i^1 \leftrightarrow \text{transverse-even seed},
\qquad
X_i^2 \leftrightarrow \text{transverse-odd seed}.
\]

\subsection{Seed subspace and embedding criterion}

Define the explicit seed space
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\left\{
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,E)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,O)}
\right\}.
\label{eq:actual_carrier_Vseed}
\end{equation}

The microscopic carrier audit succeeds if the actual microscopic linearization contains a nontrivial shell-relevant tensor subspace
\[
V_{\mathrm{car}}\subset V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\]
whose defect/shell projection has nonzero overlap with \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}\).

Equivalently, it is sufficient to find
\begin{equation}
N_{\parallel}\in V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\quad\text{such that}\quad
W_\parallel(N_{\parallel})\neq 0,
\label{eq:actual_carrier_longseed_condition}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
N_{\perp}\in V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\quad\text{such that}\quad
\bigl(W_E(N_{\perp}),W_O(N_{\perp})\bigr)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:actual_carrier_transseed_condition}
\end{equation}

Once these two seed conditions hold, finite-dimensional genericity implies that the good set
\[
W_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
W_E^2+W_O^2\neq 0
\]
is open, dense, and full measure inside the allowed carrier space.

\subsection{Operational microscopic audit}

The actual microscopic audit is therefore finite and explicit:

\paragraph{(A) Linearize the microscopic theory.}
Linearize the complete refined locked TECT equations around the relevant defect background
\[
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\]

\paragraph{(B) Extract the first-order transport kernel.}
Write the shell-relevant first-order operator in the form
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]

\paragraph{(C) Project to the low-mode sector.}
Choose the low-mode basis \(\{u_a^\pm\}\) at the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and compute
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]

\paragraph{(D) Match to the shell tensor basis.}
Read off the induced tensor coefficients in the basis
\[
\bigl(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,E)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,O)}\bigr),
\]
equivalently extract
\[
(A,B,C)
\quad\text{or}\quad
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\paragraph{(E) Perform the projection test.}
Verify
\begin{equation}
P_{V_{\mathrm{seed}}}N_{\mathrm{mic}}\neq 0,
\label{eq:actual_carrier_projectiontest}
\end{equation}
and more explicitly confirm the existence of:

\begin{enumerate}
\item at least one longitudinal seed component,
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0;
\]
\item at least one transverse seed component,
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Strongest honest theorem-level statement}

We can now state the precise theorem-level status.

\begin{theorem}[Actual microscopic carrier audit]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the refined locked TECT linearization admits a finite shell-relevant enriched tensor space \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\);
\item the microscopic carrier sector contains an effective \((i,a)\)-carrier channel;
\item after shell/defect projection, \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) contains one admissible longitudinal seed and one admissible transverse seed.
\end{enumerate}

Then the local shell witness survives:
\begin{equation}
W_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(W_E,W_O)\neq (0,0)
\end{equation}
on an open dense full-measure subset of the allowed carrier sector.

Equivalently, the shell-level local Weyl nondegeneracy is generically realized.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The longitudinal statement follows because \(W_\parallel\) is a linear functional on the allowed carrier space.
If it is nonzero on one admissible seed, then its zero set is a proper hyperplane.

The transverse statement follows because \(W_E^2+W_O^2\) is a nonzero polynomial once one admissible transverse seed exists.
Its zero set is then a proper algebraic subset.

Intersecting the two complementary good sets gives an open dense full-measure subset on which both conditions hold simultaneously.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Sharp honest frontier}

Thus the actual microscopic carrier problem is no longer conceptually open.
It is reduced to a finite yes/no projection test:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete microscopic TECT linearization project nontrivially onto the explicit shell-relevant seed space }V_{\mathrm{seed}}?
}
\label{eq:actual_carrier_final_question}
\end{equation}

Inside the concrete Class II truncation, the answer is already yes.
What remains open is only whether the final complete microscopic TECT realization actually contains that same nontrivial carrier sector in the physically relevant defect background.

%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of the Actual Microscopic Carrier Audit}

The actual microscopic carrier problem is not the infinite-dimensional question
``does some abstract witness exist?''
Rather, it is the finite projection problem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the true microscopic TECT linearization contain a shell-relevant }(i,a)\text{-carrier sector?}
}
\]

The witness requires the enriched tensor
\[
N^a_{ij},
\]
whose shell-adapted form is
\[
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\]

Thus the microscopic carrier must supply both:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one spatial derivative index}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\text{one reduced internal index.}
}
\]

At lowest derivative order, the admissible minimal carrier classes are:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class I, Class II, Class III.}
}
\]
Among them, Class II is the strongest current explicit class because it realizes all three seed coordinates simultaneously.

Its quadratic shell-relevant reduction yields
\[
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m^aC^{ab}_{ij},
\]
hence
\[
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J,
\qquad
\Gamma=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2},
\]
and therefore
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

So the explicit seed space
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\left\{
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,E)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,O)}
\right\}
\]
is exactly the shell-reduced realization of the Class II carrier decomposition.

Hence the strongest honest conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic carrier problem is fully reduced to a finite projection / seed-embedding audit.}
}
\]

What is already closed:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the explicit Class II truncation, the witness problem is generically solved.}
}
\]

What remains open:

\[
\boxed{
\text{whether the final complete microscopic TECT realization actually contains that nontrivial carrier sector.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Construction of the Full Bloch Linearization Program for the Refined Locked + Class II Microscopic PDE}

\subsection{Goal and no-loop rule}

The final target is the actual microscopic projected valley operator extracted from the full periodic TECT linearization.
From this point onward, we do \emph{not} re-prove the reduced witness theorem.
That part is already closed once the coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
are obtained and satisfy
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

The only correct next calculation is therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{full periodic microscopic operator}
\;\to\;
\text{Bloch fiber}
\;\to\;
\text{shell truncation}
\;\to\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\to\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]

\subsection{Refined locked + Class II microscopic starting point}

Let the microscopic variables be:
\[
\Psi(x,t)\in \mathbb C^3,
\qquad
X_i^a(x,t),
\]
with \(a\) labeling the reduced internal carrier directions and \(i\) a spatial index.

The working microscopic branch is the refined locked TECT sector together with the explicit Class II mediator:
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\]
We do not assume that this is already the final complete closed TECT action.
Rather, this is the strongest explicit microscopic branch currently available for the actual PDE derivation.

\subsection{Periodic BCC background}

Let the locked periodic condensate be
\[
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\]
where
\[
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{G\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}} A_G e^{iG\cdot x}
\]
is a periodic BCC background built from the selected reciprocal shell \(S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\).
For the microscopic carrier construction we take the static mediator background
\[
X_{0\,i}^a=0
\]
unless a nonzero saddle requires otherwise.

We then expand
\[
\Psi=\Psi_0+\delta\Psi,
\qquad
X_i^a=\delta X_i^a.
\]

\subsection{Linearization around the periodic background}

The full linearized microscopic system takes the schematic form
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{full}}
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta\Psi\\
\delta X
\end{pmatrix}
=0,
\]
with block operator
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{full}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal L_{\Psi\Psi} & \mathcal L_{\Psi X}\\
\mathcal L_{X\Psi} & \mathcal L_{XX}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Here:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathcal L_{\Psi\Psi}\) is the linearization of the refined locked TECT operator around \((\Psi_0,P_0)\);
\item \(\mathcal L_{XX}\) contains the heavy mediator mass term and any derivative corrections if present;
\item \(\mathcal L_{\Psi X}\), \(\mathcal L_{X\Psi}\) come from the linearization of the Class II couplings.
\end{enumerate}

The crucial point is that this linearized operator is periodic with the BCC periodicity of \(\phi_0(x)\).
Hence it admits a Floquet--Bloch decomposition.

\subsection{Bloch fiber decomposition}

For a Bloch momentum \(k\), write
\[
\delta\Psi_k(x)=e^{ik\cdot x}u_k(x),
\qquad
\delta X_{i,k}^a(x)=e^{ik\cdot x}v_{i,k}^a(x),
\]
with \(u_k,v_k\) periodic on the BCC unit cell.

Then the full linearized operator decomposes fiberwise:
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{full}}
\simeq
\int_{\mathrm{BZ}}^\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\,dk,
\]
where
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Expand the periodic Bloch amplitudes in reciprocal harmonics:
\[
u_k(x)=\sum_{G\in \mathcal G} u_G e^{iG\cdot x},
\qquad
v_{i,k}^a(x)=\sum_{G\in \mathcal G} v_{i,G}^a e^{iG\cdot x}.
\]
Then \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\) becomes an infinite matrix in the reciprocal-harmonic basis:
\[
\bigl(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\bigr)_{G,G'}.
\]

This is the actual operator-theoretic starting point of the full PDE program.

\subsection{Heavy-mediator elimination at the Bloch-fiber level}

Because the mediator is heavy, the first practical reduction is to eliminate the \(X\)-sector inside each Bloch fiber.

Formally,
\[
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1+\delta H_{XX}(k),
\qquad
M_X^2\gg |k|^2,\ |G|^2.
\]
Hence, to leading order in \(M_X^{-2}\),
\[
v_k
=
-\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k)\,u_k.
\]
Substituting back gives the effective Bloch operator for the \(\Psi\)-sector:
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\,H_{X\Psi}(k).
}
\]
This is the periodic enriched microscopic operator whose shell-valley block must be analyzed.

\subsection{Selection of the shell-relevant harmonic sector}

Choose a shell/valley point \(k_*\) associated with the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\).
We write
\[
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
\]

Let \(S_*\subset \mathcal G\) denote the finite set of near-resonant reciprocal harmonics around \(k_*\).
Define the shell projector
\[
\Pi_{S_*}:\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\to \mathcal H_{S_*}(k).
\]
Then the shell-projected effective Bloch operator is
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

This is the first finite-dimensional operator that belongs to the actual full-PDE derivation.
Everything before this point is still exact operator setup; everything after this point is finite matrix analysis.

\subsection{Valley projection inside the shell block}

Assume the shell block contains an isolated two-dimensional complex low-energy sector.
Let
\[
P_*:\mathcal H_{S_*}(0)\to \mathcal V_*
\]
be the spectral projector onto that valley subspace:
\[
\dim_{\mathbb C}\mathcal V_*=2.
\]

Define the first derivatives
\[
K_i
:=
\left.
\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\right|_{p=0}.
\]
Then the projected linear valley operator is
\[
H_{\mathrm{val}}^{(1)}(p)
=
p_i\,P_*K_iP_*.
\]

This is the exact place where the actual microscopic coefficients are to be extracted.
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\;\to\;
K_i
\;\to\;
P_*K_iP_*
}
\]
is the true computational bottleneck.

\subsection{Extraction of the Pauli-symbol coefficients}

Choose the shell-adapted frame
\[
\{\hat n,e_1,e_2\},
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n + p_1 e_1 + p_2 e_2.
\]
Inside the valley space \(\mathcal V_*\), decompose
\[
P_*K_iP_*
\]
in the Pauli basis.

The target form is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{val}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+
\gamma_i p_i \mathbf 1_2.
}
\]
The identity term \(\gamma_i p_i\mathbf 1_2\) is irrelevant for Weyl nondegeneracy.
The actual witness coefficients are therefore extracted by the Pauli projections:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{tr}\bigl[\sigma_3\,(\hat n_i P_*K_iP_*)\bigr],
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac12\operatorname{tr}\bigl[\sigma_1(e_{1i}P_*K_iP_*)+\sigma_2(e_{2i}P_*K_iP_*)\bigr],
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac12\operatorname{tr}\bigl[\sigma_2(e_{1i}P_*K_iP_*)-\sigma_1(e_{2i}P_*K_iP_*)\bigr].
\]

Equivalently, in enriched-tensor language this is the extraction of the shell tensor
\[
N^a_{ij}
\]
from the actual projected Bloch derivative operator.

\subsection{Why enriched structure is mandatory}

A plain scalar pair truncation is not enough.
The minimal scalar shell-pair Bloch problem yields at most a rank-deficient linear traceless symbol and therefore does not generically produce a full Weyl cone.

Hence the full-PDE program must retain enriched internal structure:
\[
\text{multi-component field, projector sector, or Class II-mediated carrier block.}
\]
This is exactly why the refined locked + Class II branch is the correct working microscopic branch for the complete derivation.

\subsection{Actual completion criterion}

The full-PDE derivation of the shell witness is complete once the following finite tasks are carried out:

\begin{enumerate}
\item construct the periodic fiber operator \(H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\);
\item choose the near-resonant harmonic set \(S_*\) and build \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\);
\item isolate the two-dimensional valley projector \(P_*\);
\item compute
\[
K_i=\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0);
\]
\item evaluate the three Pauli projections giving
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta.
\]
\end{enumerate}

After that, the witness theorem is not to be reproved.
One simply checks
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

\subsection{Sharp honest status}

At the present stage, what remains open is not the abstract logic of Weyl/Dirac reduction.
It is the explicit derivation of the microscopic objects
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k),\qquad
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p),\qquad
P_*K_iP_*,
\]
from the final periodic refined locked TECT/Class II operator.

Therefore the next concrete theorem target is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{construct the shell-projected enriched Bloch operator of the refined locked + Class II microscopic PDE and extract }(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary}

The project goal is fixed:

\[
\boxed{
\text{derive the actual full microscopic PDE / Bloch linearization and extract the local Dirac data from it.}
}
\]

Hence the correct no-loop progression is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{periodic refined locked microscopic operator}
\to
\text{Bloch fiber}
\to
\text{shell truncation}
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]

The key facts are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal locked isotropic PDE does not by itself produce the required enriched shell tensor;
\item the correct next calculation is the periodic BCC Bloch linearization, not another abstract witness proof;
\item a plain scalar shell-pair truncation is insufficient, so enriched internal structure must be kept;
\item the refined locked + Class II branch is therefore the correct current microscopic branch for the full-PDE derivation.
\end{enumerate}

The actual completion criterion is finite:

\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\to
P_*
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]

Once these are computed, one only checks

\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]

and then moves on immediately to
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \Delta>0,\qquad \text{mass protection}.
\]

So the repetitive phase is over.
The next stage is an actual operator-construction stage.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Full Periodic Bloch-Fiber Construction for the Refined Locked + Class II Microscopic PDE}

\subsection{Conventions and the no-loop rule}

The final target is the actual microscopic projected valley operator extracted from the full periodic TECT linearization.
From this point onward, we do \emph{not} re-prove the witness theorem.
The only legitimate next task is to construct the periodic Bloch operator and extract its projected first derivatives.

To remove the remaining notation loop, we now fix the \emph{folded Bragg convention}.
Instead of working with the unfolded shell variable
\[
q=G_*+p,
\]
we work at the Bragg quasimomentum
\[
\boxed{
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
}
\]
This is equivalent to the unfolded description after Brillouin-zone folding, but it is the correct convention for the finite-dimensional Bloch matrix calculation.

\subsection{The explicit working microscopic branch}

The strongest explicit microscopic branch currently available is the refined locked TECT sector coupled to the Class II heavy mediator:
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X\,X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X\,X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:fullmic_branch}
\end{equation}
We do not claim that \eqref{eq:fullmic_branch} is already the final complete TECT action.
Rather, it is the strongest explicit branch in which the full-PDE derivation can now be pushed concretely.

\subsection{The 12-mode BCC background}

We choose the first BCC reciprocal shell
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\,
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\,
(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\},
\qquad
|\mathcal S_{12}|=12.
\label{eq:S12}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, choosing one representative from each opposite pair,
\begin{equation}
\phi_0(x)
=
2A\sum_{\alpha=1}^{6}\cos(Q_\alpha\cdot x)
=
A\sum_{Q\in \mathcal S_{12}} e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\label{eq:bcc_12mode_phi0}
\end{equation}
The locked background is
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\label{eq:locked_bcc_background}
\end{equation}

Let
\[
u_0=z_0,
\qquad
u_1,u_2\in Q_{z_0},
\qquad
u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs},
\]
be an orthonormal internal basis adapted to the locked decomposition
\[
\mathbb C^3 = \mathbb C z_0 \oplus Q_{z_0}.
\]

\subsection{Bloch-harmonic expansion of the microscopic fluctuations}

Let \(\Gamma^*\) denote the reciprocal lattice generated by the BCC periodic background.
For each Bloch momentum \(k\), expand
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\Gamma^*}\sum_{r=0}^{2}
\psi_{G,r}(k)\,u_r\,e^{iG\cdot x},
\label{eq:deltaPsi_bloch}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\delta X_{i,k}^a(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\Gamma^*}
X_{i,G}^a(k)\,e^{iG\cdot x}.
\label{eq:deltaX_bloch}
\end{equation}

Thus the full linearized periodic problem is an infinite-dimensional Bloch-fiber eigenproblem on the coefficient space
\[
\ell^2(\Gamma^*)\otimes \mathbb C^3_{\mathrm{int}}
\oplus
\ell^2(\Gamma^*)\otimes \mathbb C^3_{\mathrm{space}}\otimes \mathbb C^{N_a}_{\mathrm{med}}.
\]

\subsection{Full Bloch block operator}

In the harmonic basis, the linearized Bloch operator has the block form
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\[3pt]
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:HBloch_block}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{A. The \(\Psi\Psi\)-block}

Write
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
\delta_{GG'}\delta_{rs}\,h_r(k+G)
+
U^{(\mathrm{per})}_{rs}(G-G')
+
U^{(\mathrm{lock})}_{rs}(G-G').
\label{eq:Hpsipsi_general}
\end{equation}
Here:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(h_r(q)\) is the translation-invariant bare kernel in the \(u_r\)-channel;
\item \(U^{(\mathrm{per})}\) comes from the periodic BCC background \(\phi_0\);
\item \(U^{(\mathrm{lock})}\) contains the projector-locking and internal-background Hessian terms.
\end{enumerate}

For the isotropic Brazovskii-type bare part,
\begin{equation}
h_0(q)=r_0 + Z|q|^2 + Y|q|^4,
\label{eq:braz_bare}
\end{equation}
and similarly for the locked transverse channels, up to channel-dependent mass shifts.

\subsubsection{B. The \(\Psi X\)- and \(X\Psi\)-blocks}

Define the background Fourier coefficients
\begin{equation}
\Phi_Q := A,
\qquad
Q\in\mathcal S_{12},
\label{eq:PhiQ}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}} \Phi_Q e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\]
Also define the internal overlap tensors
\begin{equation}
\Xi^a_{rs}:=u_r^\dagger \lambda^a u_s.
\label{eq:Xi_internal}
\end{equation}

The linearized \(J\)-vertex has the universal harmonic selection rule
\begin{equation}
\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\delta_{G'-G,Q}\,
\Phi_Q\,
\Xi^a_{rs}\,
\mathcal D_i(k;G,G';Q),
\label{eq:J_vertex_general}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal D_i\) is linear in the Bloch-shifted momentum and in the background wavevector:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal D_i(k;G,G';Q)
=
c_1\,(k_i+G'_i)+c_2\,Q_i.
\label{eq:D_general}
\end{equation}
The constants \(c_1,c_2\) depend only on the normalization convention for the microscopic current \(J_i^a\).

Likewise, the \(K\)-vertex has the same harmonic support pattern:
\begin{equation}
\bigl(\mathcal K_i^a(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
\sum_{Q\in\Gamma^*}
\delta_{G'-G,Q}\,
\Pi_Q^{\,a;rs}\,
\widetilde{\mathcal D}_i(k;G,G';Q),
\label{eq:K_vertex_general}
\end{equation}
where \(\Pi_Q^{\,a;rs}\) are the Fourier coefficients of the projector/background-induced transport kernel, and \(\widetilde{\mathcal D}_i\) is again linear in the shifted momentum.

Hence
\begin{equation}
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X \mathcal J(k)+\beta_X \mathcal K(k),
\qquad
H_{X\Psi}(k)=H_{\Psi X}(k)^\dagger.
\label{eq:HPsiX_general}
\end{equation}

\subsubsection{C. The \(XX\)-block}

To leading order in the heavy-mediator expansion,
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{XX}(k)\bigr)_{(G,i,a),(G',j,b)}
=
\delta_{GG'}\delta_{ij}\delta_{ab}\,M_X^2
+
\Delta^{XX}_{(G,i,a),(G',j,b)}(k),
\label{eq:HXX_general}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\|\Delta^{XX}(k)\|\ll M_X^2
\]
in the heavy regime.

\subsection{Elimination of the heavy mediator inside each Bloch fiber}

Define
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C(k):=\alpha_X \mathcal J(k)+\beta_X \mathcal K(k).
\label{eq:C_def}
\end{equation}
Then the exact fiberwise Schur complement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\mathcal C(k)\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\,\mathcal C(k)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:Heff_exact}
\end{equation}
In the heavy-mass expansion,
\begin{equation}
H_{XX}(k)^{-1}
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathbf 1
-
\frac{1}{M_X^4}\Delta^{XX}(k)
+
O(M_X^{-6}),
\label{eq:HXXinv_expansion}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
}
\label{eq:Heff_leading}
\end{equation}

At the harmonic-matrix level,
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
\bigl(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{G'',i,a}
\mathcal C_{(G,r),(G'',i,a)}(k)\,
\overline{\mathcal C_{(G',s),(G'',i,a)}(k)}
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
\label{eq:Heff_harmonic}
\end{equation}

This is the first explicit microscopic formula that one can directly use in the full PDE program.

\subsection{Choice of the near-Bragg shell sector}

Let \(G_*\in\mathcal S_{12}\) be the selected shell vector, and let
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\]
The near-Bragg resonant harmonics are those \(G\in\Gamma^*\) for which
\[
|k_*+G|
\]
lies near the shell minimum \(q_*\).

Choose a finite harmonic set \(S_*\subset \Gamma^*\) containing the resonant pair and the nearest background-coupled harmonics.
Define the shell projector
\begin{equation}
\Pi_{S_*}:
\ell^2(\Gamma^*)\otimes\mathbb C^3_{\mathrm{int}}
\to
\mathcal H_{S_*}.
\label{eq:PiSstar}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:Hshell_def}
\end{equation}

This is now a \emph{finite} matrix.
Its size is
\[
3\,|S_*|
\]
before any internal or spectral reduction.

\subsection{Linear expansion of the shell block}

Expand
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)
+
p_i K_i
+
O(|p|^2),
\qquad
K_i:=\left.\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
\label{eq:Hshell_linear}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:Heff_leading},
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
+
O(M_X^{-4}),
\label{eq:Ki_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left.
\partial_{k_i}H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
\right|_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
\label{eq:Ki_PsiPsi}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\left.
\partial_{k_i}\bigl(\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger\bigr)
\right|_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\label{eq:Ki_ClassII}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{align}
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\label{eq:Ki_ClassII_expanded}
\end{align}

\subsection{Why the Class II derivative term is the correct leading target}

For the isotropic bare kernel \eqref{eq:braz_bare},
\begin{equation}
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)=2\bigl(Z+2Y|q|^2\bigr)\,q_i.
\label{eq:dh0dq}
\end{equation}
At the Brazovskii shell,
\begin{equation}
|q|=q_*,
\qquad
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y},
\label{eq:qstar}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)\big|_{|q|=q_*}=0.
\label{eq:bare_derivative_zero}
\end{equation}
Thus the isotropic first-order shell transport vanishes identically on-shell.
So the first genuinely nontrivial linear shell tensor must come from either:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the full 12-mode periodic mixing beyond the locked single-mode cancellation,
\item or the explicit Class II self-energy contribution \eqref{eq:Ki_ClassII_expanded},
\item or both.
\end{enumerate}

This is exactly why the present full-PDE program must focus on \eqref{eq:Ki_ClassII_expanded} instead of recycling the minimal isotropic calculation.

\subsection{Valley isolation and final projected coefficient formulas}

Assume the shell block contains a spectrally isolated two-dimensional complex valley subspace
\[
\mathcal V_* \subset \mathcal H_{S_*},
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}\mathcal V_*=2,
\]
with spectral projector \(P_*\).

Then the linear valley Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=P_*(p_iK_i)P_*.
\label{eq:hpluslin}
\end{equation}

Choose the shell-adapted frame
\[
p=p_\parallel \hat n + p_1 e_1 + p_2 e_2,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
The target reduced form is
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha (p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta (-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+
\gamma_i p_i \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:hplus_target}
\end{equation}
Hence the actual microscopic coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal V_*}
\!\left[
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_iK_i)P_*
\right],
}
\label{eq:lambda_projector_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal V_*}
\!\left[
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*
+
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*
\right],
}
\label{eq:alpha_projector_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal V_*}
\!\left[
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*
-
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*
\right].
}
\label{eq:beta_projector_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{What has actually been achieved in this step}

This step does \emph{not} yet diagonalize the full final microscopic TECT operator.
But it does remove the remaining conceptual ambiguity in the full-PDE program.

The actual microscopic task is now reduced to the following finite construction:

\begin{enumerate}
\item build the harmonic matrices \(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\), \(\mathcal J(k)\), \(\mathcal K(k)\);
\item form the mediator-eliminated effective Bloch operator \eqref{eq:Heff_harmonic};
\item choose the near-Bragg shell set \(S_*\) and construct \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\);
\item isolate \(P_*\) and compute \(K_i\);
\item evaluate \eqref{eq:lambda_projector_final}--\eqref{eq:beta_projector_final}.
\end{enumerate}

So the full microscopic frontier is no longer vague.
It is exactly the explicit construction of the finite shell matrix and its projected derivatives.

%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary}

The no-loop full-PDE program is now fixed in the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=G_*/2.
\]

The 12-mode BCC background is
\[
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\{(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)\}.
\]

Expanding the refined locked + Class II microscopic theory in Bloch harmonics gives the block fiber operator
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

After eliminating the heavy mediator,
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\mathcal C(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\mathcal C(k)^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal C(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k),
\]
and in the heavy-mass regime,
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
\]

Projecting to the near-Bragg harmonic shell \(S_*\) yields the finite shell matrix
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*},
\]
with first derivatives
\[
K_i=\left.\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
\]

The leading Class II contribution is
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

Since the isotropic Brazovskii derivative vanishes exactly on the shell,
\[
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)\big|_{|q|=q_*}=0,
\]
the first genuinely nontrivial shell transport data must come from full periodic mixing and/or the Class II self-energy derivative.

Finally, once the two-dimensional valley projector \(P_*\) is isolated, the actual microscopic coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}
\!\left[
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_iK_i)P_*
\right],
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}
\!\left[
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*
+
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*
\right],
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}
\!\left[
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*
-
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*
\right].
\]

Therefore the full microscopic frontier is now completely localized to one finite construction pipeline:
\[
\boxed{
(H_{\Psi\Psi},\mathcal J,\mathcal K)
\to
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal Finite Shell Matrix at the Bragg Point and the Emergent Enriched Pair Space}

\subsection{Step B goal}

The goal of this step is to pass from the infinite Bloch fiber operator
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\]
to the smallest finite shell matrix that still retains the actual Dirac/Weyl data.

We work in the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
\]
The core question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{What is the minimal finite harmonic sector that contains the actual shell-pair valley data?}
}
\]

\subsection{Core resonant harmonic pair}

At the Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\), the two harmonics
\[
G=0,
\qquad
G=-G_*
\]
are exactly degenerate at the bare shell level because
\[
|k_*+0|=\left|\frac{G_*}{2}\right|,
\qquad
|k_*-G_*|=\left|-\frac{G_*}{2}\right|.
\]
Therefore the minimal resonant harmonic pair is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{core}}:=\{0,\,-G_*\}.
}
\label{eq:Score_def}
\end{equation}

This is the folded version of the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) in the unfolded picture.

\subsection{Why the core pair is not yet the whole story}

Because the BCC background has Fourier support on the 12-mode shell
\[
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\{(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)\},
\]
the periodic background scattering couples harmonics by shifts
\[
G\mapsto G+Q,
\qquad
Q\in \mathcal S_{12}.
\]
Hence the core pair \(S_{\mathrm{core}}\) is not closed under one scattering step.

The one-step closure generated from \(S_{\mathrm{core}}\) is
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{cl}}^{(1)}
=
S_{\mathrm{core}}
\cup
\bigl(0+\mathcal S_{12}\bigr)
\cup
\bigl(-G_*+\mathcal S_{12}\bigr).
\label{eq:Sclosure1_def}
\end{equation}
For a generic choice of \(G_*\in\mathcal S_{12}\), this contains 20 distinct harmonics after removing duplicates.

Thus the correct finite shell program has two natural levels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal core pair \(S_{\mathrm{core}}\), which captures the principal Bragg degeneracy;
\item the one-step closed shell \(S_{\mathrm{cl}}^{(1)}\), whose spectators renormalize the core pair through Schur complement.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Core/spectator decomposition}

Let
\[
S_*:=S_{\mathrm{cl}}^{(1)}.
\]
Then decompose the shell Hilbert space as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{S_*}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}\oplus \mathcal H_{\mathrm{sp}},
\label{eq:Hshell_split}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}
:=
\mathrm{span}\{|0,r\rangle,\ |-G_*,r\rangle\},
\]
and \(r\) runs over the shell-relevant internal doublet basis of \(Q_{z_0}\).
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}\mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}=4.
}
\label{eq:Hcore_C2C2}
\end{equation}

The remainder
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{sp}}
=
\mathcal H_{S_*}\ominus \mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}
\]
is the spectator shell sector.

\subsection{Block form of the shell matrix}

The finite shell matrix has the block form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{cc}(p) & H_{cs}(p)\\[3pt]
H_{sc}(p) & H_{ss}(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hshell_block}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(H_{cc}(p)\) acts on \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}\cong \mathbb C^2\otimes\mathbb C^2\),
\item \(H_{ss}(p)\) acts on the spectator sector,
\item \(H_{cs},H_{sc}\) are the background-induced and mediator-induced couplings between the two.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Core effective Hamiltonian by Schur complement}

Assume the spectator block is gapped away from the target shell energy \(E_*\):
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(E_*,\operatorname{spec}H_{ss}(0)\bigr)\ge \Delta_{\mathrm{sp}}>0.
\label{eq:spectator_gap}
\end{equation}
Then the exact finite core effective Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_{cc}(p)
-
H_{cs}(p)\,
\bigl(H_{ss}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}
H_{sc}(p).
}
\label{eq:Hcoreeff_exact}
\end{equation}
For the low-energy shell program one expands this at \(E\approx E_*\), \(p\approx 0\):
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,0)
+
p_i\,\mathcal K_i^{\mathrm{core}}
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hcoreeff_expand}
\end{equation}

This is the actual finite matrix object from which the projected coefficients must be extracted.

\subsection{Canonical pair \(\otimes\) internal decomposition}

Let \(\tau^a\) act on the pair basis
\[
|+\rangle:=|0\rangle,
\qquad
|-\rangle:=|-G_*\rangle,
\]
and let \(s^a\) act on the internal doublet basis of \(Q_{z_0}\).

Then any Hermitian \(4\times4\) core operator can be expanded in
\[
\tau^\mu\otimes s^\nu,
\qquad
\mu,\nu=0,1,2,3.
\]

The \emph{minimal} symmetry-compatible shell-core expansion near \(p=0\) is
\begin{align}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
&=
E_*(p)\,\mathbf 1_4
+
m_1\,\tau^1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau^2\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\tau^1\otimes
\bigl(
p_1 W^{(1)} + p_2 W^{(2)}
\bigr)
+
\tau^2\otimes
\bigl(
p_1 \widetilde W^{(1)} + p_2 \widetilde W^{(2)}
\bigr)
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:Hcore_general}
\end{align}
where \(W^{(a)},\widetilde W^{(a)}\in \mathrm{Herm}(2)\) act on the internal doublet.

The constant terms
\[
m_1\,\tau^1\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
m_2\,\tau^2\otimes\mathbf 1_2
\]
are the intervalley constant mixing terms.
If they are nonzero, they generate a Bragg mass at \(p=0\).

\subsection{The plain scalar pair versus the enriched pair}

For a plain periodic scalar pair problem, the minimal two-harmonic Bragg truncation gives only
\[
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_2 + v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau^3 + m\,\tau^1 + O(|p|^2),
\]
so its linear traceless symbol is only one-dimensional.
Therefore the plain scalar pair does not generically produce a full Weyl cone.

In contrast, the enriched shell core
\[
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
is large enough to support the Dirac generators
\[
\Gamma_1=\tau^1\otimes s^1,
\qquad
\Gamma_2=\tau^1\otimes s^2,
\qquad
\Gamma_3=\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
which satisfy
\[
\{\Gamma_i,\Gamma_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

So the full-PDE shell target is not a plain \(2\times2\) scalar pair Hamiltonian,
but an enriched \(4\times4\) pair\(\otimes\)internal Hamiltonian.

\subsection{Canonical gauge choice for the off-diagonal pair block}

By a pair-space \(U(1)\) rephasing, one may absorb one overall complex phase in the intervalley block.
Hence, after a convenient basis choice, the linear transverse off-diagonal block can be written using \(\tau^1\) only:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{can}}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau^1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes \bigl(p_1W^1+p_2W^2\bigr)
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:Hcore_can}
\end{equation}
where \(W^1,W^2\in\mathrm{Herm}(2)\).

The full shell-core problem is now compressed to determining:
\[
m,
\qquad
v_\parallel,
\qquad
W^1,
\qquad
W^2.
\]

\subsection{Minimal conditions for an actual Weyl/Dirac shell block}

The folded enriched shell Hamiltonian \eqref{eq:Hcore_can} becomes a massless Dirac principal operator if:

\paragraph{(D1) No constant intervalley mass}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m=0.
}
\label{eq:D1}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(D2) Nonzero longitudinal splitting}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:D2}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(D3) Full-rank transverse internal symbol}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^1,\ W^2
\ \text{are traceless Hermitian, nonzero, and linearly independent;}
}
\label{eq:D3a}
\end{equation}
and, after internal basis reduction,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^1=\nu_1 s^1,
\qquad
W^2=\nu_2 s^2,
\qquad
\nu_1\nu_2\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:D3b}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:D1}--\eqref{eq:D3b},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{can}}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau^1\otimes s^2
+
O(|p|^2),
}
\label{eq:Dirac_core_final}
\end{equation}
which is an exact massless Dirac principal symbol on the enriched shell space.

\subsection{How the \(2\)-dimensional valley sector appears}

There are two equivalent descriptions.

\paragraph{Folded description.}
One keeps the full \(4\)-dimensional core space
\[
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
and \eqref{eq:Dirac_core_final} is already the local massless Dirac operator.

\paragraph{Unfolded description.}
One unfolds back to the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\).
Then the same \(4\times4\) folded Dirac block decomposes into two opposite-chirality \(2\times2\) Weyl valleys.
Equivalently, there exist rank-two projectors
\[
P_+,\ P_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}P_\pm\mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}=2,
\]
selecting the two valley sectors.

Therefore the practical existence conditions for a \(2\)-dimensional valley subspace are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the spectator sector is separated by a finite gap \(\Delta_{\mathrm{sp}}>0\);
\item the core effective Hamiltonian has \(m=0\) at \(p=0\);
\item the longitudinal derivative coefficient satisfies \(v_\parallel\neq 0\);
\item the transverse internal matrices \(W^1,W^2\) are full-rank in the Pauli sense.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Actual projector-derivative data to compute next}

Once \(H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)\) is obtained, one computes
\[
\mathcal K_i^{\mathrm{core}}
=
\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)\Big|_{p=0}.
\]
In the canonical basis \eqref{eq:Hcore_can},
\[
\mathcal K_\parallel^{\mathrm{core}}
=
v_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\mathcal K_1^{\mathrm{core}}
=
\tau^1\otimes W^1,
\qquad
\mathcal K_2^{\mathrm{core}}
=
\tau^1\otimes W^2.
\]

So the remaining actual microscopic task is now finite and concrete:
extract \(m\), \(v_\parallel\), \(W^1\), \(W^2\) from the Schur-complemented shell matrix built from the full periodic refined locked + Class II Bloch operator.

%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary}

At the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the minimal resonant harmonic pair is
\[
S_{\mathrm{core}}=\{0,-G_*\}.
\]
Because the periodic BCC background scatters harmonics by
\[
G\mapsto G+Q,
\qquad
Q\in\mathcal S_{12},
\]
the core pair must be supplemented by spectator harmonics.
The smallest systematic choice is the one-step closure
\[
S_{\mathrm{cl}}^{(1)}
=
S_{\mathrm{core}}
\cup
(0+\mathcal S_{12})
\cup
(-G_*+\mathcal S_{12}).
\]

After splitting
\[
\mathcal H_{S_*}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}\oplus \mathcal H_{\mathrm{sp}},
\]
the exact finite core Hamiltonian is obtained by Schur complement:
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_{cc}(p)
-
H_{cs}(p)(H_{ss}(p)-E)^{-1}H_{sc}(p).
\]

The shell-relevant core space is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{core}}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{pair}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
}
\]

This is the minimal enriched shell space.
A plain scalar \(2\times2\) Bragg pair is not enough, because its linear traceless symbol is only one-dimensional.
The enriched \(4\times4\) shell core is the smallest space capable of carrying the three Dirac generators
\[
\Gamma_1=\tau^1\otimes s^1,\qquad
\Gamma_2=\tau^1\otimes s^2,\qquad
\Gamma_3=\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

After basis reduction, the shell-core Hamiltonian takes the canonical form
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{can}}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau^1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes (p_1W^1+p_2W^2)
+
O(|p|^2).
\]

The shell block is massless Dirac at principal order if
\[
m=0,\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad
W^1=\nu_1 s^1,\qquad
W^2=\nu_2 s^2,\qquad
\nu_1\nu_2\neq 0.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{can}}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau^1\otimes s^2
+
O(|p|^2).
\]

Thus the remaining full-PDE frontier is now a completely finite computation:

\[
\boxed{
(H_{cc},H_{cs},H_{ss})
\to
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}
\to
(m,v_\parallel,W^1,W^2).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Block-Overlap Formulae for the Core Shell Matrix}

\subsection{Purpose}

The goal of this step is to stop the structural loop completely and replace it by an explicit finite matrix-element computation.

At the Bragg point
\[
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the enriched shell basis is taken as
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:stepC_shellbasis}
\end{equation}
where \(u_a(x)\) are periodic internal-envelope functions spanning the shell doublet.
The projected shell Hamiltonian has the \(2\times2\) block form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:stepC_Hproj}
\end{equation}
with \(E_\pm(p)\) and \(B(p)\) acting on the internal doublet.
This finite block contains all shell-level Dirac data. 

\subsection{Core and spectator basis}

Fix the folded core pair
\[
S_{\mathrm{core}}=\{0,-G_*\}.
\]
Let the internal shell-doublet index be \(a=1,2\), and let spectator harmonics be labeled by
\[
\eta\in S_{\mathrm{sp}}:=S_*\setminus S_{\mathrm{core}}.
\]
Define the core basis vectors
\[
|+,a\rangle := |0,a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle := |-G_*,a\rangle,
\]
and spectator basis vectors
\[
|\eta,b\rangle.
\]

After eliminating the heavy mediator \(X\), the effective Bloch operator is
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-\mathcal C(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\mathcal C(k)^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal C(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\]
The shell matrix is
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)=\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

\subsection{Exact block definitions}

Define the shell-core blocks by matrix elements:
\begin{equation}
(E_+(p))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)|+,b\rangle,
\qquad
(E_-(p))_{ab}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)|-,b\rangle,
\label{eq:stepC_Epm_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(B(p))_{ab}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)|-,b\rangle.
\label{eq:stepC_B_def}
\end{equation}
Likewise, define the core--spectator coupling blocks
\begin{equation}
(C_+(p))_{a,\eta b}
=
\langle +,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)|\eta,b\rangle,
\qquad
(C_-(p))_{a,\eta b}
=
\langle -,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)|\eta,b\rangle,
\label{eq:stepC_Cpm_def}
\end{equation}
and the spectator block
\begin{equation}
(H_{ss}(p))_{\eta a,\zeta b}
=
\langle \eta,a|H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)|\zeta,b\rangle.
\label{eq:stepC_Hss_def}
\end{equation}

Then the finite shell matrix decomposes as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p) & C_+(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p) & C_-(p)\\
C_+(p)^\dagger & C_-(p)^\dagger & H_{ss}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:stepC_fullshellblock}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Exact core effective block after spectator elimination}

Assume the spectator block remains spectrally separated from the target shell energy \(E_*\).
Then the exact core effective Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
-
\begin{pmatrix}
C_+(p)\\
C_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}
\bigl(H_{ss}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}
\begin{pmatrix}
C_+(p)^\dagger & C_-(p)^\dagger
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:stepC_coreeff_exact}
\end{equation}

Therefore the renormalized pair-diagonal and pair-off-diagonal blocks are
\begin{equation}
E_+^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
E_+(p)-C_+(p)\,R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)\,C_+(p)^\dagger,
\label{eq:stepC_Eplus_eff}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
E_-^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
E_-(p)-C_-(p)\,R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)\,C_-(p)^\dagger,
\label{eq:stepC_Eminus_eff}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
B(p)-C_+(p)\,R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)\,C_-(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p):=\bigl(H_{ss}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}.
\label{eq:stepC_Beff_exact}
\end{equation}

This is the first fully explicit finite formula for the actual microscopic shell core.

\subsection{What each object means physically}

The block \(E_\pm(p)\) is the direct core self-energy in the \(+\) and \(-\) pair sectors.
The block \(B(p)\) is the direct pair-mixing matrix.
The blocks \(C_\pm(p)\) encode virtual scattering from the core pair into the one-step spectator shell.
The Schur term
\[
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E,p)C_-(p)^\dagger
\]
is the virtual core \(\to\) spectator \(\to\) core intervalley process that renormalizes the pair-off-diagonal shell mixing.

Thus the actual microscopic constants are not read from \(B(p)\) alone, but from the renormalized matrix \(B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)\).

\subsection{Selection rules from the 12-mode BCC background}

Because the BCC background Fourier support is exactly the first shell
\[
\mathcal S_{12},
\]
every one-step background scattering changes the harmonic label by
\[
G\mapsto G+Q,
\qquad
Q\in \mathcal S_{12}.
\]

Hence the core--core pair-mixing channel is directly allowed because
\[
0-(-G_*)=G_*\in \mathcal S_{12}.
\]
Therefore the direct Bragg off-diagonal block \(B(0)\) is generically nonzero already at the periodic background level.

Likewise, a spectator harmonic \(\eta\) couples to the \(+\) core iff
\[
\eta-0 \in \mathcal S_{12},
\]
and to the \(-\) core iff
\[
\eta+G_* \in \mathcal S_{12}.
\]
These are the exact one-step selection rules defining the nonzero entries of \(C_+\) and \(C_-\).

So the entire finite shell block is sparse and combinatorial: every nonzero element is dictated by one of these shell-difference rules, dressed by the corresponding internal overlap matrix.

\subsection{Direct microscopic origin of the constant mass matrix}

At \(p=0\), define the renormalized constant pair-mixing matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0:=B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,0)
=
B(0)-C_+(0)\,R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E_*,0)\,C_-(0)^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:stepC_M0}
\end{equation}

This is the actual Bragg mass matrix on the internal doublet.
Because \(M_0\) is a general complex \(2\times2\) matrix, the constant pair-off-diagonal part of the full \(4\times4\) core Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & M_0\\
M_0^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
\tau^1\otimes \Re M_0 - \tau^2\otimes \Im M_0.
\label{eq:stepC_M0_decomp}
\end{equation}
Therefore the complete massless-crossing condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0=0.
}
\label{eq:stepC_massless_condition}
\end{equation}
This is the precise microscopic version of the statement that all constant pair-off-diagonal mass terms must vanish on the projected shell block.

\subsection{Direct microscopic origin of the longitudinal slope}

The shell-level longitudinal coefficient is extracted from the renormalized pair-diagonal difference.
Define
\begin{equation}
D^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
:=
\frac12\bigl(E_+^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)-E_-^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)\bigr).
\label{eq:stepC_Deff}
\end{equation}
Then the scalar longitudinal slope is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac12
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
D^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)\Big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:stepC_vparallel}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{align}
v_\parallel
&=
\frac14
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\Bigl[
E_+(p)-E_-(p)
-
C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E_*,p)C_+(p)^\dagger
+
C_-(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E_*,p)C_-(p)^\dagger
\Bigr]_{p=0}.
\label{eq:stepC_vparallel_explicit}
\end{align}

This is the exact finite overlap formula for the longitudinal shell splitting.

\subsection{Direct microscopic origin of the transverse Dirac matrices}

Now define the renormalized off-diagonal derivative matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^i
:=
\partial_{p_i}B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)\Big|_{p=0},
\qquad i=1,2.
}
\label{eq:stepC_Wi_def}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:stepC_Beff_exact},
\begin{align}
W^i
&=
\partial_{p_i}B(p)\Big|_{p=0}
-
\partial_{p_i}\Bigl[C_+(p)R_{\mathrm{sp}}(E_*,p)C_-(p)^\dagger\Bigr]_{p=0}
\nonumber\\
&=
\partial_{p_i}B(p)\Big|_{p=0}
-
(\partial_{p_i}C_+)R_0 C_-^\dagger
-
C_+R_0(\partial_{p_i}C_-^\dagger)
+
C_+R_0(\partial_{p_i}H_{ss})R_0 C_-^\dagger
\Big|_{p=0},
\label{eq:stepC_Wi_explicit}
\end{align}
where
\[
R_0 := \bigl(H_{ss}(0)-E_*\bigr)^{-1},
\]
and we have suppressed the explicit \((0)\) on the undifferentiated blocks for readability.

Equation \eqref{eq:stepC_Wi_explicit} is the main actual formula of this step.
It shows that the transverse Dirac matrices come from two sources:

\begin{enumerate}
\item direct core pair-mixing derivatives \(\partial_{p_i}B\);
\item virtual spectator renormalization through differentiated Schur complement terms.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Traceless Dirac part of the transverse matrices}

Since an arbitrary \(W^i\) may contain an irrelevant scalar internal part, define
\begin{equation}
\widetilde W^i
:=
W^i-\frac12 \operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}(W^i)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:stepC_Witr}
\end{equation}
The actual transverse Dirac data are carried by \(\widetilde W^1,\widetilde W^2\).

Write
\[
\widetilde W^i = w^i_a s^a,
\qquad
w^i\in \mathbb R^3.
\]
Then the projected shell block is Dirac at principal order precisely when the two vectors \(w^1,w^2\) are linearly independent, and in the canonical anticommuting case one may choose an internal basis in which
\[
\widetilde W^1=\nu_1 s^1,
\qquad
\widetilde W^2=\nu_2 s^2,
\qquad
\nu_1\nu_2\neq 0.
\]

\subsection{What the plain scalar sector does and does not contribute}

The plain scalar BCC Bragg pair already gives a direct constant pair-mixing term \(B(0)\), i.e. a Bragg mass channel.
But it does not generically provide two independent traceless transverse internal matrices at linear order.

Therefore the actual role of the enriched microscopic structure is sharply separated:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the periodic BCC background naturally supplies the Bragg pair structure and hence the potential constant mass channel \(M_0\);
\item the enriched internal structure plus the Class II-induced transport terms are what can generate nontrivial \(\widetilde W^1,\widetilde W^2\).
\end{enumerate}

So the true full-PDE task is not vague any more:
one must compute \(M_0\), \(v_\parallel\), \(W^1\), \(W^2\) from the microscopic overlap blocks above.

\subsection{Final finite extraction dictionary}

The full \(4\times4\) core Hamiltonian near \(p=0\) is therefore
\begin{align}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
&=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
\tau^3\otimes D^{\mathrm{eff}}_{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
+
\tau^1\otimes \Re B^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
-
\tau^2\otimes \Im B^{\mathrm{eff}}(p),
\label{eq:stepC_core_dictionary1}
\end{align}
and, in the minimal Dirac reduction regime,
\begin{align}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
&=
E_0(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes \bigl(p_1\widetilde W^1+p_2\widetilde W^2\bigr)
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:stepC_core_dictionary2}
\end{align}
provided
\[
M_0=0
\]
and the non-identity internal corrections in the pair-diagonal block are negligible or removable.

Thus the actual microscopic quantities to compute next are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0,\qquad
v_\parallel,\qquad
\widetilde W^1,\qquad
\widetilde W^2.
}
\label{eq:stepC_final_targets}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary}

At the Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the enriched shell-projected Hamiltonian has the finite block form
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
where \(E_\pm(p)\) and \(B(p)\) are \(2\times2\) matrices on the internal doublet.

Including the one-step spectator shell and integrating it out gives the exact renormalized core blocks
\[
E_\pm^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
E_\pm(p)-C_\pm(p)\bigl(H_{ss}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}C_\pm(p)^\dagger,
\]
\[
B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
B(p)-C_+(p)\bigl(H_{ss}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}C_-(p)^\dagger.
\]

The exact microscopic shell quantities are therefore:

\[
\boxed{
M_0:=B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,0),
}
\]
the constant Bragg mass matrix,

\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac12
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\frac{E_+^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)-E_-^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)}{2}
\Big|_{p=0},
}
\]
the longitudinal shell slope,

and
\[
\boxed{
W^i
=
\partial_{p_i}B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)\Big|_{p=0},
\qquad i=1,2,
}
\]
the transverse pair-mixing matrices.

Explicitly,
\[
W^i
=
\partial_{p_i}B
-
(\partial_{p_i}C_+)R_0C_-^\dagger
-
C_+R_0(\partial_{p_i}C_-^\dagger)
+
C_+R_0(\partial_{p_i}H_{ss})R_0C_-^\dagger
\Big|_{p=0},
\qquad
R_0=(H_{ss}(0)-E_*)^{-1}.
\]

The traceless Dirac data are carried by
\[
\widetilde W^i
=
W^i-\frac12\operatorname{tr}(W^i)\mathbf 1_2.
\]

Hence the full-PDE shell problem is no longer abstract.
It is exactly the finite overlap computation
\[
\boxed{
(H_{cc},H_{cs},H_{ss})
\longrightarrow
M_0,\ v_\parallel,\ \widetilde W^1,\ \widetilde W^2.
}
\]

The minimal massless Dirac regime is obtained when
\[
M_0=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\widetilde W^1,\widetilde W^2
\ \text{are linearly independent traceless Hermitian matrices.}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Harmonic Matrix Elements and the Explicit Extraction of \texorpdfstring{$M_0,v_\parallel,W^1,W^2$}{M0,vparallel,W1,W2}}

\subsection{Step D goal}

The shell-level Dirac problem has already been reduced to the finite projected quantities
\[
B_0,\qquad v_\parallel,\qquad W^1,\qquad W^2.
\]
The only correct next step is therefore to write these objects as actual harmonic matrix elements of the periodic microscopic operator.

We work in the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
\]

\subsection{Constant-envelope shell basis}

To obtain explicit primitive-cell selection rules, adopt the simplest enriched shell ansatz:
\[
u_a(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad
a=1,2,
\qquad
\xi_a^\dagger\xi_b=\delta_{ab}.
\]
Define the shell basis states
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}^{(p)}(x)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}e^{i(k_*+p)\cdot x}\xi_a,
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}^{(p)}(x)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}e^{i(k_*+p-G_*)\cdot x}\xi_a.
\label{eq:stepD_shellbasis}
\end{equation}

Then the shell-projected Hamiltonian has block form
\[
H_{\mathrm{proj}}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with \(E_\pm(p),B(p)\in \mathrm{Mat}_{2\times 2}(\mathbb C)\).

\subsection{Effective enriched periodic operator}

After eliminating the heavy Class II mediator \(X\), the effective periodic operator may be organized as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
h_0(-i\nabla)\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
U_{\mathrm{eff}}(x)\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}
T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(x)\,
(-i\partial_\alpha)\otimes s^\alpha
+
\mathcal R_{\mathrm{eff}},
\label{eq:stepD_Heff_form}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(h_0\) is the scalar bare shell kernel;
\item \(U_{\mathrm{eff}}(x)\) is the scalar periodic pair-mixing potential;
\item \(T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(x)\) are the effective enriched derivative coefficients;
\item \(\mathcal R_{\mathrm{eff}}\) denotes higher-order, pair-diagonal internal, or subleading terms.
\end{enumerate}

Expand the periodic coefficient fields in primitive-cell Fourier modes:
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{eff}}(x)=\sum_{Q\in \Gamma^*}\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(x)=\sum_{Q\in \Gamma^*}\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\label{eq:stepD_fourier_expand}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Exact Bragg selection rule for core off-diagonal elements}

Consider any periodic coefficient \(F(x)=\sum_Q \widehat F(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x}\).
Then
\begin{align}
\langle \Psi_{+,a}^{(p)},\,F(x)\,\Psi_{-,b}^{(p)}\rangle
&=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\sum_Q \widehat F(Q)
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
e^{-i(k_*+p)\cdot x}
e^{iQ\cdot x}
e^{i(k_*+p-G_*)\cdot x}
\,\xi_a^\dagger \xi_b
\nonumber\\
&=
\delta_{ab}\,\widehat F(G_*).
\label{eq:stepD_scalar_selection}
\end{align}
Thus the off-diagonal shell-core channel sees only the \(Q=G_*\) Fourier coefficient.

Therefore the constant pair-mixing mass matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0
=
B^{\mathrm{eff}}(0)
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2
+
M_0^{(\mathcal R)}.
}
\label{eq:stepD_M0_main}
\end{equation}
In the minimal constant-envelope reduction, \(M_0^{(\mathcal R)}\) is absent and one simply has
\[
M_0=\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\mathbf 1_2.
\]

\subsection{Off-diagonal derivative matrix elements}

Now consider one enriched derivative term
\[
T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(x)(-i\partial_\alpha)\otimes s^\alpha.
\]
Acting on the negative-pair basis state gives
\[
(-i\partial_\alpha)\Psi_{-,b}^{(p)}
=
(k_*+p-G_*)_\alpha\,\Psi_{-,b}^{(p)}.
\]
Because \(k_*=G_*/2\) is parallel to the shell normal \(\hat n\), one has
\[
(k_*-G_*)_\alpha=0,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2
\]
in the transverse frame.
Hence
\[
(-i\partial_\alpha)\Psi_{-,b}^{(p)}
=
p_\alpha\,\Psi_{-,b}^{(p)}
\qquad
(\alpha=1,2).
\]
Therefore
\begin{align}
\langle \Psi_{+,a}^{(p)},
T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(x)(-i\partial_\alpha)\otimes s^\alpha
\Psi_{-,b}^{(p)}
\rangle
&=
p_\alpha\,\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,(s^\alpha)_{ab}.
\label{eq:stepD_Walpha_overlap}
\end{align}

Thus the exact constant-envelope extraction formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^\alpha
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:stepD_Walpha_main}
\end{equation}

This is the explicit reason the entire shell-level transverse Dirac problem reduces to first-shell Fourier coefficients.

\subsection{Direct Class II origin of the enriched coefficients}

The minimal Class II mediated UV structure is
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^A X_i^A
+
\alpha_X X_i^A J_i^A[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^A K_i^A[P,\psi].
\]
Integrating out \(X\) gives the mixed effective term
\[
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}J_i^A[\Psi]K_i^A[P,\psi].
\]

Take the minimal current choices
\[
J_i^A[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_A\Psi+\mathrm{h.c.},
\qquad
K_i^A[P,\psi]
=
\mathrm{Tr}(T_A\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\]
or, after shell reduction,
\[
K_i^A\sim \partial_i\delta P^A\,\psi.
\]

Around the periodic locked background
\[
\Psi_0(x)=\sum_{Q\in \mathcal S_{12}}A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x}z_0,
\]
the shell/background current has first-shell Fourier coefficients of the form
\begin{equation}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)
=
iQ_i\,A_Q\,j^A
\qquad
(Q\in \mathcal S_{12}),
\label{eq:stepD_Jhat}
\end{equation}
for some reduced internal coefficient \(j^A\) determined by the background internal overlaps.

Likewise, the shell-relevant part of the projector/test current may be decomposed as
\begin{equation}
K_i^A[P,\psi]
=
\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}
K_{i,\alpha}^A(x)\,
(-i\partial_\alpha)\otimes s^\alpha
+\cdots,
\label{eq:stepD_Kdecomp}
\end{equation}
with Fourier coefficients \(\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q)\).

Therefore the effective enriched coefficient field generated by Class II is
\begin{equation}
T^\alpha_{(II)}(x)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A
J_i^A[\Psi_0](x)\,
K_{i,\alpha}^A(x)
+\cdots,
\label{eq:stepD_TII_x}
\end{equation}
and its \(G_*\)-Fourier coefficient is the convolution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\,
\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
}
\label{eq:stepD_TII_conv}
\end{equation}

In the minimal first-shell-dominant route, the leading contribution is
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\approx
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A
\widehat J_i^A(G_*)\,
\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(0),
\label{eq:stepD_TII_leading}
\end{equation}
hence, using \eqref{eq:stepD_Jhat},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\propto
iA_{G_*}\,
\Bigl(C_\alpha\cdot G_*\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:stepD_TII_linear}
\end{equation}
with a proportionality constant depending on the microscopic reduced internal overlaps.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^\alpha_{(II)}
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)\,s^\alpha
\propto
iA_{G_*}\,(C_\alpha\cdot G_*)\,s^\alpha.
}
\label{eq:stepD_WII}
\end{equation}

This is the direct Class II microscopic realization of the already-known shell-level criterion
\[
W^\alpha\neq 0
\iff
A_{G_*}\neq 0,\quad
C_\alpha\cdot G_*\neq 0.
\]

\subsection{Bare/Class II/spectator decomposition}

The actual effective coefficients split naturally into three parts:
\begin{equation}
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat U_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
\label{eq:stepD_U_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*).
\label{eq:stepD_T_split}
\end{equation}
Accordingly,
\begin{equation}
M_0
=
M_0^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
M_0^{(II)}
+
M_0^{(\mathrm{sp})},
\label{eq:stepD_M0_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^\alpha
=
W^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}
+
W^\alpha_{(II)}
+
W^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\label{eq:stepD_W_split}
\end{equation}

The meaning of the three pieces is:

\paragraph{Bare periodic scalar piece.}
\[
M_0^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\]
