\section{Exact Constant-Correction Algebra Audit on the Actual Projected Shell Block}

\subsection{Goal}

The principal-symbol audit of the previous step identified the actual residual generator
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3
\]
for the projected massless \(4\times4\) shell block.
The remaining microscopic question is now purely algebraic:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Do the exact constant }O(p^0)\text{ corrections preserve }Q_*?
}
\]

If yes, then no actual constant Dirac mass can appear in the corrected block.

\subsection{Actual principal block and actual mass space}

The actual canonical projected shell symbol is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\nu_1 p_1\,\tau_1\otimes s_1
+
\nu_2 p_2\,\tau_1\otimes s_2.
\label{eq:J_Hlin_actual}
\end{equation}
Its actual mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
M_1,\,
M_2
\right\},
\qquad
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3.
}
\label{eq:J_Mactual}
\end{equation}

By direct computation,
\begin{equation}
[Q_*,M_1]=-2iM_2,
\qquad
[Q_*,M_2]=2iM_1.
\label{eq:J_Q_rotates_masses}
\end{equation}
Hence the two masses form a charged doublet under the exact \(U(1)\) generated by \(Q_*\), and therefore no nonzero element of \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\) can be \(Q_*\)-invariant.

\subsection{The full constant correction to be audited}

Write the exact corrected shell block near the crossing as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{exact}}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:J_Hexact}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
+
\Sigma(0,0).
\label{eq:J_deltaH_split}
\end{equation}

The constant-correction audit is therefore the source-by-source classification of these three terms relative to \(Q_*\) and \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\).

\subsection{Commutant of the actual residual generator}

A general Hermitian \(4\times4\) operator may be expanded as
\[
K=\sum_{a,b=0}^3 k_{ab}\,\tau_a\otimes s_b.
\]
The condition
\[
[K,Q_*]=0,
\qquad
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3,
\]
is equivalent to requiring that the \(\tau\)-sector and \(s\)-sector have the same commutation parity with \(\tau_3\) and \(s_3\), respectively.

Hence the full \(Q_*\)-commuting constant algebra is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{
\mathbf 1_4,\,
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\mathbf 1_2\otimes s_3,\,
Q_*,
\,
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}.
}
\label{eq:J_CQstar}
\end{equation}
Since
\[
M_1=\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
M_2=\tau_1\otimes s_3
\]
do \emph{not} belong to \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\), we have
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:J_CQstar_intersect_M}
\end{equation}

Therefore any exact constant correction that preserves \(Q_*\) is automatically non-mass-generating.

\subsection{Source I: scalar constant sector}

The plain scalar periodic shell obstruction was the identity-channel Bragg block
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
and this was the dangerous constant mass-like channel in the projected shell pair.
The previous steps already showed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item in the actual locked scalar branch, the bare scalar Bragg block is generically nonzero;
\item spectator cancellation generically fails near onset;
\item therefore the scalar identity channel must be removed by an actual microscopic cancellation law or by exact symmetry.
\end{enumerate}

Once that dangerous scalar channel has been removed, the remaining scalar constant sector is \(Q_*\)-invariant and non-mass-generating.
Equivalently, after transporting the standard theorem-level valley-\(U(1)\) classification to the actual canonical basis, the symmetry-preserving scalar constant algebra reduces to a two-dimensional form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}^{(\mathrm{allowed})}
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_*\,Q_*.
}
\label{eq:J_scalar_allowed}
\end{equation}
This is the actual-basis version of the theorem-level result that an exact residual valley symmetry restricts the allowed constant scalar block to the symmetry-neutral sector only. 

So the scalar audit is now sharp:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{either the scalar identity channel has already been eliminated, or the full shell block is not massless.}
}
\label{eq:J_scalar_sharp}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Source II: Class II constant sector}

The canonical Class II correction renormalizes only the derivative shell tensor coefficients \(A,B,C\), i.e. the first-order Weyl/Dirac witness sector, and does not by construction insert an independent constant shell-level mass operator. 
Moreover, every Class II pair-mixing correction carries an explicit internal Pauli generator, so its constant block, if nonzero, lies in the traceless internal sector rather than the scalar identity channel:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
\in
\mathrm{span}\{s_1,s_2,s_3\}.
\]
Under the natural shell-Dirac odd/reflection parity, the principal constant gradient block vanishes altogether:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}=0.
\]

In the actual \(Q_*\)-basis this means:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
\in
\mathrm{span}
\{
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}
\subset \mathcal C_{Q_*},
}
\label{eq:J_ClassII_allowed}
\end{equation}
or, under the natural odd shell parity,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}=0.
}
\label{eq:J_ClassII_zero}
\end{equation}

Crucially, neither case intersects the actual mass space \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\).
Indeed,
\[
\mathrm{span}
\{
\tau_1\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_2,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_1,\,
\tau_2\otimes s_2
\}
\cap
\mathrm{span}
\{
\tau_2\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_1\otimes s_3
\}
=
\{0\}.
\]
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is fully compatible with mass protection in the actual }Q_*\text{-basis and does not generate }M_1\text{ or }M_2.
}
\label{eq:J_ClassII_nomass}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Source III: remote self-energy \texorpdfstring{$\Sigma(0,0)$}{Sigma(0,0)}}

The theorem-level result states that if the full microscopic theory preserves the residual valley symmetry and remote-sector elimination preserves that symmetry, then
\[
[Q_V,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\]
and in the little-group scalar sector
\[
\Sigma(0,0)=a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
in the standard doubled Dirac basis.
Transporting this statement by the unitary equivalence between the standard doubled basis and the actual canonical basis gives:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0,
\qquad
\Sigma(0,0)=\tilde a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+\tilde a_*\,Q_*,
}
\label{eq:J_Sigma_actual}
\end{equation}
in the actual projected shell basis, provided the same residual symmetry is exact microscopically.

Therefore the remote self-energy cannot generate either of the actual masses \(M_1,M_2\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}
\qquad
\text{if the exact }Q_*\text{-symmetry survives remote elimination.}
}
\label{eq:J_Sigma_nomass}
\end{equation}

So the theorem-level radiative stability statement becomes an explicit actual-basis statement:
if the exact microscopic theory preserves the same \(Q_*\), then no radiative constant mass can be generated on the isolated projected shell block.

\subsection{Combined constant-correction audit theorem}

We can now state the actual constant-correction audit in the form needed for the full PDE program.

\begin{theorem}[Actual constant-correction audit]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the projected shell block has been reduced to the massless canonical form \eqref{eq:J_Hlin_actual};
\item the dangerous scalar identity-channel Bragg block has been removed;
\item the exact corrected microscopic block preserves the actual residual generator
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3;
\]
\item remote-sector elimination preserves the same exact symmetry.
\end{enumerate}
Then every exact constant correction belongs to the \(Q_*\)-commuting algebra
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\in \mathcal C_{Q_*},
\]
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:J_main_theorem}
\end{equation}
Hence no exact constant Dirac mass can appear in the corrected projected shell block.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By source decomposition,
\[
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
+
\Sigma(0,0).
\]
After removing the scalar identity channel, the remaining scalar constant sector is \(Q_*\)-invariant and lies in \(\mathrm{span}\{\mathbf 1_4,Q_*\}\).
The Class II constant sector is either zero (under natural shell odd parity) or belongs to the traceless \(Q_*\)-commuting non-mass sector.
The remote self-energy is \(Q_*\)-invariant by exact symmetry preservation and therefore also lies in \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\).
Since \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}\), no exact constant mass survives.
\end{proof}

\subsection{What is now really left open}

This finishes the algebra.
The only remaining microscopic question is no longer the classification of constant operators.
That is done.

The only remaining yes/no input is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual full microscopic corrected block preserve the same exact }Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3\text{ symmetry?}
}
\label{eq:J_last_open}
\end{equation}

If yes, the mass-protection part of the full local Dirac program is closed.
If no, one must identify the precise symmetry-breaking constant term and check whether it lies in \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\).

\section{Full Microscopic Symmetry-Preservation Audit}

\subsection{Goal}

At this stage the local shell Dirac block, the actual mass space, and the actual residual generator
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3
\]
have already been identified on the projected \(4\times4\) shell block.

Therefore the final full-PDE mass-protection question is no longer a structural one.
It is the explicit source-by-source symmetry audit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[Q_*,H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}]=0,
\qquad
[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
}
\label{eq:K_main_audit}
\end{equation}

If all three hold, then no exact constant mass can appear in the corrected projected shell block.

\subsection{What is already known at theorem level}

For the doubled local Dirac block
\[
H_D(p)=\sum_i v_i p_i(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),

the genuine constant Dirac mass space is
\begin{equation}

If the full microscopic theory preserves the residual valley symmetry and remote elimination preserves it, then the Schur-complement shell Hamiltonian inherits the same symmetry and

Under little-group scalarity, this restricts the zero-momentum self-energy to

\label{eq:K_sigma_standard}
\end{equation}
so no radiatively generated term proportional to \(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2\) or \(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\) can appear. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection{Transport to the actual canonical shell basis}

In the actual projected shell basis of the full-PDE construction, the massless canonical shell block was written as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=

There exists a unitary basis change \(U_{\mathrm{can}}\) relating the standard doubled-Dirac basis and the actual canonical shell basis such that

Q_*=U_{\mathrm{can}}Q_VU_{\mathrm{can}}^{-1},

\Sigma(0,0)\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.

\subsection{Source I: scalar constant sector}

The current locked scalar branch gives the periodic scalar Hessian

U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(x)=u\,|\phi_0(x)|^2,

and hence the scalar identity-channel Bragg obstruction

B_0^{(\mathrm{scalar})}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2.

The alignment term contributes nothing on the locked branch, and the canonical Class II correction does not directly cancel the scalar identity channel. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

Therefore the scalar source audit is sharp:
either the dangerous identity-channel block has already been removed by an actual scalar cancellation law, or the shell block is not massless to begin with.
Once that scalar identity-channel piece is removed, the remaining symmetry-preserving scalar constant sector lies in the neutral \(Q_*\)-commuting subalgebra:

\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}^{(\mathrm{allowed})}

\label{eq:K_scalar_allowed}

Hence the scalar sector is harmless \emph{after} the identity-channel obstruction is eliminated.

\subsection{Source II: Class II constant sector}

The canonical minimal Class II representative
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel\hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},\qquad

\]
renormalizes only the derivative shell tensor coefficients \(A,B,C\), equivalently the first-order Weyl/Dirac witnesses. It does not by construction insert an independent constant \(4\times4\) mass operator. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

More sharply, every projected constant pair-mixing block induced by Class II, if nonzero, lies in the traceless internal Pauli channel

\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
\in \mathrm{span}\{s_1,s_2,s_3\},

so in the shell-pair block it is of the form

\tau_1\otimes s_a
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_2\otimes s_a,

not \(\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2\). Under the natural shell-Dirac odd/reflection parity, the gradient-sector constant pair-mixing vanishes at principal order:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}=0.

Hence Class II renormalizes the derivative witness sector but does not remove the scalar Bragg obstruction and does not directly generate an actual mass. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

In the actual \(Q_*\)-basis this means:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}^{\mathrm{const}}=0
\quad
\text{(natural odd shell parity),}

\label{eq:K_ClassII_zero}

or more weakly

\label{eq:K_ClassII_CQ}
\end{equation}
So the Class II source passes the mass audit.

\subsection{Source III: remote self-energy}

The only genuinely open microscopic part is remote-sector inheritance.
At theorem level, if the full microscopic theory admits a symmetry action

(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta})H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta})^{-1}=H_{\mathrm{full}}(p),

[Q_*,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.

Under the transported little-group scalarity,

\Sigma(0,0)=\tilde a_0\,\mathbf 1_4+\tilde a_*\,Q_*,

so no term in \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\) can be generated. :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13} :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

Therefore the remote self-energy source passes the mass audit \emph{if and only if} the exact same residual symmetry is actually preserved by the full microscopic theory and by remote elimination.

\subsection{Combined actual audit theorem}

We can now formulate the exact logical status in the actual basis.

\begin{theorem}[Actual full-microscopic mass-protection audit]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the projected shell block has been reduced to the actual canonical massless form \eqref{eq:K_H_actual};
\item the dangerous scalar identity-channel Bragg block has been removed;
\item the full microscopic corrected block preserves the actual residual generator
\[
Q_*=\tau_3\otimes s_3;
\]
\item remote elimination preserves the same exact symmetry.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}
=
\delta H_{\mathrm{scalar}}
+
\delta H_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
+
\Sigma(0,0)
\in \mathcal C_{Q_*},
\label{eq:K_dH_in_CQ}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\cap \mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:K_final_mass_no}
\end{equation}
Hence no exact constant Dirac mass can appear in the corrected projected shell block.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
After the scalar identity-channel obstruction is removed, the remaining scalar constant block is \(Q_*\)-neutral.
The canonical Class II correction is either zero at constant order or lies in the traceless non-mass sector and does not intersect \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}\).
If the same residual symmetry is exact in the full microscopic theory, then the remote self-energy commutes with \(Q_*\) and is restricted to \(\tilde a_0\mathbf 1_4+\tilde a_*Q_*\).
Thus every exact constant correction lies in \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\), while \(\mathcal C_{Q_*}\cap\mathcal M_{\mathrm{actual}}=\{0\}\).
\end{proof}

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

The only remaining full-PDE question is no longer the classification of masses or residual generators.
Those are already explicit.

}

If yes, the mass-protection part of the local Dirac program is closed.
If no, one must identify the explicit symmetry-breaking constant term and check whether it projects onto \(M_1\) or \(M_2\).

\section{Scalar Identity-Channel Elimination in the Actual Microscopic Scalar Sector}

\subsection{Goal}

After the source-level \(Q_*\)-audit, the only genuinely dangerous remaining constant source is the scalar identity-channel Bragg block
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{scalar}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
The purpose of this step is to determine whether the currently known microscopic scalar sector of TECT can eliminate this obstruction \emph{within the actual safe operator library}.

\subsection{Exact scalar Bragg-mass formula}

Take the most general shell-relevant scalar periodic contribution built from the three natural locked first-shell scalar operators:
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{tot}}(x)
=
c_0\,\phi_0(x)^2
+
c_1\,|\nabla\phi_0(x)|^2
+
c_2\,\phi_0(x)(-\Delta)\phi_0(x).
\label{eq:M_Utot}
\end{equation}
For the locked 12-mode BCC branch, the first-shell Fourier coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)=4A^2,
\label{eq:M_phi2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\widehat{|\nabla\phi_0|^2}(G_*)=2q_*^2A^2,
\label{eq:M_gradphi2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0(-\Delta)\phi_0}(G_*)=4q_*^2A^2.
\label{eq:M_phiLapphi}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{align}
\widehat U_{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*)
&=
c_0(4A^2)
+
c_1(2q_*^2A^2)
+
c_2(4q_*^2A^2)
\nonumber\\
&=
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr).
\label{eq:M_Uhat}
\end{align}
Therefore the projected scalar Bragg block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}
=
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:M_B0tot}
\end{equation}
The exact scalar cancellation condition is thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2=0.
}
\label{eq:M_cancel}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Actual coefficients contributed by the currently known safe sectors}

The actual uploaded microscopic analysis isolates the contributions of the presently known safe sectors.

\paragraph{Sector 1: actual scalar Hessian.}
Inside the actual \(Q\)-sector scalar Hessian, the only periodic scalar contribution is
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{per}}^{\mathrm{tot}}(x)=u\,|\phi_0(x)|^2.
\label{eq:M_actual_scalar}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0^{(\mathrm{scalar})}=u,
\qquad
c_1^{(\mathrm{scalar})}=0,
\qquad
c_2^{(\mathrm{scalar})}=0.
}
\label{eq:M_scalar_coeffs}
\end{equation}
So
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0^{(\mathrm{scalar})}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:M_scalar_B0}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Sector 2: alignment term.}
On the locked branch
\[
\Psi=z\phi,\qquad P=zz^\dagger=\mathrm{const},
\]
one has
\[
\partial_iP=0,
\]
hence the refined alignment term vanishes identically on the locked sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0^{(\mathrm{align})}=0,
\qquad
c_1^{(\mathrm{align})}=0,
\qquad
c_2^{(\mathrm{align})}=0.
}
\label{eq:M_align_coeffs}
\end{equation}
So
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0^{(\mathrm{align})}=0.
}
\label{eq:M_align_B0}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Sector 3: canonical Class II.}
The exact Class II witness formulas modify only the derivative witness coefficients:
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J.
\]
So Class II acts in the derivative witness sector \((W_\parallel,W_I,W_J)\), not in the scalar identity-channel Bragg block.
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_0^{(\mathrm{Class\,II})}=0,
\qquad
c_1^{(\mathrm{Class\,II})}=0,
\qquad
c_2^{(\mathrm{Class\,II})}=0
}
\label{eq:M_classII_coeffs}
\end{equation}
as a direct scalar cancellation channel.

\subsection{Exact no-go theorem for the current safe operator library}

Summing the known safe microscopic sectors gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_0,c_1,c_2)_{\mathrm{known}}=(u,0,0).
}
\label{eq:M_known_coeffs}
\end{equation}
Substituting into \eqref{eq:M_B0tot},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0^{\mathrm{known}}
=
4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:M_known_B0}
\end{equation}
Hence, for \(u\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0^{\mathrm{known}}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:M_known_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{theorem}[No-go inside the current safe operator library]
Within the currently known safe microscopic sectors of the locked 12-mode BCC branch,
namely:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual scalar Hessian,
\item the refined alignment term,
\item the canonical minimal Class II mediator,
\end{enumerate}
the scalar identity-channel Bragg block cannot be eliminated.
Equivalently,
\[
2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2
=
2u\neq 0
\]
for \(u\neq 0\), so the exact scalar cancellation law cannot be satisfied.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:M_cancel} and \eqref{eq:M_known_coeffs}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Why canonical Class II cannot help}

The reason is structural, not numerical.
Every Class II contribution carries an explicit internal Pauli generator in the projected shell block:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
\in
\mathrm{span}\{s_1,s_2,s_3\},
\]
so the constant pair block is of the form
\[
\tau_1\otimes s_a
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_2\otimes s_a,
\]
never
\[
\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Hence the scalar identity channel and the traceless Pauli channel are orthogonal, and Class II cannot directly cancel
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

\subsection{Exact classification of the remaining routes}

The reduced operator analysis already isolates the only two logically distinct possibilities.

\paragraph{Route 1: direct identity-channel cancellation.}
To cancel the scalar Bragg mass directly, one must introduce an additional microscopic sector whose projected constant pair block has a nonzero identity component:
\begin{equation}
\delta M_0^{\mathrm{id}}
=
\delta m_0\,\mathbf 1_2+\delta\widetilde M_0,
\qquad
\delta m_0\neq 0,
\label{eq:M_idroute}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta m_0=-B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:M_idcondition}
\end{equation}
Any UV completion whose projected constant pair block is purely traceless cannot realize this route.

\paragraph{Route 2: graded \(2+2\) bypass.}
Instead of cancelling the scalar Bragg block inside the plain scalar shell-pair reduction,
one passes to a \(J\)-graded \(2+2\) low-energy sector in which the relevant principal operator is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(J\)-odd,
\item first-order in momentum.
\end{enumerate}
Then the reduced infrared operator is block-off-diagonal and first-order, so the dangerous constant scalar Bragg block is absent from the relevant low-energy block from the outset.

Therefore the exact classification is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{identity-carrying mediator route}
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\text{graded }2+2\text{ bypass route.}
}
\label{eq:M_two_routes}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

At this point the local full-PDE program becomes completely explicit.

\begin{enumerate}
\item The derivative witness sector has already been isolated and Class II provides a concrete route for generating it.
\item The actual constant-mass algebra and residual generator have already been identified on the projected \(4\times4\) shell block.
\item The remote-sector source becomes harmless once the zero-mixing label audit gives \(V(0)=0\).
\item The only unresolved microscopic source is the scalar identity-channel Bragg block.
\item Inside the current safe operator library, this scalar block cannot be removed.
\end{enumerate}

So the full-PDE frontier is no longer broad.
It is precisely the choice between:
\[
\boxed{
\text{adding an identity-carrying microscopic sector,}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{abandoning the plain scalar shell-pair channel in favor of the graded }2+2\text{ bypass route.}
}

\section{Route B Mainline: Graded \texorpdfstring{$2+2$}{2+2} Bypass as the Actual Full-PDE Program}

but an isolated four-dimensional graded infrared sector
\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,

\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\]
whose leading reduced operator is first-order and odd under the grading.

\subsection{Abstract graded structure}

Let \(J\) be a grading involution on the low-energy sector:
\begin{equation}
J^\dagger=J,
\qquad
J^2=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
J|_{K_\pm}=\pm 1.
\label{eq:RB_J_def}
\end{equation}
Let the projected reduced operator be
\begin{equation}
D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)=\Pi_K L(p)\Pi_K
=
D_1(p)+O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:RB_Deff}
\end{equation}
and assume the leading term is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item first-order in momentum,
\item \(J\)-odd:
\begin{equation}
JD_1(p)J^{-1}=-D_1(p).
\label{eq:RB_Jodd}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then in the \(J\)-graded basis one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_iM_i.
}
\label{eq:RB_block_form}
\end{equation}

This is the rigorous reduced bypass structure already isolated in the manuscripts.

\subsection{Why the scalar Bragg mass is absent}

The dangerous obstruction in the plain scalar shell-pair route was a momentum-independent constant block
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
But in the graded bypass route, the relevant principal infrared operator is by definition first-order:
\[
A_1(p)=p_iM_i.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(0)=0,
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:RB_D1_zero}
\end{equation}
Therefore the scalar Bragg block is not cancelled inside \(D_1\); it is absent because the relevant principal operator starts at first order in momentum.

This is the precise meaning of the bypass mechanism.

\subsection{General mixed symbol and finite nondegeneracy matrix}

Write the off-diagonal mixed symbol in Pauli form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\ell_0(p)\mathbf 1_2
+
\ell_a(p)\sigma_a,
\qquad
\ell_\alpha(p)=C_\alpha{}^{i}p_i.
}
\label{eq:RB_A1_general}
\end{equation}
The identity part \(\ell_0(p)\mathbf 1_2\) is not a mass obstruction because it is still linear in \(p\).
The actual load-bearing data are the traceless coefficient vectors \(C_a{}^i\).

Define the finite nondegeneracy matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3 C_a{}^{i}C_a{}^{j}
-
C_0{}^{i}C_0{}^{j}.
}
\label{eq:RB_Gij}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)=-p_iG_{ij}p_j,
\qquad
\det D_1(p)=\bigl(p_iG_{ij}p_j\bigr)^2.
}
\label{eq:RB_det}
\end{equation}
Thus the graded bypass route reduces the Dirac question to the finite test
\[
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0.
}
\]

\subsection{Actual local CP\texorpdfstring{$^2$}{2} projector-defect operator class}

The manuscripts already identify the actual local TECT projector-defect geometry as belonging to this graded operator class.

For a local defect background
\[
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\]
the physical tangent fluctuation lives in the rank-two complex bundle
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
}
\label{eq:RB_QB}
\end{equation}
Thus the defect fluctuation problem is already non-scalar.

For a reflection-symmetric representative
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
the leading worldvolume transport kernel is built linearly from the transverse gradient, hence is odd:
\[
\mathcal V^\mu(-\xi)=-\mathcal V^\mu(\xi).
\]
Therefore the actual local projector Hessian matches the abstract graded operator class:
static rank-two bundle operator + even/odd low channels + odd first-order transport kernel.

\subsection{Natural local symmetry-compatible branch: S2}

Inside the actual local projector-defect transport class, the natural local branch is S2:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:RB_S2}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in terms of projected transport matrices,
\[
M^\mu
=
C_0{}^\mu \mathbf 1_2 + C_a{}^\mu \sigma_a.
\]
For the actual local projector-defect transport ansatz one has
\[
C_0{}^i=0,
\]
and
\[
(C_1{}^{1},C_2{}^{1},C_3{}^{1})=(I_\theta\Lambda_E,\ I_\theta\Lambda_O,\ 0),
\]
\[
(C_1{}^{2},C_2{}^{2},C_3{}^{2})=(-I_\theta\Lambda_O,\ I_\theta\Lambda_E,\ 0),
\]
\[
(C_1{}^{\parallel},C_2{}^{\parallel},C_3{}^{\parallel})=(0,\ 0,\ I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel).
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}
=
I_\theta^2
\begin{pmatrix}
\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2 & 0 & 0\\
0 & \Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2 & 0\\
0 & 0 & \Lambda_\parallel^2
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:RB_Gij_actual}
\end{equation}

Hence the graded bypass nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:RB_nondeg_Lambda}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:RB_nondeg_lambdas}
\end{equation}

So the graded bypass route is not an independent mystery:
inside the actual local projector-defect operator class, it reduces exactly to the same three transport coefficients that already control the witness problem.

\subsection{Concrete minimal transport ansatz}

A concrete minimal microscopic transport action compatible with the actual local projector-defect geometry is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trans}}^{\min}
=
-i\,\eta^\dagger
\Big[
g_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
g_E\,\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
g_O\,\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\label{eq:RB_Ltrans}
\end{equation}
Its projected coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:RB_coeffs}
\end{equation}
Therefore the full local S2 nondegeneracy condition becomes exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:RB_gc_condition}
\end{equation}

So the graded bypass route has now been compressed to a finite coefficient-extraction problem.

\subsection{What is proved and what remains open}

What is now genuinely closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the plain scalar Bragg route is not the correct mainline;
\item the graded \(2+2\) reduced Dirac theorem is rigorous;
\item the actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry belongs to this operator class;
\item the natural local branch is S2;
\item the dangerous scalar Bragg block is absent from the relevant graded principal operator because
\[
D_1(0)=0;
\]
\item the full principal Dirac nondegeneracy problem is reduced to the finite test
\[
g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item derive the actual transport kernel \(V^\mu(\xi)\) from the \emph{full} microscopic TECT operator rather than postulate it as a minimal local ansatz;
\item prove that the actual reduced leading perturbation is indeed grading-odd in the full microscopic defect/valley reduction;
\item compute the actual microscopic values of
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O;
\]
\item verify directly that complete TECT indeed gives
\[
g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

Thus the graded bypass route is now the correct non-repetitive mainline.

The decisive unresolved microscopic problem is no longer
\[
\text{``how do we cancel }B_0\text{?''}
\]
but rather
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual defect/projector reduced operator admit the required }2+2\text{ grading and produce nonzero }g_c,g_E,g_O?
}
\label{eq:RB_honest_frontier}
\end{equation}

If yes, then the principal infrared operator is Dirac automatically.

\section{Final Summary}

The scalar identity-channel Bragg block cannot be removed inside the current safe scalar/Class II operator library.
Therefore the correct mainline is no longer scalar-channel cancellation, but the graded \(2+2\) bypass route.

In the graded route, the relevant infrared sector is
\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\]
with a grading involution \(J\) such that the leading projected operator is first-order and \(J\)-odd:
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_iM_i.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
D_1(0)=0,
}
\]
so the dangerous scalar Bragg block is absent from the relevant principal operator rather than cancelled inside it. 

The full nondegeneracy problem reduces to the finite matrix
\[
\boxed{
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3 C_a{}^{i}C_a{}^{j}-C_0{}^{i}C_0{}^{j},
}
\]
with
\[
\det A_1(p)=-p_iG_{ij}p_j.
\]
In the actual local projector-defect transport class, the natural branch is S2,
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
So the graded bypass route is not a separate mystery; it reduces exactly to the same three transport coefficients that already control the witness problem. 

The strongest honest current conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Dirac emergence is rigorously proved at the reduced graded-spectral level,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual local CP}^2\text{ projector-defect geometry belongs to this operator class,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic TECT closure is now reduced to extracting }g_c,\ g_E,\ g_O
\text{ from the actual transport kernel }V^\mu(\xi).
}
\]

\section{Actual Graded \texorpdfstring{$2+2$}{2+2} Coefficient Extraction}

\subsection{Goal}

In the graded bypass route, the remaining microscopic task is no longer to cancel the scalar Bragg block.
The actual remaining task is to extract the transport coefficients of the projected first-order mixed symbol from the defect/projector transport kernel.

The full extraction chain is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_B(\xi)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
V^\mu(\xi)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
u_a^\pm(\xi)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
(M^\mu)_{ab}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\Lambda_\parallel,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O
\;\Longrightarrow\;
g_c,g_E,g_O.
}
\label{eq:N_full_chain}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Actual local defect background and the four-mode infrared sector}

Let
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\label{eq:N_PB}
\end{equation}
be a static defect background depending only on the transverse coordinate \(\xi\).
Projector fluctuations satisfy
\[
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0,
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C Q_B=2.
}
\label{eq:N_QB}
\end{equation}

For a reflection-symmetric defect background, the transverse defect operator admits even/odd low modes
\[
f_+(-\xi)=f_+(\xi),
\qquad
f_-(-\xi)=-f_-(\xi).
\]
Choosing a local orthonormal frame \(e_a(\xi)\) of \(Q_B\), the low modes are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2,
}
\label{eq:N_u_pm}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal K=\mathrm{span}\{u_a^\pm\},
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C\mathcal K=4.
}
\label{eq:N_Kdim}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Projected mixed symbol}

The actual projected overlap matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)\,V^\mu(\xi)\,e_b(\xi).
}
\label{eq:N_Mmu}
\end{equation}
These are the coefficient matrices of the first-order graded symbol.

Expand each \(M^\mu\) in the Pauli basis:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu
=
C_0{}^\mu \mathbf 1_2 + C_i{}^\mu \sigma_i.
}
\label{eq:N_Cmu}
\end{equation}
Then the reduced off-diagonal symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\label{eq:N_A1}
\end{equation}
and the graded nondegeneracy matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3 C_a{}^i C_a{}^j - C_0{}^i C_0{}^j.
}
\label{eq:N_Gij}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Actual local projector-defect transport class}

The actual local projector-defect transport class is odd and \(Q_B\)-endomorphism valued. Its minimal S2-compatible form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu \Sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
\cdots
}
\label{eq:N_Vmu_actual}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(n^\mu\) is the worldvolume singlet direction,
\item \(E^\mu{}_a\) is the transverse worldvolume doublet,
\item \(J^\mu{}_a=\epsilon_{ab}E^\mu{}_b\),
\item \(\Sigma_a\) is the canonical \(Q_B\)-fiber Pauli basis,
\item \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\) is the possible constant-leading longitudinal branch,
\item \(\lambda_c\) is the primitive commutator-square longitudinal coefficient.
\end{enumerate}

The honest notes explicitly distinguish these two longitudinal branches: in the broad actual-local class, a constant-leading longitudinal \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\) is symmetry-allowed, whereas in the exact concrete Class II branch the longitudinal term starts only in the primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\) channel. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{Projection integrals}

Define the two universal defect overlap integrals
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
:=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi),
}
\label{eq:N_Itheta}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
:=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:N_Itheta3}
\end{equation}
Then projecting \eqref{eq:N_Vmu_actual} onto the graded low modes gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu
=
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu \sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\,n^\mu \sigma_3
+
\cdots
}
\label{eq:N_Mmu_projected}
\end{equation}
where the omitted terms are higher-order or symmetry-subleading.

Thus the reduced S2 symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:N_S2_symbol}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:N_lambda_alpha_beta_general}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Exact concrete Class II branch}

In the exact concrete Class II local formulas, the transverse sector starts in the \(I_\theta\) channel while the longitudinal sector starts only in the primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\) channel. Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\quad\text{(exact concrete Class II branch),}
}
\label{eq:N_Lambda0_zero}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:N_exact_ClassII_coeffs}
\end{equation}

The notes also record the explicit local overlap values for the concrete representative:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:N_Itheta_values}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:N_lambda_parallel_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:N_alpha_beta_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Coefficient vectors and nondegeneracy matrix}

From \eqref{eq:N_Mmu_projected}, the coefficient vectors are
\begin{equation}
C_0{}^i=0,
\label{eq:N_C0_zero}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(C_1{}^1,C_2{}^1,C_3{}^1)=\bigl(I_\theta\Lambda_E,\ I_\theta\Lambda_O,\ 0\bigr),
\label{eq:N_C1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(C_1{}^2,C_2{}^2,C_3{}^2)=\bigl(-I_\theta\Lambda_O,\ I_\theta\Lambda_E,\ 0\bigr),
\label{eq:N_C2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(C_1{}^\parallel,C_2{}^\parallel,C_3{}^\parallel)=\bigl(0,\ 0,\ \lambda_\parallel\bigr).
\label{eq:N_Cparallel}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
I_\theta^2(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2) & 0 & 0\\
0 & I_\theta^2(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2) & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel^2
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:N_Gij_explicit}
\end{equation}

Hence the graded bypass nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:N_G_positive}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the exact concrete Class II branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:N_G_positive_ClassII}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Dictionary to \texorpdfstring{$(g_c,g_E,g_O)$}{(g_c,g_E,g_O)}}

The local Class II shell/defect dictionary identifies
\[
g_c\leftrightarrow \lambda_c,
\qquad
g_E\leftrightarrow \Lambda_E,
\qquad
g_O\leftrightarrow \Lambda_O,
\]
up to the already-isolated overall normalization fixed by the final shell/defect overlap completion.
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0)
}
\label{eq:N_g_condition}
\end{equation}
is exactly the same finite microscopic test as
\eqref{eq:N_G_positive_ClassII}.

Moreover, inside the explicit seed space of the concrete Class II reduction,
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J,
\]
so explicit witness seeds exist already at the reduced level. What remains open is whether the \emph{true complete TECT action} realizes that nontrivial sector in the physically relevant defect background.

\subsection{What is actually closed and what remains open}

What is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the graded \(2+2\) bypass route is the correct mainline;
\item the actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry provides the right \(4\)-mode graded sector;
\item the projected coefficient extraction formulas are explicit:
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta
\]
are given by \eqref{eq:N_lambda_alpha_beta_general};
\item in the exact concrete Class II branch, the longitudinal/transverse split is explicit:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O;
\]
\item the entire Dirac nondegeneracy problem is reduced to the finite test
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains honestly open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item derive the actual full microscopic transport kernel \(V^\mu(\xi)\) from complete TECT, rather than postulate the minimal local ansatz;
\item decide which longitudinal branch the complete microscopic theory realizes:
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\ \text{with primitive }I_{\theta'^3}\text{ only};
\]
\item compute the actual microscopic values of
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O;
\]
\item verify directly that complete TECT indeed yields
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

Therefore the graded bypass frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is exactly the coefficient-extraction problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{derive }V^\mu(\xi)\text{ from full TECT and extract }
\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:N_honest_frontier}
\end{equation}
Once this is done, the principal Dirac operator follows immediately.

\section{Final Summary}

In the graded \(2+2\) bypass route, the remaining microscopic extraction chain is

\[
\boxed{
P_B(\xi)\to V^\mu(\xi)\to u_a^\pm(\xi)\to (M^\mu)_{ab}\to
\Lambda_\parallel,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\to g_c,g_E,g_O.
}
\]

The actual local defect/projector geometry gives a natural four-mode infrared sector:
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C\mathcal K=4.
\]

The projected mixed symbol is
\[
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
}
\]

For the actual local S2-compatible transport class,
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu \Sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3+\cdots,
\]
the projected coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\]

In the exact concrete Class II branch,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\]

Using the explicit overlap coefficients,
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

Hence the full graded nondegeneracy problem reduces to the finite test
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

So the strongest honest current conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the graded bypass route is fully reduced to extracting }
\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O
\text{ from the actual full TECT transport kernel }V^\mu(\xi).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Transport-Kernel Derivation Protocol from the Full Microscopic Hessian}

\subsection{Goal}

The graded \(2+2\) bypass route has reduced the full microscopic frontier to a single explicit calculation:
derive the actual odd first-order transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
\]
from the complete TECT Hessian around the shell-/defect-adapted background, and then project it to obtain the coefficients
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

This section fixes the operator protocol for that extraction.

\subsection{Background split}

The correct minimal microscopic background is shell-/defect-adapted rather than constant:
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}
=
(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
or, if the gauge sector is kept explicitly,
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)).
\]
This is exactly the background choice already isolated in the notes for obtaining a genuinely nontrivial background-dependent Hessian and nonzero cubic vertices. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Write the fluctuation split as
\begin{equation}
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi.
\label{eq:O_background_split}
\end{equation}
Then the microscopic quadratic operator is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\left.
\frac{\delta^2\Gamma}{\delta\varphi\,\delta\varphi}
\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}.
\label{eq:O_Hessian_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Projector parametrization of the defect fluctuations}

For the local projector-defect sector, the background projector is
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\label{eq:O_PB}
\end{equation}
and fluctuations are parameterized by
\begin{equation}
\delta P
=
\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0.
\label{eq:O_deltaP}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C Q_B=2.
}
\label{eq:O_eta_QB}
\end{equation}
This is the actual rank-two bundle structure of the local reduced problem. 

\subsection{Step 1: identify the static transverse operator}

After substituting \eqref{eq:O_deltaP} into the full Hessian and separating transverse from worldvolume derivatives
\[
y^\mu=(t,x_1,x_2),
\qquad
\xi=\text{transverse coordinate},
\]
the quadratic operator takes the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:O_operator_split}
\end{equation}
where the static transverse operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_B=-\partial_\xi^2+U_B(\xi)
}
\label{eq:O_HB}
\end{equation}
acting on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B\). This is exactly the operator whose low even/odd modes define the graded \(2+2\) infrared sector. 

\subsection{Step 2: isolate the odd first-order transport kernel}

The actual first-order transport piece is the coefficient of \(-i\partial_{y^\mu}\) in the background-dependent Hessian:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
}
\label{eq:O_L1}
\end{equation}
The structural notes already fix its microscopic origin:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B)T^\mu,
}
\label{eq:O_V_protocol}
\end{equation}
for some microscopic bundle endomorphism-valued tensors \(T^\mu\). Because
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B(-\xi)=-\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\label{eq:O_V_odd}
\end{equation}
Thus the microscopic TECT linearization naturally supplies the odd transport kernel required by the graded reduced theorem. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\paragraph{Operational extraction rule.}
Given the explicit Hessian \(\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\), one extracts \(V^\mu(\xi)\) by:
\begin{enumerate}
\item expanding the Hessian to first order in worldvolume derivatives;
\item collecting all terms linear in \(\partial_{y^\mu}\);
\item moving all \(\xi\)-dependent coefficient matrices to the left of \(\partial_{y^\mu}\);
\item projecting the result onto the tangent bundle \(Q_B\).
\end{enumerate}
The resulting bundle endomorphism coefficient is precisely \(V^\mu(\xi)\).

\subsection{Step 3: construct the isolated graded \(2+2\) sector}

Solve the static transverse problem
\[
H_B u=\varepsilon u
\]
on \(Q_B(\xi)\).
For a reflection-symmetric defect background, \(H_B\) decomposes into even and odd transverse parity channels, so the natural low modes are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_a^+(\xi),\qquad
u_a^-(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2,
}
\label{eq:O_u_pm}
\end{equation}
with
\[
u_a^+(-\xi)=+u_a^+(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(-\xi)=-u_a^-(\xi).
\]
This yields the isolated graded sector
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus \mathcal K_-,
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C\mathcal K_\pm=2.
}
\label{eq:O_Kgraded}
\end{equation}
The notes already identify this as the actual next calculation gap rather than a conceptual gap. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsection{Step 4: project the transport kernel}

The mixed first-order overlap matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
=
\int d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger V^\mu(\xi)u_b^-.
}
\label{eq:O_Mmu}
\end{equation}
Because
\[
u_a^+\ \text{is even},
\qquad
u_b^-\ \text{is odd},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)\ \text{is odd},
\]
the integrand is even, so the overlap is generically nonzero. This is the direct microscopic origin of the mixed first-order symbol. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

Expand
\begin{equation}
M^\mu=C_0{}^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i{}^\mu\sigma_i.
\label{eq:O_Mmu_Pauli}
\end{equation}
Then the reduced mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\label{eq:O_A1}
\end{equation}
and its load-bearing nondegeneracy data are the traceless coefficient vectors
\[
b^\mu=(C_1{}^\mu,C_2{}^\mu,C_3{}^\mu)\in\mathbb R^3.
\]
The already-established criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{span}\{b^1,b^2,b^3\}=\mathbb R^3
\iff
A_1(p)\ \text{is nondegenerate for generic }p\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:O_spancrit}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3 C_a{}^iC_a{}^j-C_0{}^iC_0{}^j,
\qquad
G_{ij}>0.
}
\label{eq:O_Gij}
\end{equation}
The identity part \(C_0{}^\mu\mathbf 1_2\) is not load-bearing once the traceless symbol is nondegenerate. 

\subsection{Step 5: convert to the actual S2 coefficients}

The local CP\(^2\) projector-defect geometry naturally supports the S2 branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:O_S2}
\end{equation}
The actual local overlap formulas are already known:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:O_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))\bigr),
}
\label{eq:O_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))\bigr).
}
\label{eq:O_beta}
\end{equation}
These are exactly the coefficient-extraction formulas we need. 

\paragraph{Meaning.}
So the microscopic task is not to guess \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\).
It is to derive the coefficient functions
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\qquad
h_{11}(\theta),\qquad
h_{12}(\theta),\qquad
h_{21}(\theta),\qquad
h_{22}(\theta)
\]
from the full background-dependent Hessian.

\subsection{Step 6: exact concrete Class II/local branch}

Inside the explicit local Class II-compatible branch, one may write
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]
The exact local reduction then yields
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\label{eq:O_explicit_local}
\end{equation}
with
\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:O_lambda_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:O_alphabeta_explicit}
\end{equation}
Hence the full S2 nondegeneracy condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:O_nondeg}
\end{equation}
This is already isolated as the exact remaining coefficient problem in the explicit local operator class. 

\subsection{The actual Hessian-extraction protocol}

We can now summarize the operator protocol that must be executed on the complete TECT PDE.

\paragraph{Protocol O1. Background insertion.}
Insert the shell-/defect-adapted background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(\bar A_B,\bar n_B,\bar\chi_B)
\]
into the full microscopic action or equations of motion.

\paragraph{Protocol O2. Tangent parametrization.}
Rewrite projector fluctuations as
\[
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
\eta\in Q_B.
\]

\paragraph{Protocol O3. Hessian construction.}
Compute the full background-dependent Hessian
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\]
as an operator on \(\eta(\xi,y)\).

\paragraph{Protocol O4. First-order derivative split.}
Separate the operator into
\[
H_B(\xi)-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}+W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}+\cdots
\]
and extract the odd first-order coefficient \(V^\mu(\xi)\).

\paragraph{Protocol O5. Low-mode problem.}
Solve the static transverse bundle problem
\[
H_Bu=\varepsilon u
\]
to obtain the graded low modes \(u_a^\pm\).

\paragraph{Protocol O6. Projection.}
Compute
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]

\paragraph{Protocol O7. Pauli decomposition.}
Write
\[
M^\mu=C_0{}^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i{}^\mu\sigma_i.
\]

\paragraph{Protocol O8. S2 reduction.}
Match the extracted matrices to the S2 form and read off
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
or equivalently
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

\paragraph{Protocol O9. Final finite test.}
Check
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:O_finaltest}
\end{equation}

\subsection{What is actually open}

At this point the strongest honest statement is exact and narrow.

What is already closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the graded \(2+2\) reduced Dirac theorem;
\item the structural matching of the actual local CP\(^2\) projector-defect Hessian to this operator class;
\item the explicit overlap formulas for the local S2 coefficients;
\item the finite nondegeneracy criterion in terms of
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains genuinely open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the final full microscopic TECT condensate/projector PDE in closed background-dependent Hessian form suitable for direct spectral analysis;
\item the explicit derivation of the coefficient functions
\[
h_\parallel,\ h_{11},\ h_{12},\ h_{21},\ h_{22}
\]
or equivalently the actual transport kernel \(V^\mu(\xi)\);
\item the direct microscopic verification that
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0)
\]
in complete TECT.
\end{enumerate}
These are exactly the open items isolated in the notes. 

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

So the full-PDE frontier has now been compressed as far as it can be compressed without inventing new microscopic dynamics:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{derive the actual background-dependent Hessian of complete TECT, extract }V^\mu(\xi),\text{ and evaluate the three coefficients }
\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:O_frontier}
\end{equation}

Once that is done, the graded bypass route either closes immediately or fails explicitly.

\section{Final Summary}

The graded \(2+2\) bypass route is now reduced to an explicit operator-extraction protocol.

The actual local defect/projector geometry supplies the rank-two bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\]
and the isolated graded infrared sector
\[
\mathcal K=\mathcal K_+\oplus \mathcal K_-,
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C\mathcal K_\pm=2,
\]
with low modes \(u_a^\pm(\xi)\).

The first-order transport kernel is extracted from the background-dependent Hessian as
\[
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B)T^\mu,
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\]

Projecting onto the graded low modes gives
\[
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle,
\qquad
M^\mu=C_0{}^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i{}^\mu\sigma_i.
}
\]

For the actual local S2 branch, the reduced symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with overlap formulas
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))).
}
\]

In the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
}
\]
so the finite graded nondegeneracy test is simply
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Therefore the strongest honest current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the graded bypass route is fully reduced to deriving }V^\mu(\xi)
\text{ from the complete TECT Hessian and extracting }
\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

This is no longer a conceptual gap.
It is an explicit background-Hessian calculation gap.
