\section{Background-Dependent Full Hessian Template for the Graded \texorpdfstring{$2+2$}{2+2} Route}

\subsection{Goal}

The graded bypass route has already reduced the full microscopic frontier to a single operator-extraction problem:
derive the actual odd first-order transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
\]
from the complete TECT Hessian around the shell-/defect-adapted background.

The purpose of this section is to fix the full Hessian template and the source-by-source protocol for reading off \(V^\mu(\xi)\).

\subsection{Minimal shell-/defect-adapted background}

The correct minimal background is not a uniform constant configuration, but the shell-/defect-adapted one
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:P_bgmin}
\end{equation}
or, if the gauge sector is kept explicitly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:P_bgmin_full}
\end{equation}

This is the minimal admissible choice because it:

\begin{enumerate}
\item preserves the shell/defect geometry,
\item keeps the reflection selection structure,
\item and produces nontrivial background-dependent vertices
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\qquad
\Gamma^{(3)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],\qquad
\Gamma^{(4)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}].
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Background split and Hessian}

Expand
\begin{equation}
\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi,
\qquad
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta),
\label{eq:P_split}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
A=a,\qquad
n=\bar n_B+\nu,\qquad
\chi=\bar\chi_B+\zeta.
\]
The full quadratic fluctuation operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\left.
\frac{\delta^2\Gamma}{\delta\varphi\,\delta\varphi}
\right|_{\bar\Phi_{\min}}.
}
\label{eq:P_Hessian}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Projector-defect parametrization}

For the local defect/projector sector, write
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\label{eq:P_PB}
\end{equation}
and parametrize the physical tangent fluctuations by
\begin{equation}
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0.
\label{eq:P_deltaP}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C Q_B=2.
}
\label{eq:P_QB}
\end{equation}

This converts the defect fluctuation problem into a rank-two bundle problem on \(Q_B(\xi)\).

\subsection{Coordinate split}

Let
\[
x=(y^\mu,\xi),
\qquad
y^\mu=(t,x_1,x_2)
\]
be worldvolume coordinates \(y^\mu\) plus one transverse coordinate \(\xi\).
The full Hessian can then be expanded in worldvolume derivatives:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+
\cdots.
}
\label{eq:P_Hessian_split}
\end{equation}

This is the full Hessian template that the complete TECT operator must be reduced to.

\subsection{Interpretation of the blocks}

The three relevant pieces in \eqref{eq:P_Hessian_split} are:

\paragraph{(i) Static transverse channel operator}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_B(\xi)=-\partial_\xi^2+\mathcal U_B(\xi)+\mathcal W_B(\xi)+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:P_HB}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal U_B,\mathcal W_B\) are \(Q_B\)-endomorphism-valued background potentials induced by the complete TECT Hessian.

This operator determines the even/odd low modes
\[
u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\]

\paragraph{(ii) Odd first-order transport kernel}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
}
\label{eq:P_L1}
\end{equation}
This is the load-bearing piece for the graded \(2+2\) route.

\paragraph{(iii) Higher-order worldvolume kinetic block}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_2=W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}.
}
\label{eq:P_L2}
\end{equation}
This influences dispersion corrections and spectral normalization, but not the principal first-order graded symbol.

\subsection{Source-by-source decomposition of the Hessian}

The complete microscopic Hessian should be organized as
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{grad}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pot}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{ani}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{med}}
+\cdots.
\label{eq:P_sources}
\end{equation}
The source-to-block mapping is then:

\paragraph{Gradient/background kinetic sector}
Contributes to all of
\[
H_B,\qquad V^\mu,\qquad W^{\mu\nu},
\]
through background-covariant derivatives and mixed \((\xi,y)\)-derivative terms.

\paragraph{Potential / static background sector}
Contributes only to
\[
H_B,
\]
through \(\xi\)-dependent channel mass/potential matrices.

\paragraph{Derivative anisotropy / transport sector}
This is the primary microscopic source for
\[
V^\mu(\xi),
\]
because it couples background gradients to worldvolume derivatives.

\paragraph{Gauge-fixing / projector-constraint sector}
Contributes to
\[
H_B,\qquad V^\mu,\qquad W^{\mu\nu}
\]
through bundle connection terms, frame-covariant derivative corrections, and projection constraints.

\paragraph{Mediator sector}
If the complete microscopic TECT realization contains the effective Class II carrier sector in the defect background, then its reduction can contribute to \(V^\mu(\xi)\) through induced traceless transport tensors, but not to the dangerous scalar identity-channel of the plain shell-pair route.

\subsection{Microscopic origin of the odd transport kernel}

The actual structural theorem already fixes the leading microscopic form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)\sim
(\partial_\xi P_B(\xi))\,T^\mu
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
(\partial_\xi z_B(\xi))\,\widetilde T^\mu
\sim
\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:P_Vorigin}
\end{equation}
Since \(P_B(\xi)\) is reflection-even,
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\]
one has
\[
\partial_\xi P_B(-\xi)=-\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi),
\]
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\label{eq:P_Vodd}
\end{equation}

This oddness is the entire reason why same-parity overlaps vanish while mixed even/odd overlaps survive.

\subsection{Low-mode problem}

Once \(H_B(\xi)\) is extracted, one solves
\begin{equation}
H_B u=\varepsilon u
\label{eq:P_static_spec}
\end{equation}
on the rank-two bundle \(Q_B(\xi)\).
For a reflection-symmetric defect background, the transverse spectrum decomposes into even and odd parity channels, giving the graded low modes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_a^+(\xi),\qquad u_a^-(\xi),
\qquad a=1,2,
}
\label{eq:P_u_pm}
\end{equation}
with
\[
u_a^+(-\xi)=+u_a^+(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(-\xi)=-u_a^-(\xi).
\]

\subsection{Projection formula for the mixed symbol}

The projected mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
=
\int d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger(\xi)\,V^\mu(\xi)\,u_b^-(\xi).
}
\label{eq:P_Mmu}
\end{equation}
Because \(u_a^+\) is even, \(u_b^-\) is odd, and \(V^\mu\) is odd, the integrand is even, so the mixed overlap is generically nonzero.

By contrast,
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,V^\mu u_b^\pm\rangle=0
\]
by parity, so the leading reduced operator is automatically grading-odd:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
}
\label{eq:P_D1}
\end{equation}
In particular,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:P_D1_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Conversion to S2 coefficients}

Expand
\begin{equation}
M^\mu=C_0{}^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i{}^\mu\sigma_i.
\label{eq:P_Mmu_pauli}
\end{equation}
The natural local branch is the S2 form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:P_S2}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
are read off from the corresponding components of \(M^\mu\).

The actual overlap formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:P_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
\bigl(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))\bigr),
}
\label{eq:P_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
\bigl(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))\bigr).
}
\label{eq:P_beta}
\end{equation}

So the real microscopic job is to derive the coefficient functions
\[
h_\parallel,\qquad h_{11},\qquad h_{12},\qquad h_{21},\qquad h_{22}
\]
from the complete Hessian.

\subsection{Equivalent transport-coefficient form}

In the explicit local transport language one may write
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\Sigma_3+\cdots.
\label{eq:P_V_transport}
\end{equation}
Projecting gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:P_transport_coeffs}
\end{equation}
with
\[
I_\theta=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3.
\]

In the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch one has
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:P_transport_coeffs_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Final finite test}

Therefore the full graded nondegeneracy problem is reduced to the finite microscopic extraction of
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O,
\]
or equivalently
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta.
\]
The final test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:P_finaltest}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Protocol summary}

The actual full-Hessian extraction protocol is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Insert the shell-/defect-adapted background \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\) into the complete TECT action.
\item Expand to second order and compute the background-dependent Hessian \(\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\).
\item Rewrite projector fluctuations in tangent-bundle form \(\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger\), \(z_B^\dagger\eta=0\).
\item Split the Hessian into the form
\[
H_B(\xi)-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}+W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}+\cdots.
\]
\item Solve the static bundle eigenproblem for \(H_B\) and identify the even/odd low modes \(u_a^\pm\).
\item Compute the projected overlaps
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]
\item Decompose \(M^\mu\) in the Pauli basis and match to the S2 form.
\item Read off \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\) or equivalently \(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\).
\item Check the finite nondegeneracy criterion \eqref{eq:P_finaltest}.
\end{enumerate}

%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary}

The full microscopic graded-bypass frontier is now reduced to a single Hessian-extraction protocol.

The correct shell-/defect-adapted background is
\[
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\bar\Phi_{\min}^{\mathrm{full}}=(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)).
}
\]

Projector fluctuations are written as
\[
\boxed{
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0,
\qquad
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
}
\]

The complete background-dependent Hessian must be reduced to
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
}
\]

The load-bearing piece is the odd first-order transport kernel
\[
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)\sim (\partial_\xi P_B)T^\mu,
\qquad
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\]

Solving the static transverse bundle problem for \(H_B\) gives the graded low modes \(u_a^\pm\), and the mixed symbol is
\[
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
}
\]
Same-parity overlaps vanish, so the leading reduced operator is automatically grading-odd:
\[
\boxed{
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
}
\]

Matching to the natural S2 branch gives
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

Equivalently, in the local transport-coefficient language,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\]
In the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\]

Therefore the full graded nondegeneracy problem is reduced to the finite microscopic test
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

So the strongest honest current statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the only remaining full-PDE gap is to derive }V^\mu(\xi)\text{ from the complete background-dependent Hessian and evaluate }
\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Source-by-Source Hessian Block Enumeration for the Full TECT Graded Route}

\subsection{Goal}

The graded \(2+2\) bypass route is already reduced to the extraction of the odd first-order transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]
What remains is not a conceptual theorem, but a source-by-source decomposition of the complete background-dependent Hessian:
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\longrightarrow
H_B(\xi),\quad
V^\mu(\xi),\quad
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi).
\]

The purpose of this section is to fix that decomposition in a way that can be used directly for the next explicit differentiation step.

\subsection{Universal Hessian template}

For the shell-/defect-adapted background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi))
\]
or
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}^{\mathrm{full}}=(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
the full quadratic operator on tangent fluctuations \(\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi)\) is organized as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+
\cdots.
}
\label{eq:Q_master_split}
\end{equation}
This is the actual operator template already structurally matched to the local projector Hessian. The remaining gap is only the explicit calculation of the coefficient blocks. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\subsection{Projector-defect geometry block}

The fluctuation bundle is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0.
}
\label{eq:Q_bundle}
\end{equation}
Thus every Hessian source must first be projected to the tangent bundle \(Q_B\). This bundle reduction is not optional; it is the actual microscopic low-energy field space. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\subsection{Source decomposition of the full Hessian}

We write the complete microscopic Hessian schematically as
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{grad}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pot}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{ani}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{med}}
+
\cdots,
\label{eq:Q_source_split}
\end{equation}
where each source class has a distinct block signature in \eqref{eq:Q_master_split}.

\subsection{Block A: gradient/background kinetic sector}

This is the sector originating from the background-covariant derivative structure of the complete action.
After inserting the \(\xi\)-dependent defect background, the gradient terms split into:

\begin{enumerate}
\item pure \(\xi\)-derivative pieces:
\[
\partial_\xi^\dagger\partial_\xi
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
H_B(\xi);
\]
\item mixed \((\xi,y^\mu)\)-derivative pieces:
\[
(\partial_\xi \bar\Phi_B)\,\partial_{y^\mu}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
V^\mu(\xi);
\]
\item pure worldvolume second-derivative pieces:
\[
\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{grad}}
\leadsto
H_B
\oplus
V^\mu
\oplus
W^{\mu\nu}.
}
\label{eq:Q_grad_map}
\end{equation}

This is the unavoidable source of the odd transport kernel, because the leading local candidates are linear in
\[
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi),\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\]
all of which are reflection-odd. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

\subsection{Block B: static potential / defect pinning sector}

Any source with no worldvolume derivatives contributes only to the transverse static channel operator.
Examples include:

\begin{enumerate}
\item projector pinning / anisotropy potentials \(U(P)\),
\item defect-background-dependent channel masses,
\item local static scalar self-interactions evaluated on \(\bar\Phi_{\min}\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pot}}
\leadsto
H_B(\xi)
\quad\text{only.}
}
\label{eq:Q_pot_map}
\end{equation}

This is exactly why the open problem list includes explicit derivation of the background-dependent potential matrix \(\mathcal U_B\): it belongs to \(H_B\), not to \(V^\mu\). :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13} :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

\subsection{Block C: anisotropic / transport sector}

This is the primary source for the load-bearing first-order transport kernel.
Its generic structure is
\[
(\text{background tensor})\cdot \partial_{y^\mu}
\]
projected to \(Q_B\).

At the local effective level this is the sector encoded by
\[
V^\mu(\xi)\sim \theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
or more explicitly by the S2-compatible transport ansatz
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\Sigma_3+\cdots.
\]

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{ani}}
\leadsto
V^\mu(\xi)
\quad\text{(primary load-bearing source).}
}
\label{eq:Q_ani_map}
\end{equation}

This is the source class whose projection determines
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O,
\]
and therefore the actual graded nondegeneracy test. :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15}

\subsection{Block D: gauge-fixing / projector-constraint / bundle-connection sector}

Because fluctuations live in the moving rank-two bundle \(Q_B(\xi)\), the Hessian must be expressed in a local frame \(e_a(\xi)\).
Differentiating this moving frame generates connection-like terms.
Thus the projector-constraint sector contributes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item bundle-covariant \(\xi\)-channel terms \(\to H_B\),
\item mixed bundle-connection transport terms \(\to V^\mu\),
\item possible worldvolume connection-squared pieces \(\to W^{\mu\nu}\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}
\leadsto
H_B
\oplus
V^\mu
\oplus
W^{\mu\nu}.
}
\label{eq:Q_proj_map}
\end{equation}

This sector is structurally unavoidable once the tangent bundle \(Q_B\) and the moving frame \(e_a(\xi)\) are used. :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16}

\subsection{Block E: mediator sector}

If the full microscopic realization contains the effective Class II carrier sector in the defect background, then its Hessian contribution is not primarily a static scalar mass source in the graded route.
Rather, the canonical minimal Class II representative renormalizes the derivative shell tensor coefficients while leaving the constant shell-level mass sector absent. :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17} :contentReference[oaicite:18]{index=18}

Therefore, in the graded bypass route:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{med}}
\leadsto
V^\mu(\xi)
\quad\text{(traceless transport sector),}
}
\label{eq:Q_med_map}
\end{equation}
and not the dangerous scalar identity-channel Bragg block of the discarded plain shell-pair route.

\subsection{Parity selection rule}

For a reflection-symmetric defect background,
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B(-\xi)=-\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),
\]
hence the leading transport kernel is odd:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Q_parity_V}
\end{equation}
Let the low transverse modes be
\[
u_a^+(-\xi)=+u_a^+(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(-\xi)=-u_a^-(\xi).
\]
Then
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,V^\mu u_b^\pm\rangle=0,
\qquad
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle\neq 0
\]
generically.

Thus the leading reduced symbol is automatically grading-odd:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:Q_D1}
\end{equation}
This is the concrete reason the graded bypass route avoids the scalar Bragg obstruction. :contentReference[oaicite:19]{index=19} :contentReference[oaicite:20]{index=20}

\subsection{Projection block and final coefficient extraction}

Once \(H_B(\xi)\) is constructed, solve
\[
H_Bu=\varepsilon u
\]
to obtain the low even/odd modes \(u_a^\pm\).
Then compute
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
}
\label{eq:Q_Mmu}
\end{equation}
Expanding
\[
M^\mu=C_0{}^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i{}^\mu\sigma_i,
\]
the natural S2 reduction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:Q_S2}
\end{equation}
Thus the only load-bearing microscopic outputs are
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad
\alpha,\qquad
\beta,
\]
or equivalently
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad
\Lambda_E,\qquad
\Lambda_O.
\]

In the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]
So the full graded nondegeneracy test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Q_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Source map summary}

The full source map is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{grad}}
\to
H_B\oplus V^\mu\oplus W^{\mu\nu},
}
\label{eq:Q_map1}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pot}}
\to
H_B,
}
\label{eq:Q_map2}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{ani}}
\to
V^\mu,
}
\label{eq:Q_map3}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}
\to
H_B\oplus V^\mu\oplus W^{\mu\nu},
}
\label{eq:Q_map4}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{med}}
\to
V^\mu
\quad\text{(in the graded bypass route).}
}
\label{eq:Q_map5}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

This finishes the source-level organization.

What remains open is no longer ``which mechanism might work.''
It is the explicit differentiation of the complete TECT action to obtain the coefficient blocks in \eqref{eq:Q_master_split}, especially the odd transport kernel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }V^\mu(\xi)\text{ from the full background-dependent Hessian and evaluate }
(M^\mu)_{ab}.
}
\label{eq:Q_honest_frontier}
\end{equation}
Once that is done, the graded bypass route either closes immediately or fails explicitly.

\section{Final Summary}

The complete TECT Hessian around the shell-/defect-adapted background must be organized as
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
}
\]

Here:

\[
\boxed{
H_B(\xi)
}
\]
is the static transverse channel operator on the rank-two bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\]

\[
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
}
\]
is the odd first-order transport kernel built from the \(\xi\)-variation of the defect background, and

\[
\boxed{
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)
}
\]
contains higher-order worldvolume kinetic corrections.

The source-by-source Hessian map is:

\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{grad}}
\to
H_B\oplus V^\mu\oplus W^{\mu\nu},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{pot}}
\to
H_B,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{ani}}
\to
V^\mu,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}
\to
H_B\oplus V^\mu\oplus W^{\mu\nu},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{med}}
\to
V^\mu
\quad\text{(graded bypass route).}
}
\]

For a reflection-symmetric defect background, the leading transport kernel is odd:
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\]
Hence same-parity overlaps vanish and mixed even/odd overlaps survive:
\[
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
}
\]
This automatically gives a grading-odd principal symbol
\[
\boxed{
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
}
\]

Matching to the natural S2 branch yields the final finite microscopic test
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Therefore the graded bypass frontier is now completely localized:
\[
\boxed{
\text{differentiate the complete TECT action, extract }V^\mu(\xi),\text{ project it to }(M^\mu)_{ab},\text{ and evaluate }
\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Term-by-Term Differentiation Rules for the Full TECT Hessian}

\subsection{Goal}

The graded \(2+2\) bypass route has already reduced the local Dirac problem to the extraction of the odd first-order transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
\]
from the background-dependent Hessian of complete TECT.

At this point, the correct next step is not another structural theorem.
It is to fix the term-by-term differentiation rules:
given a microscopic source term in the complete TECT action, which part of its second variation contributes to
\[
H_B(\xi),\qquad
V^\mu(\xi),\qquad
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)?
\]

\subsection{Background and tangent fluctuation}

We work with the shell-/defect-adapted background
\begin{equation}
\bar\Phi_{\min}=(0,\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\qquad
\text{or}
\qquad
\bar\Phi_{\min}^{\mathrm{full}}=(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\label{eq:R_bg}
\end{equation}
and project the defect fluctuations to the physical tangent bundle
\begin{equation}
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0,
\qquad
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:R_eta}
\end{equation}
This is the actual low-energy field space of the defect/projector problem. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{Normal-ordered Hessian decomposition}

After inserting \eqref{eq:R_bg} and \eqref{eq:R_eta} into the full microscopic action and taking the second variation, every quadratic term can be written, after integration by parts in \(\xi\), in the normal-ordered form
\begin{equation}
\delta^2\Gamma
=
\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\eta^\dagger
\Big[
\mathcal A(\xi)
+
\mathcal B(\xi)\partial_\xi
+
\mathcal C(\xi)\partial_\xi^2
+
\mathcal D^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal E^\mu(\xi)\partial_\xi\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal F^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots
\Big]\eta.
\label{eq:R_normal_ordered}
\end{equation}
The Hermitianized block decomposition is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:R_master}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Universal reading rule}

The extraction rule is purely algebraic:

\paragraph{(R1) Static transverse block}
All terms with no worldvolume derivative belong to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_B(\xi).
}
\label{eq:R_rule_HB}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(R2) First-order transport block}
All terms with exactly one worldvolume derivative belong to the operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
}
\label{eq:R_rule_V}
\end{equation}
Only the Hermitianized coefficient of \(-i\partial_{y^\mu}\) matters.

\paragraph{(R3) Higher kinetic block}
All terms with exactly two worldvolume derivatives belong to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}.
}
\label{eq:R_rule_W}
\end{equation}

Thus the only load-bearing microscopic term for the graded bypass route is the coefficient of exactly one worldvolume derivative.

\subsection{Term-by-term rule for the kinetic / gradient sector}

Take a generic two-derivative kinetic term
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}
=
\int d^4x\;
\mathcal K_{AB}(\Phi)\,
\partial_M\Phi^A\,\partial^M\Phi^B.
\label{eq:R_grad_generic}
\end{equation}
Expanding \(\Phi=\bar\Phi_{\min}+\varphi\), the quadratic fluctuation operator contains schematically:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \((\partial_\xi\varphi)^2\) and background-dependent potential pieces
\[
\Rightarrow H_B;
\]
\item \((\partial_{y^\mu}\varphi)^2\)
\[
\Rightarrow W^{\mu\nu};
\]
\item mixed background-gradient pieces
\[
(\partial_\xi\bar\Phi_{\min})\,\varphi\,\partial_{y^\mu}\varphi
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
V^\mu.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}
\leadsto
H_B^{(\mathrm{grad})}
\oplus
V_{\mathrm{grad}}^\mu
\oplus
W_{\mathrm{grad}}^{\mu\nu}.
}
\label{eq:R_grad_map}
\end{equation}

The actual local projector notes already indicate that the odd transport kernel is built from background gradients such as
\[
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B,\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\]
which come precisely from this mixed background-gradient channel. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\subsection{Term-by-term rule for the static potential sector}

Take a local potential term
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{pot}}=\int d^4x\;V(\Phi).
\label{eq:R_pot_generic}
\end{equation}
Its second variation contains no worldvolume derivatives at all. Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{pot}}
\leadsto
H_B^{(\mathrm{pot})}
\quad\text{only.}
}
\label{eq:R_pot_map}
\end{equation}
This is exactly why the open problem list separates the explicit derivation of the potential matrix \(\mathcal U_B\) from the transport kernel \(\mathcal V^\mu\): the former belongs to \(H_B\), not to \(V^\mu\). :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\subsection{Term-by-term rule for the anisotropic / transport sector}

Take a microscopic anisotropic transport term whose local reduced form is schematically
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{ani}}
=
\int d^4x\;
\mathcal T^\mu(\Phi,\partial_\xi\Phi)\,
\varphi^\dagger(-i\partial_{y^\mu})\varphi.
\label{eq:R_ani_generic}
\end{equation}
After background insertion,
\[
\mathcal T^\mu(\bar\Phi_{\min},\partial_\xi\bar\Phi_{\min})
\]
is a \(\xi\)-dependent bundle endomorphism, so its second variation contributes directly to the odd first-order transport kernel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{ani}}
\leadsto
V_{\mathrm{ani}}^\mu(\xi)
\quad\text{(primary load-bearing source).}
}
\label{eq:R_ani_map}
\end{equation}

This is the microscopic source class encoded by the actual-local transport ansatz
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
whose leading invariant coefficients \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)}\) were already isolated as the true microscopic coefficient problem. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\subsection{Term-by-term rule for the projector-constraint / moving-frame sector}

Because the physical fluctuations live in the moving bundle \(Q_B(\xi)\), one must express them in a local orthonormal frame \(e_a(\xi)\):
\[
\eta(\xi,y)=\eta^a(\xi,y)e_a(\xi).
\]
Differentiating this frame produces bundle-connection terms:
\[
\partial_\xi\eta
=
(\partial_\xi \eta^a)e_a+\eta^a \partial_\xi e_a.
\]
Hence the projector-constraint sector contributes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item static bundle-connection terms \(\to H_B\),
\item mixed connection/transport terms \(\to V^\mu\),
\item worldvolume kinetic corrections \(\to W^{\mu\nu}\).
\end{enumerate}

So:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}
\leadsto
H_B^{(\mathrm{proj})}
\oplus
V_{\mathrm{proj}}^\mu
\oplus
W_{\mathrm{proj}}^{\mu\nu}.
}
\label{eq:R_proj_map}
\end{equation}

This is structurally unavoidable once the tangent-bundle parametrization is used. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\subsection{Term-by-term rule for the mediator sector}

If the full microscopic realization contains the effective Class II carrier sector, then after integrating out the heavy mediator the induced quadratic operator has the schematic form
\begin{equation}
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}
\sim
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal C[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\,\mathcal C[\bar\Phi_{\min}]^\dagger.
\label{eq:R_med_generic}
\end{equation}
In the graded bypass route, this sector contributes to the traceless transport kernel rather than the discarded scalar Bragg channel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}
\leadsto
V_{\mathrm{med}}^\mu(\xi),
}
\label{eq:R_med_map}
\end{equation}
with the exact local compatible form
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{med}}^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3n^\mu\Sigma_3+\cdots.
\label{eq:R_med_local}
\end{equation}
In the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch one has
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]
This is precisely the coefficient dictionary already isolated in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14} :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15} :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16}

\subsection{Oddness filter}

For a reflection-symmetric background,
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi),
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B(-\xi)=-\partial_\xi P_B(\xi).
\]
Therefore any candidate term contributing to \(V^\mu\) must be odd in \(\xi\). This provides a strict filter:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Only terms linear in } \partial_\xi P_B,\ \partial_\xi z_B,\ \theta'(\xi)
\text{ (or odd descendants thereof) can contribute to }V^\mu.
}
\label{eq:R_odd_filter}
\end{equation}

As a consequence,
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,V^\mu u_b^\pm\rangle=0,
\qquad
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle\neq 0
\]
generically, so the leading reduced operator is automatically grading-odd:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:R_D1}
\end{equation}
This is the concrete microscopic reason the graded route bypasses the scalar Bragg obstruction. :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17} :contentReference[oaicite:18]{index=18}

\subsection{What is actually to be differentiated next}

After the source map above, the next explicit calculation is completely determined.

One must take each microscopic source term in the complete TECT action and compute only the coefficient of exactly one worldvolume derivative in the tangent-bundle Hessian:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left[\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}\right]_{1y},
\qquad
\left[\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{ani}}\right]_{1y},
\qquad
\left[\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}\right]_{1y},
\qquad
\left[\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}\right]_{1y}.
}
\label{eq:R_nextcalc}
\end{equation}
Their sum is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
V_{\mathrm{grad}}^\mu(\xi)
+
V_{\mathrm{ani}}^\mu(\xi)
+
V_{\mathrm{proj}}^\mu(\xi)
+
V_{\mathrm{med}}^\mu(\xi).
}
\label{eq:R_Vsum}
\end{equation}
The potential sector does not enter \(V^\mu\).

\subsection{Final finite extraction stage}

Once \(V^\mu(\xi)\) is known, the remaining steps are already fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item solve \(H_Bu=\varepsilon u\) on \(Q_B(\xi)\) to get \(u_a^\pm\);
\item compute
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle;
\]
\item decompose
\[
M^\mu=C_0{}^\mu\mathbf 1_2+C_i{}^\mu\sigma_i;
\]
\item match to the S2 form
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2);
\]
\item test
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

So the project has now been compressed to an actual differentiation checklist.

The open problem is not:
\[
\text{``which route should we use?''}
\]
That is settled.

The open problem is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{differentiate the complete TECT action term-by-term, extract the odd first-order tangent-bundle kernel }V^\mu(\xi),\text{ and evaluate its projected coefficients.}
}
\label{eq:R_frontier}
\end{equation}
This is now the only remaining microscopic gap in the graded bypass mainline.

\section{Final Summary}

The full TECT Hessian around the shell-/defect-adapted background is organized as
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
}
\]

The term-by-term differentiation rule is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{0 worldvolume derivatives } \Longrightarrow H_B(\xi),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{1 worldvolume derivative } \Longrightarrow V^\mu(\xi),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{2 worldvolume derivatives } \Longrightarrow W^{\mu\nu}(\xi).
}
\]

Accordingly, the full Hessian source map is:

\[
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}
\leadsto
H_B^{(\mathrm{grad})}\oplus V_{\mathrm{grad}}^\mu\oplus W_{\mathrm{grad}}^{\mu\nu},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{pot}}
\leadsto
H_B^{(\mathrm{pot})}\quad\text{only},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{ani}}
\leadsto
V_{\mathrm{ani}}^\mu\quad\text{(primary load-bearing source)},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}
\leadsto
H_B^{(\mathrm{proj})}\oplus V_{\mathrm{proj}}^\mu\oplus W_{\mathrm{proj}}^{\mu\nu},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}
\leadsto
V_{\mathrm{med}}^\mu
\quad\text{(graded bypass route)}.
}
\]

The reflection-odd filter is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi),
}
\]
so only terms linear in
\[
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B,\qquad
\theta'(\xi)
\]
or odd descendants thereof can contribute to the load-bearing first-order transport kernel.

Hence the actual next calculation is fully fixed:
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
V_{\mathrm{grad}}^\mu(\xi)
+
V_{\mathrm{ani}}^\mu(\xi)
+
V_{\mathrm{proj}}^\mu(\xi)
+
V_{\mathrm{med}}^\mu(\xi),
}
\]
with the potential sector absent from \(V^\mu\).

Therefore the only remaining microscopic gap in the graded-bypass mainline is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{differentiate the complete TECT action term-by-term, extract }V^\mu(\xi),\text{ and project it to obtain }\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Second Variation of the Gradient/Background Kinetic Sector}

\subsection{Goal}

We now differentiate the gradient/background kinetic sector explicitly and determine whether the pure isotropic kinetic core alone can generate the odd first-order transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]

The answer will be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the bare isotropic quadratic gradient core generates }H_B\text{ and }W^{\mu\nu},
\text{ but not a genuine }V^\mu\text{ at raw local Hessian level.}
}
\]

\subsection{Minimal isotropic projector gradient sector}

Take the minimal local projector gradient action
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}[P]
=
\frac{\rho}{4}\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\Tr(\partial_M P\,\partial^M P),
\qquad
M=(\xi,\mu),
\label{eq:S_grad_min}
\end{equation}
with a static defect background
\[
P_B=P_B(\xi),
\qquad
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi).
\]

Physical tangent fluctuations are parameterized by
\begin{equation}
\delta P=\eta z_B^\dagger+z_B\eta^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger\eta=0,
\qquad
\eta(\xi,y)\in Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\label{eq:S_deltaP_eta}
\end{equation}

Choose a local orthonormal frame \(e_a(\xi)\) of \(Q_B\) and write
\[
\eta(\xi,y)=\eta^a(\xi,y)e_a(\xi).
\]
Then the bundle connection is
\[
\mathcal A_\xi=-\,i\,e^\dagger\partial_\xi e.
\]

For the explicit defect frame already identified in the local projector analysis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal A_\xi=0.
}
\label{eq:S_Axi_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Quadratic variation of the isotropic core}

Expanding \eqref{eq:S_grad_min} to quadratic order around \(P_B\), the tangent-bundle fluctuation operator takes the standard bundle-Schr\"odinger form
\begin{equation}
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}
=
\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\eta^\dagger
\Big[
-\rho D_\xi^2
+
\mathcal U_B^{(\rho)}(\xi)
-
\rho\,\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\mu}
\Big]\eta,
\label{eq:S_d2G_grad}
\end{equation}
where
\[
D_\xi=\partial_\xi+i\mathcal A_\xi
\]
and \(\mathcal U_B^{(\rho)}(\xi)\) is the background-dependent Hermitian bundle potential induced by the \(\xi\)-dependent defect geometry.

Using \eqref{eq:S_Axi_zero}, one gets in the chosen frame
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}
=
\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\eta^\dagger
\Big[
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2
+
\mathcal U_B^{(\rho)}(\xi)
-
\rho\,\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\mu}
\Big]\eta.
}
\label{eq:S_d2G_grad_frame}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Block identification}

Comparing \eqref{eq:S_d2G_grad_frame} with the universal Hessian decomposition
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots,
\]
we read off:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_B^{(\mathrm{grad})}
=
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2+\mathcal U_B^{(\rho)}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:S_HB_grad}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{grad}}(\xi)=0
\qquad
\text{for the bare isotropic quadratic core in the explicit } \mathcal A_\xi=0 \text{ frame},
}
\label{eq:S_Vgrad_zero}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^{\mu\nu}_{\mathrm{grad}}(\xi)=\rho\,\delta^{\mu\nu}\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:S_Wgrad}
\end{equation}

Thus the pure isotropic two-derivative core supplies the static transverse operator and the second-order worldvolume kinetic block, but no genuine odd first-order transport kernel.

\subsection{Why this does not contradict the local matching theorem}

The local projector-defect matching theorem says that, for a reflection-symmetric defect background, the leading transport kernel is odd and is built from background gradients such as
\[
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi),\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi),\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\]
so same-parity overlaps vanish and mixed even/odd overlaps survive. This is a structural operator-class statement, not yet the explicit derivation of the final microscopic coefficient functions. The notes explicitly mark the derivation of the concrete transport kernel \(\mathcal V^\mu\) and its coefficient functions as still open.  :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

So \eqref{eq:S_Vgrad_zero} means only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the raw isotropic quadratic core by itself is not enough to produce the load-bearing first-order mixed symbol.}
}
\]

It does \emph{not} say that the final defect/projector operator class lacks such a symbol.

\subsection{Comparison with the shell-isotropic no-go}

This result is fully consistent with the previously established shell-level no-go:
for the naive free isotropic shell dispersion, and even in the locked one-mode slow-envelope expansion,
the first-order transport coefficient vanishes identically:
\[
\Bigl[Z D_{G_*}^2-Y(D_{G_*}^2)^2\Bigr]_{\text{1st order}}=0.
\]
Hence the actual coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
cannot arise from the pure free isotropic shell dispersion alone. They must come from more structured transport sectors. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

Equation \eqref{eq:S_Vgrad_zero} is the local projector analogue of that same obstruction.

\subsection{What kind of terms can generate a nonzero \(V^\mu\)?}

To generate a genuine first-order transport kernel, one needs a term in the quadratic Hessian that is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item linear in one worldvolume derivative \(\partial_{y^\mu}\),
\item odd under \(\xi\mapsto -\xi\),
\item bundle-endomorphism valued on \(Q_B\).
\end{enumerate}

Thus the minimal candidate sources are terms linear in
\[
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B,\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\]
multiplied by an internal/worldvolume tensor structure. This is precisely the structural content of the local transport ansatz
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

Therefore the genuinely load-bearing source classes are:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{ani}}(\xi),
\qquad
V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}(\xi),
\qquad
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
}
\label{eq:S_real_sources}
\end{equation}
rather than the bare isotropic quadratic core.

\subsection{Explicitly compatible structured sectors}

The notes already isolate the concrete structured sources that can realize the needed coefficients:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the local projector-defect transport matrix
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
whose microscopic coefficient functions remain open in full TECT; 

\item the primitive longitudinal commutator-square channel
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu,
\]
which gives in the explicit representative
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3;
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\item the explicit transverse odd-gradient channels
\[
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a;
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\item admissible mixed \((i,a)\)-carrier sectors such as Class II, whose local seed ansatz yields
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J
\]
generically inside the Class II truncation. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Practical conclusion for the Hessian program}

The result of the present differentiation step is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}
=
H_B^{(\mathrm{grad})}
+
W_{\mathrm{grad}}^{\mu\nu}\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu},
\qquad
V^\mu_{\mathrm{grad}}=0
\ \text{for the bare isotropic quadratic core}.
}
\label{eq:S_final_grad}
\end{equation}

Hence the actual next source to differentiate is not the isotropic core again, but the first structured transport-producing sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{ani}}
\quad\text{and/or}\quad
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}.
}
\label{eq:S_next_source}
\end{equation}
Only these can determine the genuine microscopic coefficient functions
\[
h_\parallel,\ h_{11},\ h_{12},\ h_{21},\ h_{22}
\]
or equivalently
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary}

For the minimal isotropic projector gradient sector
\[
\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}[P]
=
\frac{\rho}{4}\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\Tr(\partial_M P\,\partial^M P),
\]
expanded around the shell-/defect-adapted background and projected to the tangent bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\]
the quadratic fluctuation operator in the explicit defect frame with
\[
\mathcal A_\xi=0
\]
takes the form
\[
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}
=
\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\eta^\dagger
\Big[
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2
+
\mathcal U_B^{(\rho)}(\xi)
-
\rho\,\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\mu}
\Big]\eta.
\]

Therefore its Hessian blocks are
\[
\boxed{
H_B^{(\mathrm{grad})}
=
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2+\mathcal U_B^{(\rho)}(\xi),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{grad}}(\xi)=0
\quad
\text{for the bare isotropic quadratic core},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
W^{\mu\nu}_{\mathrm{grad}}(\xi)=\rho\,\delta^{\mu\nu}\mathbf 1_2.
}
\]

This is fully consistent with the already-established shell-level result that the naive free isotropic shell dispersion and locked one-mode isotropic kinetic truncation produce no nontrivial first-order witness data. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

It is also consistent with the honest local matching theorem: the theorem proves that the \emph{operator class} naturally admits an odd transport kernel built from defect gradients, but the exact microscopic coefficient functions of that kernel remain open.  :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12}

Hence the practical conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the bare isotropic quadratic gradient core is not the load-bearing source of }V^\mu(\xi).
}
\]

The genuine microscopic transport sources must instead come from structured gradient-sensitive sectors:
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{ani}}(\xi),\qquad
V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}(\xi),\qquad
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi).
}
\]

So the Hessian program has now advanced to a sharper form:
\[
\boxed{
\text{differentiate the first structured transport-producing sector next, not the isotropic core again.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Second Variation of the Anisotropic / Transport Sector}

\subsection{Goal}

The previous step established that the bare isotropic quadratic gradient core gives
\[
H_B^{(\mathrm{grad})}\neq 0,
\qquad
W_{\mathrm{grad}}^{\mu\nu}\neq 0,
\qquad
V_{\mathrm{grad}}^\mu=0
\]
at raw local Hessian level.

Therefore the first genuinely nonzero microscopic source of the graded first-order transport kernel must come from a structured transport-producing sector.
The purpose of the present step is to differentiate that sector explicitly and identify its contribution to
\[
V^\mu(\xi).
\]

\subsection{Important distinction: static anisotropy potential versus transport anisotropy}

A static anisotropy potential such as
\begin{equation}
V(P)=\frac{\lambda}{2}\,\Tr([H,P]^2),
\qquad
H=\mathrm{diag}(1,0,-1),
\label{eq:T_static_anisotropy}
\end{equation}
does \emph{not} itself produce the odd first-order worldvolume transport block.
Its second variation contributes only to the static bundle Schr\"odinger operator \(H_B\), yielding the explicit channel-diagonal Hessian
\[
\mathcal H_B^{\mathrm{stat}}
=
-\rho\,\partial_\xi^2
+
\begin{pmatrix}
\lambda \cos^2 2\theta(\xi)-2\rho\,\theta'(\xi)^2 & 0\\
0 & \lambda-\rho\,\theta'(\xi)^2
\end{pmatrix},
\]
while the leading odd transport kernel is a separate background-gradient-built structure. 

Hence the source we must differentiate now is not the static anisotropy potential \eqref{eq:T_static_anisotropy}, but the actual first-order transport sector.

\subsection{Strongest honest local transport source}

The strongest honest local transport form already isolated in the notes is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:T_V_general}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, at the action level one writes the transport source as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma_{\mathrm{trans}}
=
-i\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\eta^\dagger(\xi,y)\,
V^\mu(\xi)\,
\partial_{y^\mu}\eta(\xi,y).
}
\label{eq:T_Gtrans}
\end{equation}
This is already a quadratic fluctuation term on the tangent bundle \(Q_B(\xi)\), so in the Hessian language it is itself a second-variation contribution.

Thus the second variation is immediate:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{trans}}
=
-i\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\eta^\dagger(\xi,y)\,
V^\mu(\xi)\,
\partial_{y^\mu}\eta(\xi,y).
}
\label{eq:T_d2Gtrans}
\end{equation}

Comparing with the master Hessian decomposition
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots,
\]
we read off immediately:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_B^{(\mathrm{ani/trans})}=0,
\qquad
V_{\mathrm{ani/trans}}^\mu(\xi)=V^\mu(\xi),
\qquad
W_{\mathrm{ani/trans}}^{\mu\nu}=0
}
\label{eq:T_read_off}
\end{equation}
at principal order.

So this source is purely load-bearing for the graded first-order symbol.

\subsection{Reflection parity}

For the explicit defect representative
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
one has
\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr).
\]
Therefore \(\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi)\), so the kernel \eqref{eq:T_V_general} is automatically odd:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(-\xi)=-V^\mu(\xi).
}
\label{eq:T_V_odd}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the parity property required by the graded even/odd overlap theorem. 

\subsection{S2-compatible decomposition}

The broad actual-local transport class admits the shell-compatible singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
\Lambda_0^{(0)}\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
O(\theta^2).
}
\label{eq:T_M_broad}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{broad}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_0^{(0)}\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta' \theta^2).
}
\label{eq:T_V_broad}
\end{equation}

Projecting this kernel to the even/odd low modes gives the leading witnesses
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:T_lambda_broad}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)}I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\beta
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)}I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:T_ab_broad}
\end{equation}
with
\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\neq 0.
\]
So in the broad actual-local class, a constant-leading longitudinal branch is symmetry-allowed. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\subsection{Exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch}

The exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch is sharper.
The transverse sector already appears at order \(\theta'(\xi)\), but the longitudinal sector is not of \(I_\theta\)-type.
Instead, it arises from the primitive commutator-square channel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q\,
n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:T_V_parallel_primitive}
\end{equation}
Using
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\]
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel),\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:T_V_parallel_tr}
\end{equation}
Thus the longitudinal witness is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:T_lambda_parallel_exact}
\end{equation}
with
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0.
\]

The transverse channels are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
}
\label{eq:T_V_transverse_exact}
\end{equation}
giving
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:T_alpha_beta_exact}
\end{equation}

So in the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{ani/trans}}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:T_V_exact}
\end{equation}
This is the first genuinely nonzero microscopic source of the full S2 witness triplet. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9} :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\subsection{Projection and reduced symbol}

Let \(u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi)\) be the graded low modes of the static bundle operator.
Then
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\label{eq:T_Mmu}
\end{equation}
Since \(V^\mu\) is odd, same-parity overlaps vanish, while the mixed overlaps survive.
Therefore the reduced first-order symbol is automatically grading-odd:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:T_D1_S2}
\end{equation}

Thus the anisotropic/transport sector is precisely the first source that can produce a genuinely nonzero \(V^\mu\) and hence nontrivial \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\).

\subsection{Final finite test}

The full graded nondegeneracy problem is therefore reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:T_final_test}
\end{equation}
or equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:T_final_test2}
\end{equation}

\subsection{What is actually proved and what remains open}

What is proved at this step:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the first genuinely nonzero microscopic source of the odd first-order transport kernel is the anisotropic / transport sector, not the bare isotropic gradient core;
\item its second variation contributes directly to \(V^\mu(\xi)\) and not primarily to \(H_B\) or \(W^{\mu\nu}\);
\item the broad actual-local operator class allows a constant-leading longitudinal branch;
\item the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch realizes the transverse channels at \(I_\theta\)-order and the longitudinal channel in the primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\)-branch.
\end{enumerate}

What remains honestly open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual complete microscopic TECT transport kernel has not yet been derived from the final full action;
\item therefore the actual coefficient point
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\ \Lambda_E^{(0)},\ \Lambda_O^{(0)}
\]
or equivalently
\[
\lambda_c,\ \Lambda_E,\ \Lambda_O
\]
is not yet known;
\item consequently, the full microscopic verification of
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0)
\]
remains the final coefficient-identification problem.
\end{enumerate}

%%%%%

\section{Final Summary}

The bare isotropic quadratic gradient core is not the load-bearing source of the odd first-order transport kernel.
Its second variation gives
\[
H_B^{(\mathrm{grad})}\neq 0,
\qquad
W_{\mathrm{grad}}^{\mu\nu}\neq 0,
\qquad
V_{\mathrm{grad}}^\mu=0
\]
at raw local Hessian level. This is fully consistent with the previously established shell-level isotropic first-order no-go. :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

The first genuinely nonzero microscopic source of \(V^\mu(\xi)\) is instead the anisotropic / transport sector, whose quadratic Hessian contribution is already of the form
\[
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{ani/trans}}
=
-i\int \eta^\dagger V^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\eta.
\]
So at principal order,
\[
\boxed{
H_B^{(\mathrm{ani/trans})}=0,
\qquad
V_{\mathrm{ani/trans}}^\mu(\xi)=V^\mu(\xi),
\qquad
W_{\mathrm{ani/trans}}^{\mu\nu}=0.
}
\]

In the broad actual-local transport class,
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
with shell-compatible leading invariant coefficients
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\qquad
\Lambda_E^{(0)},\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)},
\]
so a constant-leading longitudinal branch is symmetry-allowed. 

In the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch, however, the transverse sector starts at \(I_\theta\)-order while the longitudinal sector starts only in the primitive commutator-square channel:
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{ani/trans}}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+\cdots.
}
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\]

Therefore the anisotropic/transport sector is the first explicit microscopic source that can produce the full nontrivial S2 witness triplet, and the full graded nondegeneracy test remains
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

So the honest remaining microscopic gap is now completely localized to the coefficient-identification problem:
derive the actual complete TECT transport kernel and determine whether it lands at a nondegenerate coefficient point.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Second Variation of the Class II Mediator Sector}

\subsection{Goal}

The graded \(2+2\) bypass route has isolated the genuinely load-bearing microscopic source classes for the first-order transport kernel.
Among them, Class II is the strongest currently explicit microscopic class because it packages all three invariant coordinates at once:
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O.
\]
The purpose of this step is to compute the quadratic Class II reduction far enough to identify the actual mediator contribution to
\[
-iV^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]

\subsection{UV Class II action and heavy-field elimination}

The minimal Class II mediated UV Lagrangian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}\,X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha\,X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta\,X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:U_ClassII_UV}
\end{equation}
Here \(X_i^a\) carries exactly the needed \((i,a)\)-carrier structure, and the minimal choices are
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)\,T_a\,\Psi+\mathrm{h.c.},
\qquad
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T_a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\label{eq:U_JK_min}
\end{equation}
or after shell/tangent reduction
\[
K_i^a\sim \partial_i\delta P^a\,\psi.
\]
All of this is already explicit in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

Eliminating the heavy mediator gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_i^a
=
-\frac{\alpha}{M_X^2}J_i^a[\Psi]
-\frac{\beta}{M_X^2}K_i^a[P,\psi],
}
\label{eq:U_X_elim}
\end{equation}
hence the exact effective action contains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
S_0
-
\frac{\alpha^2}{2M_X^2}\int J_i^aJ_i^a
-
\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\int J_i^aK_i^a
-
\frac{\beta^2}{2M_X^2}\int K_i^aK_i^a.
}
\label{eq:U_Seff_expand}
\end{equation}
The load-bearing mixed term is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\int J_i^a[\Psi]\,K_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:U_Smix}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the mixed source already identified as the relevant one. 

\subsection{Background expansion}

Expand around the shell-/defect-adapted background
\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}
=
(\bar A_B(\xi),\bar n_B(\xi),\bar\chi_B(\xi)),
\]
or, in the reduced locked notation,
\[
\Psi=(\phi_0+\sigma)z_0+\psi,
\qquad
P=P_B+\delta P,
\qquad
\delta P\sim z_B\xi^\dagger+\xi z_B^\dagger.
\]
Then decompose
\begin{equation}
J_i^a
=
\bar J_i^a(\xi)
+
J_{i}^{a(1)}[\eta]
+
J_i^{a(2)}[\eta]
+\cdots,
\label{eq:U_J_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^a
=
\bar K_i^a(\xi)
+
K_{i}^{a(1)}[\eta]
+
K_i^{a(2)}[\eta]
+\cdots,
\label{eq:U_K_expand}
\end{equation}
where \(\eta\in Q_B(\xi)\) is the tangent fluctuation field.

For the defect background, the background-gradient content enters through
\[
\partial_\xi P_B,\qquad
\partial_\xi z_B,\qquad
\theta'(\xi),
\]
so any first-order transport contribution extracted from \(J^{(1)}\) or \(K^{(1)}\) is automatically odd in \(\xi\). This parity fact is already closed. 

\subsection{Normal form of the first variations}

The only pieces relevant to the graded principal symbol are those linear in \(\eta\) and containing exactly one worldvolume derivative.
So we write the first variations in normal form:
\begin{equation}
J_i^{a(1)}[\eta]
=
\mathcal J_{i}^{a(0)}(\xi)\,\eta
+
\mathcal J_{i}^{a\mu}(\xi)\,(-i\partial_{y^\mu})\eta
+\cdots,
\label{eq:U_J1_normal}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^{a(1)}[\eta]
=
\mathcal K_{i}^{a(0)}(\xi)\,\eta
+
\mathcal K_{i}^{a\mu}(\xi)\,(-i\partial_{y^\mu})\eta
+\cdots.
\label{eq:U_K1_normal}
\end{equation}
Here the superscript \((0)\) means no worldvolume derivative, while the \(\mu\)-part carries exactly one \(-i\partial_{y^\mu}\).

\subsection{Quadratic mediator Hessian}

Substituting \eqref{eq:U_J_expand} and \eqref{eq:U_K_expand} into \eqref{eq:U_Seff_expand}, the quadratic fluctuation operator from the mediator sector is schematically
\begin{align}
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}
&=
-\frac{\alpha^2}{2M_X^2}\,\delta^2(JJ)
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\,\delta^2(JK)
-\frac{\beta^2}{2M_X^2}\,\delta^2(KK).
\label{eq:U_d2G_med_split}
\end{align}

At the level of the graded principal symbol, the only load-bearing contributions are those with exactly one worldvolume derivative.
These arise from the first variations \eqref{eq:U_J1_normal}--\eqref{eq:U_K1_normal}.

Keeping only the \(1y\)-terms, one obtains
\begin{align}
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}\Big|_{1y}
&=
-i\int d\xi\,d^3y\;
\eta^\dagger
\Big[
V^\mu_{JJ}(\xi)+V^\mu_{JK}(\xi)+V^\mu_{KK}(\xi)
\Big]\partial_{y^\mu}\eta,
\label{eq:U_d2G_1y}
\end{align}
with
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{JJ}(\xi)
=
-\frac{\alpha^2}{M_X^2}
\bigl[\bar J_i^a(\xi)\,\mathcal J_i^{a\mu}(\xi)\bigr]_{\mathrm{tan}},
\label{eq:U_VJJ}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{JK}(\xi)
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\bigl[
\bar J_i^a(\xi)\,\mathcal K_i^{a\mu}(\xi)
+
\bar K_i^a(\xi)\,\mathcal J_i^{a\mu}(\xi)
\bigr]_{\mathrm{tan}},
\label{eq:U_VJK}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{KK}(\xi)
=
-\frac{\beta^2}{M_X^2}
\bigl[\bar K_i^a(\xi)\,\mathcal K_i^{a\mu}(\xi)\bigr]_{\mathrm{tan}}.
\label{eq:U_VKK}
\end{equation}
The subscript “tan” means projection to the tangent bundle endomorphism sector on \(Q_B(\xi)\).

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
V^\mu_{JJ}(\xi)+V^\mu_{JK}(\xi)+V^\mu_{KK}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:U_Vmed_sum}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Why the mixed \(J\!\cdot\!K\) channel is the load-bearing one}

The honest class-by-class coefficient audit already showed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item pure scalar/projector/amplitude-only classes are excluded;
\item a naive even singlet such as \(\theta'^2\sigma_3\) is excluded by parity;
\item the transverse doublet is explicitly allowed;
\item the primitive odd longitudinal singlet is the minimal surviving longitudinal mechanism;
\item Class II is the strongest explicit class because it packages all three directions \((a,b,c)\) at once.
\end{enumerate}


Translated into \eqref{eq:U_Vmed_sum}, this means:

- \(V^\mu_{JJ}\) and \(V^\mu_{KK}\) may renormalize static or non-load-bearing sectors, but by themselves they do not provide the sharpest explicit unified three-coordinate realization.
- The mixed channel \(V^\mu_{JK}\) is the cleanest admissible source carrying both:
  \[
  \text{background/shell gradient structure}
  \quad\text{and}\quad
  \text{internal tangent projector structure.}
  \]
So the actual load-bearing microscopic prototype is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med,\,lb}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\bigl[
\bar J_i^a(\xi)\,\mathcal K_i^{a\mu}(\xi)
+
\bar K_i^a(\xi)\,\mathcal J_i^{a\mu}(\xi)
\bigr]_{\mathrm{tan}}.
}
\label{eq:U_Vmed_lb}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Exact concrete quadratic reduction template}

Inside the exact concrete Class II quadratic reduction already extracted in the notes, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^aX_i^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,X_i^a\,C_{ij}^{ab}(D_j\psi)\,\xi^b
+\mathrm{h.c.}
}
\label{eq:U_LX2}
\end{equation}
Integrating out \(X_i^a\) yields the induced enriched tensor
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^aC_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\label{eq:U_deltaN}
\end{equation}
For the shell-adapted seed family
\[
m^a=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{33}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C_{ij}^{31}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C_{ij}^{32}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
this gives
\begin{equation}
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\label{eq:U_gcgego}
\end{equation}
Thus Class II is the unique currently explicit microscopic class realizing all three directions at once. 

In the local defect/projector transport language, this reduction matches the explicit S2 kernel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:U_Vmed_local}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:U_lambdas}
\end{equation}
This exact local coefficient dictionary is already closed. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\subsection{What is actually proved at this step}

What is proved:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the mediator sector contributes to the Hessian at quadratic order through the heavy-field Schur-complement structure \eqref{eq:U_Seff_expand};
\item its load-bearing first-order transport contribution is the \(1y\)-part of \(\delta^2(JK)\), namely \eqref{eq:U_Vmed_lb};
\item inside the exact concrete Class II quadratic template, this source reduces to the explicit three-coordinate transport kernel \eqref{eq:U_Vmed_local};
\item hence the graded nondegeneracy problem is reduced to
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

What is still honestly open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the unreduced final complete TECT expressions for \(J_i^a[\Psi]\) and \(K_i^a[P,\psi]\) in the physically relevant defect background;
\item whether the true complete TECT action actually realizes a nontrivial Class II sector there;
\item the final absolute normalization of \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\), equivalently \((\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\), in the complete dynamics.
\end{enumerate}
This is exactly the current honest status recorded in the notes. 

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

Therefore the mediator differentiation step is now as closed as it can be without inventing extra microscopic data.

The result is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}
\text{ contributes a genuine odd first-order transport kernel,}
}
\end{equation}
and inside the concrete Class II reduction template this kernel already carries the full S2 triplet
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

So the remaining full-PDE frontier is not the existence of a transport-producing mediator mechanism.
That is already explicit.

It is only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{whether the final complete TECT action realizes that nontrivial Class II sector in the relevant defect background, and with what coefficients.}
}
\label{eq:U_honest_frontier}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The Class II mediator sector starts from the explicit UV action
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha\,X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta\,X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\]
Eliminating the heavy field gives
\[
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
=
S_0
-
\frac{\alpha^2}{2M_X^2}\int J_i^aJ_i^a
-
\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\int J_i^aK_i^a
-
\frac{\beta^2}{2M_X^2}\int K_i^aK_i^a.
}
\]

The load-bearing source is the mixed term
\[
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(II)}
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}\int J_i^aK_i^a.
}
\]

After expanding around the shell-/defect-adapted background and keeping only the quadratic terms with exactly one worldvolume derivative, the mediator contribution to the graded transport kernel is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
V^\mu_{JJ}(\xi)+V^\mu_{JK}(\xi)+V^\mu_{KK}(\xi),
}
\]
with the actual load-bearing microscopic prototype
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med,\,lb}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{\alpha\beta}{M_X^2}
\bigl[
\bar J_i^a(\xi)\,\mathcal K_i^{a\mu}(\xi)
+
\bar K_i^a(\xi)\,\mathcal J_i^{a\mu}(\xi)
\bigr]_{\mathrm{tan}}.
}
\]

Inside the exact concrete Class II quadratic reduction already closed in the notes,
\[
\boxed{
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^aX_i^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,X_i^a C_{ij}^{ab}(D_j\psi)\xi^b+\mathrm{h.c.},
}
\]
integrating out \(X_i^a\) yields
\[
\boxed{
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^aC_{ij}^{ab}.
}
\]

For the shell-adapted seed family this gives
\[
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J,
}
\]
so Class II is the only currently explicit microscopic class that packages all three invariant coordinates at once.

In the local defect/projector transport language this becomes
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+\cdots,
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\]

Therefore the full graded nondegeneracy test is again
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

The strongest honest conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}
\text{ provides a genuinely explicit odd first-order transport source,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is still open whether the final complete TECT action realizes this nontrivial Class II sector in the physically relevant defect background, and with what final normalization.}
}
\]

\section{Actual Source Synthesis for the Graded Transport Kernel}

\subsection{Goal}

The graded \(2+2\) bypass route has already reduced the full microscopic frontier to the extraction of the odd first-order transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]
The remaining task is now to combine all genuinely nontrivial microscopic sources into a single transport kernel and separate:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the broad actual-local transport class,
\item the exact concrete Class II-compatible branch.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Master source synthesis}

From the previous steps, the bare isotropic quadratic core contributes only to
\[
H_B(\xi),\qquad W^{\mu\nu}(\xi),
\]
and not to a genuine odd first-order transport kernel.
Hence the actual transport source is the sum of the structured sectors:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
V^\mu_{\mathrm{trans}}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:V_master_sum}
\end{equation}
Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{trans}}\) denotes the direct odd transport/anisotropic sector;
\item \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}\) denotes bundle-connection/projector-frame induced transport;
\item \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}\) denotes the effective Class II mediator contribution.
\end{itemize}

All three are \(Q_B\)-endomorphism valued and reflection-odd in \(\xi\).

\subsection{Broad actual-local transport class}

The broad actual-local transport class already isolated in the notes is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:V_broad_form}
\end{equation}
with the leading shell-compatible invariant expansion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
\Lambda_0^{(0)}\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
O(\theta^2).
}
\label{eq:V_broad_inv}
\end{equation}

Thus the synthesized broad transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{broad}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_0^{(0)}\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta'\theta^2).
}
\label{eq:V_broad_kernel}
\end{equation}

Projecting onto the graded low modes gives
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:V_broad_projected}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\alpha
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)}I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\beta
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)}I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
}
\label{eq:V_broad_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Since \(I_\theta\neq 0\), the broad-class nondegeneracy test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:V_broad_test}
\end{equation}

This shows that in the broad actual-local operator class a constant-leading longitudinal branch is allowed. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\subsection{Exact concrete Class II-compatible branch}

The exact concrete Class II-compatible branch is sharper.
Its key feature is that the transverse channels start at the \(I_\theta\)-level, while the longitudinal witness does not come from the constant-leading \(I_\theta\)-branch.
Instead it starts in the primitive commutator-square channel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.

\end{equation}

The transverse channels are

\qquad

=
\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.

\label{eq:V_trans_explicit}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact concrete Class II-compatible transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+

\Bigr]
+\cdots.

\end{equation}

Projecting to the low modes gives
\begin{equation}

\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\Lambda_O.

\label{eq:V_ClassII_coeffs}
\end{equation}
Hence the exact concrete Class II nondegeneracy test is

\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),

equivalently

\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).

This is the exact finite witness test already recorded in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\subsection{Unified longitudinal decision protocol}

The notes already give the exact practical execution order.
We can rewrite it as the following deterministic decision tree.

\paragraph{(W1) Extract the shell-compatible local transport matrix.}
Compute
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
\]
from the actual complete TECT Hessian extraction.

\paragraph{(W2) Test the constant-leading longitudinal coefficient.}
Compute
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\,\Tr\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)\bigr].
}
\label{eq:W_Lambda0_def}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(W3) If \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\), stop.}
Then the actual theory lies on Branch A, and
\[
\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}+O(\theta_0^3\kappa).

\paragraph{(W4) If \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\), compute the primitive channel.}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}},
}
\label{eq:W_Sxi}
\end{equation}
and project the actual longitudinal transport onto
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu
