to extract \(\lambda_c\).

\paragraph{(W5) If \(\lambda_c\neq 0\), stop.}
Then the actual theory lies on Branch B, and
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

\paragraph{(W6) If both vanish, the current branch library is exhausted.}
That is, if
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\lambda_c=0,
\]
then the currently established longitudinal seed library contains no surviving branch, and one must inspect higher-order even longitudinal channels explicitly.

This exact protocol is already stated in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10}

\subsection{Why the longitudinal sector is the true bottleneck}

The notes are explicit that once the transverse channel survives microscopically, the real bottleneck is the longitudinal one:
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently, once \((\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)\) is under control, the only remaining witness problem is the survival of one admissible longitudinal seed direction inside the actual microscopic transport space \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\). :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

Thus the full witness problem is no longer symmetric among the three coefficients.
The actual audit order is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{transverse already largely reduced}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{longitudinal branch selection is the remaining bottleneck.}
}
\label{eq:W_bottleneck}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Exact final finite tests}

The branch-sensitive final tests are therefore:

\paragraph{Branch A test}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:W_testA}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Branch B test}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:W_testB}
\end{equation}

If one wants a single combined formulation, it is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl[\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\ \text{or}\ 
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\ \text{and}\ \lambda_c\neq 0)\bigr]
\quad\text{and}\quad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:W_unified_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Strongest honest conclusion}

We can now state the exact honest branch-sensitive status:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the longitudinal witness problem is reduced to a two-branch finite decision protocol.}
}
\label{eq:W_closed}
\end{equation}

What remains open is not the reduced spectral logic, but the actual microscopic coefficient extraction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the complete microscopic TECT transport extraction has not yet determined whether }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\text{ or instead }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\text{ with }
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:W_open}
\end{equation}
This is already explicitly isolated in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\section{Final Summary}

The graded-bypass Dirac problem is now reduced to a branch-sensitive coefficient audit.

What is already closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The reduced graded \(2+2\) theorem is rigorous.
\item The actual local projector-defect geometry supports the natural S2 branch
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
\item In the broad actual-local operator class, the nondegeneracy test is
\[
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\item In the exact concrete Class II branch, the witness coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\]
so the nondegeneracy test becomes
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

The actual unresolved question is only which longitudinal branch the complete microscopic TECT transport extraction realizes:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Branch A: }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}+O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Branch B: }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\ \lambda_c\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

Thus the exact final finite tests are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Branch A: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,\quad (\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)})\neq (0,0),
}
\]

or

\[
\boxed{
\text{Branch B: }\lambda_c\neq 0,\quad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Therefore the strongest honest current conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the longitudinal witness problem is fully reduced to a two-branch finite decision protocol,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the complete microscopic TECT transport extraction has not yet determined which branch the actual coefficient point lies on.}
}
\]

\section{Actual Longitudinal Branch Test}

\subsection{Goal}

The graded \(2+2\) route has already reduced the full local Dirac problem to the S2 witness condition
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
The transverse sector is already in explicit \(I_\theta\)-form, so the true remaining bottleneck is the longitudinal sector. 

The actual microscopic task is therefore not another structural reduction.
It is the finite branch selection problem:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\text{ with }\lambda_c\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\label{eq:X_branch_question}
\]

\subsection{Input data from the local transport extraction}

Assume the full microscopic extraction has produced the shell-compatible local transport kernel
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:X_Vmu}
\end{equation}
with invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:X_Minv}
\end{equation}
Then the actual witness formulas are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:X_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_E(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_O(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:X_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}
This is already explicitly fixed in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\subsection{Step 0: transverse sector is already reduced}

The transverse sector is already completely in \(I_\theta\)-form:
\[
\alpha=I_\theta \Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta \Lambda_O,
\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0.
\]
Hence the only remaining transverse condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:X_transverse_test}
\end{equation}
So the actual remaining ambiguity is exclusively longitudinal. 

\subsection{Branch A: constant-leading longitudinal test}

In the broad actual-local operator class, the leading invariant longitudinal coefficient
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
\]
is not symmetry-forbidden. If it is nonzero, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
}
\label{eq:X_branchA_formula}
\end{equation}
Since \(I_\theta\neq 0\), it follows immediately that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:X_branchA_implication}
\end{equation}
Thus the Branch A decision criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\textbf{Branch A test: }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:X_branchA_test}
\end{equation}
This branch is allowed in the broad actual-local class, but has not yet been proven to be the one realized by the complete microscopic TECT extraction. 

\subsection{Branch B: primitive longitudinal test}

If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
one must pass to the primitive longitudinal channel already explicitly isolated in the notes.

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\label{eq:X_Sxi_def}
\end{equation}
Then the primitive longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
}
\label{eq:X_Vparallel_primitive}
\end{equation}
Factor the actual primitive longitudinal component as
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{act}}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu
+
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{rem}}(\xi),
\label{eq:X_lambda_c_factor}
\end{equation}
where \(V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{rem}}\) is orthogonal to the primitive target covector in the reduced witness pairing. This is the exact protocol already written in the notes. 

In the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:X_Sxi_explicit}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:X_Vparallel_tr}
\end{equation}
The corresponding primitive overlap is
\begin{equation}
J_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:X_Jparallel}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
}
\label{eq:X_Itheta3_nonzero}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:X_branchB_formula}
\end{equation}
So the Branch B decision criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\textbf{Branch B test: }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\quad
\lambda_c\neq 0,\quad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:X_branchB_test}
\end{equation}
Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\), this implies immediately
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:X_branchB_implication}
\end{equation}
All of this is already explicitly established for the concrete primitive/Class II-compatible branch. 

\subsection{Unified decision tree}

The two branches combine into a single deterministic audit protocol:

\paragraph{(X1) Extract the invariant transport matrix.}
Compute \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) from the actual microscopic TECT linearization and reduce it to the invariant profile functions
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\qquad
h_E(\theta),\qquad
h_O(\theta).
\]

\paragraph{(X2) Test the leading longitudinal invariant.}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)].
}
\label{eq:X_Lambda0}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(X3) If \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\), stop.}
Then the actual coefficient point lies on Branch A and
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\]
immediately.

\paragraph{(X4) If \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\), test the primitive channel.}
Compute
\[
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\]
and extract the primitive coefficient \(\lambda_c\) from the projection of the actual longitudinal transport onto
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
\]

\paragraph{(X5) If \(\lambda_c\neq 0\), stop.}
Then the actual coefficient point lies on Branch B and
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{(X6) If both vanish, the current branch library is exhausted.}
That is,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\lambda_c=0
\]
means the presently established longitudinal seed library contains no surviving witness and one must inspect higher-order even longitudinal channels explicitly. This is already the honest closure statement in the notes. 

\subsection{Why this is the true bottleneck}

The transverse sector already sits in the \(I_\theta\)-branch and is reduced to a finite nonzero test on \((\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\).
The longitudinal sector is different because a naive even singlet source proportional to \(\theta'^2\sigma_3\) fails by parity, so the primitive commutator-square channel is the first admissible odd singlet. 

Therefore the remaining actual microscopic problem is no longer the full \(3\)-parameter witness problem symmetrically.
It is only the longitudinal branch selection:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete microscopic TECT transport extraction realize Branch A or Branch B?}
}
\label{eq:X_true_bottleneck}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Strongest honest conclusion}

The longitudinal witness chain is now closed \emph{conditional on branch choice}:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:X_closed_A}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\ \lambda_c\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:X_closed_B}
\end{equation}
What is still open is only the actual microscopic determination of which branch the extracted coefficient point belongs to.

\subsection{Input from the full Hessian extraction}

\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu},

}
\label{eq:X_transverse_test_final}

So the true bottleneck is longitudinal only.

\subsection{Branch A test: constant-leading longitudinal coefficient}

\subsection{Operational decision tree}

The actual longitudinal branch test is now completely deterministic.

\paragraph{Step X1.}
Extract the invariant transport matrix \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) from the full background-dependent Hessian.

\item What remains open is not the reduced logic, but the actual microscopic coefficient extraction:

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

Thus the longitudinal witness chain is now closed \emph{conditional on branch choice}:

\section{Operator Checklist for Reading \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal M^\mu(0)$}{M(0)} and \texorpdfstring{$S_\xi$}{Sxi} from the Full Hessian}

\subsection{Goal}

The reduced graded \(2+2\) logic is already closed.
The only remaining microscopic task is to determine which longitudinal branch the actual complete TECT coefficient point lies on:
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\ \text{with}\ \lambda_c\neq 0.

So the only thing still needed is an executable extraction protocol from the full background-dependent Hessian.

\subsection{Starting operator}

Begin from the shell-/defect-adapted background-dependent Hessian
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=

+

\label{eq:Y_master}
\end{equation}
acting on tangent fluctuations
\[

with invariant decomposition

+

\end{equation}
This is exactly the local transport input already isolated in the notes. 

\subsection{Step Y1: isolate the transport kernel from the Hessian}

Compute the full quadratic operator and collect \emph{only} the terms with exactly one worldvolume derivative:
\[
\left[\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\right]_{1y}.
\]
Move all \(\xi\)-dependent coefficient matrices to the left of \(\partial_{y^\mu}\), project to \(Q_B(\xi)\), and write
\begin{equation}

\left[\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]\right]_{1y}
=
-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.

\label{eq:Y_step1}
\end{equation}
This is the only block from which \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\) and \(\lambda_c\) are to be read.

\subsection{Step Y2: divide out the universal odd factor}

Because the defect background is reflection-even and the transport kernel is reflection-odd, the leading local transport kernel factors through \(\theta'(\xi)\):
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))
=
\frac{V^\mu(\xi)}{\theta'(\xi)}
}
\label{eq:Y_step2}
\end{equation}
on the support where \(\theta'(\xi)\neq 0\), followed by smooth continuation to \(\theta=0\).

This is the precise operator meaning of the transport reduction
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

\subsection{Step Y3: read the constant-leading longitudinal coefficient}

Evaluate the invariant transport matrix at \(\theta=0\):
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(0).

Then project onto the shell-compatible longitudinal singlet direction:

\paragraph{Branch A criterion.}

+

+

then the actual coefficient point lies on Branch B and \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\) follows immediately.

\subsection{Step Y7: the complete decision tree}

The full longitudinal branch test is now a deterministic checklist:

Extract \(V^\mu(\xi)\) from the one-worldvolume-derivative block of the full Hessian.

\section{PROJECT: TECT --- Master Contents for Continuation (Route B Mainline)}

\section{Current Global Status}

The plain scalar Bragg-pair route is no longer the correct mainline.
Inside the currently known safe microscopic operator library, the scalar identity-channel Bragg block remains nonzero:
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{scalar}}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0,
\]
while the alignment term vanishes on the locked branch and canonical Class II only renormalizes the derivative witness sector.

Therefore the correct current mainline is the graded \(2+2\) bypass route.

\section{What is Already Closed}

\subsection{Minimal locked isotropic PDE no-go}

For the minimal locked isotropic complex-triplet Brazovskii PDE:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the linearized quartic term does not directly generate an enriched first-order Pauli-sector shell tensor;
\item the isotropic kinetic first-order shell term cancels exactly at the Brazovskii shell;
\item the locked zeroth-order cross-shell quartic projection vanishes.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the minimal locked isotropic PDE alone does not close the full witness problem.

\subsection{Scalar-channel no-go inside the current safe operator library}

The shell-relevant scalar constant sector can be parameterized by
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}
=
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
\]
The exact scalar cancellation condition is therefore
\[
2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2=0.
\]

For the currently known safe microscopic sectors:
\[
(c_0,c_1,c_2)_{\mathrm{scalar}}=(u,0,0),
\qquad
(c_0,c_1,c_2)_{\mathrm{align}}=(0,0,0),
\qquad
(c_0,c_1,c_2)_{\mathrm{Class\,II}}=(0,0,0)
\]
as a direct scalar-cancellation channel.

Therefore
\[
(c_0,c_1,c_2)_{\mathrm{known}}=(u,0,0),
\]
and so
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{known}}=4uA^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0
\qquad (u\neq 0).
\]

So the scalar identity-channel Bragg block cannot be removed inside the current safe operator library.

\subsection{Class II does not cancel the identity channel}

Every Class II constant pair-mixing contribution carries an explicit traceless internal Pauli generator:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
\in \mathrm{span}\{s_1,s_2,s_3\},
\]
hence it is orthogonal to the scalar identity channel
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Therefore Class II renormalizes derivative witnesses but does not remove the scalar Bragg obstruction.

\section{Why Route B is the Correct Mainline}

The correct mainline is the graded \(2+2\) reduced route:

\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\]
with grading-odd first-order projected symbol
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\]

Because the relevant principal operator is first-order and grading-odd,
\[
D_1(0)=0,
\]
so the dangerous scalar Bragg block is absent from the relevant principal infrared operator rather than cancelled inside it.

\section{Actual Local CP\(^2\) Projector-Defect Realization}

For a local projector defect background
\[
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\]
the physical tangent fluctuation lives in the rank-two complex bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp.
\]

Using a reflection-symmetric explicit representative
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
one has
\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1,
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger).
\]

Hence every leading local transport kernel linear in the defect gradient factors through
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

The low transverse bundle problem gives even/odd modes
\[
u_a^+(\xi),\qquad u_a^-(\xi),
\qquad a=1,2,
\]
and the mixed symbol is
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]

By parity,
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,V^\mu u_b^\pm\rangle=0,
\qquad
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle\neq 0
\]
generically, so the leading reduced operator is automatically grading-odd.

\section{Natural S2 Branch}

The natural local symmetry-compatible branch is S2:
\[
A_1(p)
=

+

So the transverse finite test is simply
\[
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).

\section{Exact Concrete Class II Primitive Branch}

\section{Exact full-Hessian extraction formula for the Route B longitudinal audit}

We now stop discussing the reduced theorem abstractly and derive the exact operator-level
extraction formulas needed for the actual microscopic branch decision.

The goal is to reduce the full microscopic TECT linearization to the finite coefficient audit
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},
\qquad
\lambda_c,
\qquad
\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\Lambda_O.
\]

\section{Microscopic starting point and honest scope}

Let the microscopic TECT field be the complex triplet
\[
\Psi(x,t)\in\mathbb C^3,
\]
with minimal local core
\[
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+Z\nabla^2\Psi
-Y\nabla^4\Psi
-g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi,
\]
possibly supplemented by alignment and/or Class II enriched terms.

We do \emph{not} assume that the minimal isotropic core alone is sufficient.
Indeed, that route is already known to be insufficient for generating the full shell witness sector.
The present task is different:
given the \emph{final complete microscopic operator}, derive the exact formulas that extract the
actual local transport matrix and decide whether the theory lands on Branch A or Branch B.

\section{Defect background and bundle-valued fluctuation sector}

Work in the frozen-amplitude projector regime
\[
\Psi_B(\xi)=\rho_0\,z_B(\xi),
\qquad
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\]
where the defect depends only on the normal coordinate \(\xi\), while the worldvolume coordinates
are denoted by
\[
y^\mu,
\qquad
\mu\in\{\parallel,1,2\}.
\]

The physical tangent fluctuation lives in the rank-two complex bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi):=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\Pi_Q(\xi)=\mathbf 1_3-P_B(\xi).
\]

Choose a local orthonormal frame
\[
e(\xi)=\bigl(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)\bigr)
\]
for \(Q_B(\xi)\), so that every tangent fluctuation can be written as
\[
\eta(\xi,y)=e(\xi)\,\chi(\xi,y),
\qquad
\chi(\xi,y)\in\mathbb C^2.
\]

\section{Full Hessian and exact first-order transport extraction}

Let
\[
\mathfrak E[\Psi]=0
\]
be the full microscopic TECT equation of motion.
Linearizing around \(\Psi_B\) gives the Hessian operator
\[
\mathbb H_B:=\left.\frac{\delta \mathfrak E}{\delta \Psi^\dagger}\right|_{\Psi_B}.
\]

Because the background is translationally invariant along the worldvolume coordinates \(y^\mu\),
the linearized operator admits the exact tangential derivative expansion
\begin{equation}
\mathbb H_B
=
\mathbb H_0(\xi,\partial_\xi)
+
\sum_{\mu}\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi,\partial_\xi)\,(-i\partial_{y^\mu})
+
O(\partial_y^2).
\label{eq:HB_expand}
\end{equation}
The exact first-order coefficient operators are therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_1^\mu
=
\left.
\frac{\partial \mathbb H_B}{\partial(-i\partial_{y^\mu})}
\right|_{\partial_y=0}.
}
\label{eq:H1mu_exact_def}
\end{equation}

Equation \eqref{eq:H1mu_exact_def} is the first key point:
to obtain the local transport kernel, one does \emph{not} guess it.
One differentiates the full Hessian with respect to the tangential derivative operator and then sets
all worldvolume derivatives to zero.

\section{Reduction to the shell-compatible local transport kernel}

After restriction to the tangent bundle and rewriting in the local frame \(e(\xi)\), define
\begin{equation}
\widetilde{\mathbb H}_1^\mu
:=
e^\dagger\,\Pi_Q\,\mathbb H_1^\mu\,\Pi_Q\,e.
\label{eq:H1mu_restricted}
\end{equation}

The shell-compatible local transport coefficient is the multiplication part of
\(\widetilde{\mathbb H}_1^\mu\) after all \(\partial_\xi\)-derivatives are pushed, by integration by parts,
onto the low-mode profiles.
Equivalently, the actual reduced mixed symbol is obtained directly from the even/odd low modes.

Let
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\]
be the even/odd low transverse modes.
Then the reduced first-order matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,\mathbb H_1^\mu u_b^-\rangle_\xi,
}
\label{eq:Mmu_exact_projection}
\end{equation}
and the reduced principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\label{eq:A1_exact_projection}
\end{equation}

Thus the microscopic audit is finite once the operators \(\mathbb H_1^\mu\) are known.

\section{Reflection symmetry and grading-oddness}

Assume a reflection-symmetric defect:
\[
P_B(-\xi)=P_B(\xi).
\]
Then
\[
\partial_\xi P_B(-\xi)=-\partial_\xi P_B(\xi).
\]
Hence every leading transport contribution that is linear in the defect gradient is odd under
\(\xi\mapsto -\xi\):
\begin{equation}
\mathbb H_1^\mu(-\xi)=-\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi).
\label{eq:H1mu_odd}
\end{equation}

Therefore the same-parity matrix elements vanish:
\[
\langle u_a^\pm,\mathbb H_1^\mu u_b^\pm\rangle_\xi=0,
\]
while the opposite-parity matrix elements
\[
\langle u_a^+,\mathbb H_1^\mu u_b^-\rangle_\xi
\]
are generically allowed.
This is exactly the microscopic origin of the grading-odd \(2+2\) reduced Dirac structure.

\section{Exact factorization through the defect gradient}

For the explicit local representative
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
one has
\[
\partial_\xi z_B=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\qquad
\partial_\xi P_B=\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger\bigr).
\]
Therefore every leading local transport term linear in the defect gradient must factor through
\(\theta'(\xi)\), and the restricted transport kernel takes the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:Vmu_factor_exact}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\in \mathrm{Herm}(2).
\]

Equivalently, on the open set where \(\theta'(\xi)\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi))
=
\theta'(\xi)^{-1}\,V^\mu(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Mmu_from_Vmu}
\end{equation}

This is the second key point:
the actual coefficient-point audit is the audit of the Hermitian \(2\times 2\) matrix-valued function
\(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\).

\section{Pauli decomposition and exact invariant coefficient formulas}

Because \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) is Hermitian,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\,\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta)\,\sigma_i.
\label{eq:Pauli_decomp_exact}
\end{equation}

Now impose the \(S2\)-compatible invariant decomposition:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:Minv_exact}
\end{equation}

Assuming the basis tensors are orthonormal in the standard way, the scalar profile functions are
extracted exactly by traces:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_0(\theta)
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\right],
}
\label{eq:h0_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\right],
}
\label{eq:hpar_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_E(\theta)
=
\frac12\,E_{\mu a}\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[\sigma_a\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\right],
}
\label{eq:hE_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_O(\theta)
=
\frac12\,J_{\mu a}\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[\sigma_a\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\right].
}
\label{eq:hO_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact Branch A coefficient}

Expand the longitudinal invariant near \(\theta=0\):
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(2)}\theta^2
+
O(\theta^4).
\label{eq:hpar_expand_exact}
\end{equation}

Then the exact constant-leading longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
h_\parallel(0)
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)\right].
}
\label{eq:Lambda0_exact}
\end{equation}

This is the exact Branch A test.
No further reduction is needed.

Likewise, the transverse constant-leading coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=h_E(0),
\qquad
\Lambda_O=h_O(0).
}
\label{eq:LambdaE_O_exact}
\end{equation}

\section{Reduced witness formulas}

Define the even-odd weight
\[
w(\xi):=f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
\]
Then the reduced witness coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,w(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:lambda_par_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,w(\xi)\,h_E(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,w(\xi)\,h_O(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:alpha_beta_exact}
\end{equation}

On Branch A,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_\theta
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(2)}I_{\theta^2\theta'}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\label{eq:lambda_par_branchA}
\end{equation}
where
\[
I_\theta:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta',
\qquad
I_{\theta^2\theta'}:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta^2\theta'.
\]

Therefore
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\]
immediately implies
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\]
provided \(I_\theta\neq 0\).

\section{Exact Branch B coefficient}

If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
we pass to the primitive longitudinal channel.

Define
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\label{eq:Txi_Sxi_exact}
\end{equation}

For the explicit representative,
\begin{equation}
S_\xi=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Sxi_explicit_exact}
\end{equation}

The primitive target kernel is
\begin{equation}
K^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}}(\xi):=\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
\label{eq:Kprim_def}
\end{equation}

Now define the weighted pairing
\begin{equation}
\langle A,B\rangle_w
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[A(\xi)^\dagger B(\xi)\right].
\label{eq:weighted_pairing}
\end{equation}

Then the exact primitive coefficient extracted from the actual transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
\frac{\langle K^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}},\,V_{\parallel,\mathrm{act},\mu}\rangle_w}
{\langle K^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}},\,K_{\mathrm{prim},\mu}\rangle_w}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_c_projection_exact}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{act}}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu
+
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{rem}}(\xi),
\qquad
\langle K^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}},V_{\parallel,\mathrm{rem},\mu}\rangle_w=0.
\label{eq:primitive_decomp_exact}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:Sxi_explicit_exact}, the projected primitive piece becomes
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{proj}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Vparallel_proj_exact}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced longitudinal witness on Branch B is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_par_branchB_exact}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact Branch B decision criterion is simply
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0.
\]

\section{Unified theorem-level extraction statement}

\begin{theorem}[Exact full-Hessian branch-decision formula]
Assume the full microscopic TECT Hessian around the projector defect admits the shell-compatible
local first-order reduction
\[
\mathbb H_B
=
\mathbb H_0
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
O(\partial_y^2),
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact Branch A coefficient is
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)\right];
\]

\item if \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\), the longitudinal witness survives on the \(I_\theta\)-branch;

\item if \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\), the exact Branch B coefficient is given by the weighted
projection formula \eqref{eq:lambda_c_projection_exact};

\item if \(\lambda_c\neq 0\), then
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0;
\]

\item if both \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\) and \(\lambda_c\) vanish, then the currently established
branch library is exhausted and higher even longitudinal channels must be audited explicitly.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Items (1)--(2) follow immediately from the invariant decomposition
\eqref{eq:Minv_exact} and the expansion \eqref{eq:hpar_expand_exact}.
Items (3)--(4) follow from the orthogonal projection of the actual longitudinal transport onto the
primitive target kernel \(K^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}}\), together with
\eqref{eq:Sxi_explicit_exact}.
Item (5) is just the statement that no nonzero longitudinal seed remains inside the currently
established two-branch library.
\end{proof}

\section{What this does and does not close}

This calculation closes the \emph{extraction formalism} completely.

What is now fully fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item how to obtain \(\mathbb H_1^\mu\) from the full Hessian;
\item how to pass from \(\mathbb H_1^\mu\) to the local transport matrix \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\);
\item how to compute the Branch A scalar \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\);
\item how to compute the Branch B scalar \(\lambda_c\);
\item how to reconstruct the reduced witnesses \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\).
\end{enumerate}

What is still not yet numerically or symbolically completed is only this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{insert the final complete microscopic TECT operator and perform the term-by-term Hessian audit.}
}
\]

So the frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is a finite, explicit coefficient extraction problem.

\section{Final Summary: exact Route B extraction formula}

Let
\[
\mathbb H_B
=
\mathbb H_0
+
\mathbb H_1^\mu(-i\partial_{y^\mu})
+
O(\partial_y^2)
\]
be the full microscopic Hessian around the projector defect background.

The exact first-order transport operator is
\[
\mathbb H_1^\mu
=
\left.
\frac{\partial \mathbb H_B}{\partial(-i\partial_{y^\mu})}
\right|_{\partial_y=0}.
\]

After restriction to the rank-two tangent bundle and local low-mode reduction,
the transport kernel has the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\in\mathrm{Herm}(2).
\]

Its invariant decomposition is
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Therefore the exact Branch A coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\left[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)\right].
}
\]

If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\]
the longitudinal witness survives immediately on the \(I_\theta\)-branch.

If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
define
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
K^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}}=\theta' S_\xi n^\mu.
\]
Then the exact primitive coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
\frac{\langle K^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}},\,V_{\parallel,\mathrm{act},\mu}\rangle_w}
{\langle K^\mu_{\mathrm{prim}},\,K_{\mathrm{prim},\mu}\rangle_w}.
}
\]

For the explicit defect representative,
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'^2\sigma_3,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

Thus the exact two-branch decision protocol is:
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0,
\qquad
\text{if not, } \lambda_c\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\]

What remains open is no longer the logical structure of the audit, but only the explicit
term-by-term insertion of the final complete microscopic TECT operator into this extraction formula.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Term-by-term operator audit for the actual Route B mainline}

We now freeze the no-loop rule and perform the actual source decomposition of the strongest
currently explicit microscopic branch.

The honest starting point is not the unknown final complete TECT action in full generality,
but the strongest explicit branch presently constructed:
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:OA_starting_branch}
\end{equation}

The shell-/defect-adapted quadratic operator is organized as
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:OA_master_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
V^\mu_{\mathrm{grad}}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{ani}}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi).
\label{eq:OA_V_split}
\end{equation}
The potential sector contributes only to \(H_B\) and does not enter \(V^\mu\).

\section{Sector-by-sector status}

\subsection{Minimal isotropic core}

For the isotropic Brazovskii bare kernel,
\begin{equation}
h_0(q)=r_0+Z|q|^2+Y|q|^4,
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)=2\bigl(Z+2Y|q|^2\bigr)q_i.
\end{equation}
At the Brazovskii shell,
\begin{equation}
|q|=q_*,
\qquad
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y},
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)\big|_{|q|=q_*}=0.
\label{eq:OA_bare_shell_cancel}
\end{equation}
Therefore the minimal isotropic first-order shell transport vanishes on-shell.

So the minimal isotropic core does not by itself generate a nonzero constant-leading
longitudinal coefficient \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\).

\subsection{Alignment sector}

On the locked branch,
\begin{equation}
\Psi=z\,\phi,
\qquad
P=zz^\dagger=\mathrm{const},
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\partial_iP=0.
\end{equation}
Hence the refined alignment term vanishes identically on the locked sector and contributes neither
to the scalar Bragg cancellation nor to the odd first-order transport kernel:
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{align}}(\xi)=0.
\label{eq:OA_align_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Projector / gauge-fixing sector}

Because the physical tangent fluctuations live in the moving bundle
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb Cz_B(\xi))^\perp,
\]
we must write
\[
\eta(\xi,y)=\eta^a(\xi,y)e_a(\xi).
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi\eta
=
(\partial_\xi\eta^a)e_a+\eta^a\partial_\xi e_a,
\end{equation}
so bundle-connection terms are unavoidable.

Therefore the projector/gauge-fixing sector contributes
\begin{equation}
\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}
\leadsto
H_B^{(\mathrm{proj})}
\oplus
V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}(\xi)
\oplus
W^{\mu\nu}_{\mathrm{proj}}(\xi).
\label{eq:OA_proj_contrib}
\end{equation}

This is the main currently available candidate for a genuine Branch A source,
namely for a nonzero constant-leading coefficient in the invariant component
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(2)}\theta^2
+
O(\theta^4).
\]

\subsection{Mediator / Class II sector}

Inside each Bloch fiber, the heavy mediator is eliminated by the Schur complement:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\mathcal C(k)\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\,\mathcal C(k)^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal C(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\label{eq:OA_Heff_exact}
\end{equation}
In the heavy-mass expansion,
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
\label{eq:OA_Heff_leading}
\end{equation}

After shell projection,
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
+
O(M_X^{-4}),
\label{eq:OA_Ki_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\label{eq:OA_Ki_II}
\end{equation}

Thus the mediator sector is the strongest explicit currently calculable source of the
nontrivial first-order shell tensor.

\section{What is already decided for the longitudinal branch}

The total constant-leading longitudinal coefficient decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_{\parallel,\Psi\Psi}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{ani}}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{proj}}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{med}}^{(0)}.
\label{eq:OA_Lambda_split}
\end{equation}

At the current explicit level, the following are already fixed:

\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{\parallel,\min}^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{align}}^{(0)}=0.
\label{eq:OA_known_zero}
\end{equation}

Moreover, in the exact concrete Class II-compatible local branch,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{med}}^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\label{eq:OA_ClassII_branchB}
\end{equation}

Therefore, within the strongest explicit currently constructed branch,
the concrete mediator realization is Branch B, not Branch A.

\section{Immediate consequence}

Hence the actual remaining candidate sources for
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\]
are reduced to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the projector/gauge-fixing transport sector;
\item any still-unspecified background-dependent anisotropic pieces inside \(L_\Psi^{\mathrm{ref}}\).
\end{enumerate}

By contrast, if one stays inside the exact currently constructed concrete Class II branch,
the longitudinal audit should proceed directly through
\begin{equation}
\lambda_c
\stackrel{?}{\neq}0
\end{equation}
rather than through
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\end{equation}

\section{Actual next calculation}

Thus the next explicit computation is not an abstract theorem.
It is the operator derivative audit:
\begin{equation}
\left[\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{grad}}\right]_{1y},
\qquad
\left[\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{ani}}\right]_{1y},
\qquad
\left[\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{gf/proj}}\right]_{1y},
\qquad
\left[\delta^2\Gamma_{\mathrm{med}}\right]_{1y},
\end{equation}
followed by
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\end{equation}

If one works with the explicit Bloch branch, the practical order is:
\begin{equation}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k),\ \mathcal J(k),\ \mathcal K(k)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
K_i
\;\Longrightarrow\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\Longrightarrow\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\end{equation}

This is now the unique correct mainline.

\section{Final Summary}

The current operator-level status is:

\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
H_B(\xi)
-
iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots,
\qquad
V^\mu
=
V^\mu_{\mathrm{grad}}
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{ani}}
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}.
\end{equation}

The potential sector does not contribute to \(V^\mu\).

At the currently explicit level:

\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\min}\ \text{does not generate on-shell isotropic first-order shell transport,}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{align}}=0
\quad
\text{on the locked branch,}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}
\ \text{and}\ 
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}
\ \text{are the only nontrivial source sectors for the odd transport kernel.}
\end{equation}

For the strongest explicit periodic microscopic branch,
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi],
\end{equation}
the Bloch-fiber elimination of the heavy mediator gives
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\mathcal C(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\mathcal C(k)^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal C(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k),
\end{equation}
and the shell-linear coefficient is
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
\end{equation}

The total constant-leading longitudinal coefficient satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\Lambda_{\parallel,\Psi\Psi}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{ani}}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{proj}}^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{med}}^{(0)}.
\end{equation}

What is already fixed is:
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{\parallel,\min}^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{align}}^{(0)}=0.
\end{equation}

Moreover, in the exact currently constructed concrete Class II-compatible branch,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{\parallel,\mathrm{med}}^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit currently constructed mediator branch is Branch B.

Hence the only remaining candidate sources for a genuine Branch A realization are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{proj}}
\quad\text{and/or}\quad
\text{still-unspecified background-dependent anisotropic pieces in }L_\Psi^{\mathrm{ref}}.
}
\end{equation}

So the actual next computation is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k),\ \mathcal J(k),\ \mathcal K(k)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
K_i
\;\Longrightarrow\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\Longrightarrow\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Finite harmonic-matrix template for the full periodic Route B audit}

\section{Goal}

The remaining microscopic task is no longer a conceptual theorem.
It is the explicit construction of the Bloch-harmonic matrix of the refined locked
TECT branch with the Class II mediator, followed by shell projection and first-derivative extraction.

The correct no-loop sequence is
\[
\text{full periodic microscopic operator}
\;\to\;
\text{Bloch fiber}
\;\to\;
\text{shell truncation}
\;\to\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\to\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

We now write the exact finite-dimensional template needed for that computation.

\section{Folded Bragg convention and BCC background}

We work in the folded Bragg convention
\begin{equation}
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
\label{eq:folded_Bragg_conv}
\end{equation}

Choose the first BCC reciprocal shell
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\,
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\,
(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\},
\qquad
|\mathcal S_{12}|=12,
\label{eq:S12_BCC}
\end{equation}
and the locked periodic background
\begin{equation}
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\label{eq:locked_periodic_background}
\end{equation}

Let
\begin{equation}
u_0=z_0,
\qquad
u_1,u_2\in Q_{z_0},
\qquad
u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs},
\qquad
\mathbb C^3=\mathbb Cz_0\oplus Q_{z_0},
\label{eq:internal_basis_locked}
\end{equation}
be the internal basis adapted to the locked decomposition.

\section{Bloch-harmonic expansion of the fluctuations}

For the triplet fluctuation, write
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\mathcal G}\sum_{r=0}^2
c_{G,r}\,u_r\,e^{iG\cdot x},
\label{eq:deltaPsi_Bloch}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal G\) is the reciprocal lattice generated by the periodic BCC background.

For the Class II mediator,
\begin{equation}
\delta X_{i}^{a}(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\mathcal G}
x_{G,i,a}\,e^{iG\cdot x}.
\label{eq:deltaX_Bloch}
\end{equation}

Thus the Bloch fiber acts on the coefficient vector
\begin{equation}
\mathbf v(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
c_{G,r} \\
x_{G,i,a}
\end{pmatrix}_{G\in\mathcal G},
\label{eq:Bloch_vector}
\end{equation}
and has the block form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Bloch_block_matrix}
\end{equation}

\section{Triplet block \(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\)}

\subsection{Universal structure}

The refined locked triplet block always splits as
\begin{equation}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{bare}}(k)
+
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{per}}(k),
\label{eq:Hpsipsi_split}
\end{equation}
where the bare translationally invariant part is diagonal in reciprocal harmonics and the periodic background produces convolution terms.

In the adapted basis \((G,r)\), write
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
\delta_{G,G'}\,h^{(0)}_{rs}(k+G)
+
U^{rs}_{G-G'}
+
A^{rs}_{G,G'}(k).
\label{eq:Hpsipsi_general_template}
\end{equation}

Here:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(h^{(0)}_{rs}(q)\) is the bare triplet symbol coming from the refined locked kinetic part;
\item \(U^{rs}_{G-G'}\) is the periodic Hessian generated by the background \(\Psi_0\);
\item \(A^{rs}_{G,G'}(k)\) collects explicitly \(k\)-dependent refined derivative/anisotropic terms.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Minimal isotropic benchmark}

For the minimal isotropic triplet Brazovskii core,
\begin{equation}
h^{(0)}_{rs}(q)=h_0(q)\delta_{rs},
\qquad
h_0(q)=r_*+K\left(|q|^2-q_*^2\right)^2,
\label{eq:min_bare_h0}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)=4K\left(|q|^2-q_*^2\right)q_i.
\label{eq:dh0_dq}
\end{equation}
Hence on the shell \(|q|=q_*\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)\big|_{|q|=q_*}=0.
}
\label{eq:shell_derivative_zero}
\end{equation}

This is the operator-level reason why the bare isotropic scalar part is not the load-bearing source for the first-order shell witness.

\section{Mediator block \(H_{XX}(k)\)}

If the Class II mediator is purely heavy and algebraic at leading order, then
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{XX}(k)\bigr)_{(G,i,a),(G',j,b)}
=
M_X^2\,\delta_{G,G'}\delta_{ij}\delta^{ab}
+
D^{ab}_{ij}(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}
+
V^{ab}_{ij;G-G'},
\label{eq:HXX_general}
\end{equation}
where the last two terms are optional refinements.

At the strict minimal heavy-mediator level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\,\mathbf 1_X.
}
\label{eq:HXX_minimal}
\end{equation}

If gradient or periodic corrections of the mediator are present, they can be included in
\(D_{ij}^{ab}\) and \(V_{ij;G-G'}^{ab}\), but they do not change the Schur-complement logic below.

\section{Mixed block \(H_{\Psi X}(k)\)}

The Class II UV action is
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:Lmic_branch_repeat}
\end{equation}

Therefore the mixed fiber block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\,\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\,\mathcal K(k),
}
\label{eq:HpsiX_C}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C(k):=\alpha_X\,\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\,\mathcal K(k).
\label{eq:Ck_def}
\end{equation}

The harmonic matrix elements are obtained by unit-cell projection:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k)
=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
e^{-i(k+G)\cdot x}\,
u_r^\dagger
\left(
\frac{\delta J_i^a}{\delta\Psi}
\right)_{\Psi_0}
e^{i(k+G')\cdot x},
\label{eq:J_harmonic_matrix}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\mathcal K_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k)
=
\frac{1}{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\,
e^{-i(k+G)\cdot x}\,
u_r^\dagger
\left(
\frac{\delta K_i^a}{\delta\Psi}
\right)_{\Psi_0,P_0}
e^{i(k+G')\cdot x}.
\label{eq:K_harmonic_matrix}
\end{equation}

These matrices are finite after truncation to a finite harmonic set.

\section{Mediator elimination and effective triplet Bloch operator}

Eliminating the heavy mediator by the Schur complement gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\,H_{X\Psi}(k).
}
\label{eq:Heff_exact}
\end{equation}

With the shorthand \(\mathcal C(k)=H_{\Psi X}(k)\), this is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\mathcal C(k)\,H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\,\mathcal C(k)^\dagger.
\label{eq:Heff_C}
\end{equation}

At strict leading order in the heavy-mass expansion,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
}
\label{eq:Heff_heavy}
\end{equation}

\section{Near-Bragg shell truncation}

At the folded Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\), the two near-degenerate harmonics are
\begin{equation}
|+\!,a\rangle \equiv |G=0,a\rangle,
\qquad
|-\!,a\rangle \equiv |G=-G_*,a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:shell_basis_folded}
\end{equation}
where \(a=1,2\) spans the internal tangent doublet.

Thus the shell space is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal V_*
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+\!,1\rangle,|+\!,2\rangle,|-\!,1\rangle,|-\!,2\rangle\},
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C\mathcal V_*=4.
\label{eq:Vstar_def}
\end{equation}

Let \(\Pi_{S_*}\) denote the harmonic projector onto this four-dimensional near-Bragg shell sector.
Then the shell-truncated operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:Hshell_def}
\end{equation}

\section{Definition of the first-derivative matrices \(K_i\)}

Expand \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\) around \(p=0\):
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)
+
p_i K_i
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hshell_expand}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i
=
\left.
\frac{\partial H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)}{\partial p_i}
\right|_{p=0}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_def}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:Heff_heavy},
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
+
O(M_X^{-4}),
\label{eq:Ki_split_final}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
}
\label{eq:Ki_PsiPsi}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_ClassII}
\end{equation}

This is the exact finite harmonic matrix formula required by the full Route B audit.

\section{What vanishes immediately and what can actually survive}

\subsection{Bare isotropic scalar diagonal part}

If
\[
H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{bare}}(k)
=
\delta_{G,G'}\,h_0(k+G)\,\mathbf 1_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
then by \eqref{eq:shell_derivative_zero},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\Psi\Psi}^{\mathrm{bare}}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}
=0.
}
\label{eq:bare_scalar_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Purely scalar periodic potential part}

If \(U^{rs}_{G-G'}\) is \(k\)-independent, then
\begin{equation}
\partial_{k_i}U^{rs}_{G-G'}=0,
\label{eq:periodic_potential_k_indep}
\end{equation}
hence such a purely scalar background-convolution piece contributes to \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0)\), but not to \(K_i\).

Therefore the genuinely load-bearing sources for \(K_i\) must come from:

\begin{enumerate}
\item explicitly \(k\)-dependent refined internal/anisotropic pieces \(A^{rs}_{G,G'}(k)\) inside \(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\),
\item the mediator correction \(K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final coefficient extraction}

Let \(P_*\) be the projector onto the isolated \(2\times 2\) internal shell block after the shell-space identification.
Then the actual microscopic coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal V_*}
\!\left[
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_iK_i)P_*
\right],
}
\label{eq:lambda_extract_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal V_*}
\!\left[
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*
+
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*
\right],
}
\label{eq:alpha_extract_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal V_*}
\!\left[
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*
-
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*
\right].
}
\label{eq:beta_extract_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the full operator-construction program is now reduced to a finite matrix computation.

\section{Exact logical consequence}

The true remaining microscopic question is no longer
``what kind of mechanism might work?''
It is only this finite calculation:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k),\quad
\mathcal J(k),\quad
\mathcal K(k)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\;\Longrightarrow\;
K_i
\;\Longrightarrow\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:finite_matrix_pipeline}
\end{equation}

In particular, the present template shows that:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the bare isotropic scalar piece is not the load-bearing source of \(K_i\);
\item a purely \(k\)-independent scalar periodic potential is not the load-bearing source of \(K_i\);
\item the actual microscopic load-bearing sectors are the refined \(k\)-dependent internal triplet block and the Class II Schur-complement term.
\end{enumerate}

So the problem is now genuinely finite and explicit.

\section{Term-by-term survival test for \texorpdfstring{$K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}$}{Ki(PsiPsi)}}

\section{Goal}

We now isolate, inside the triplet Bloch block
\[
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k),
\]
which terms can actually contribute to
\[
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.

This is the exact next microscopic question, because the correct no-loop Route B program is already fixed as
\[
\text{periodic refined locked microscopic operator}
\;\to\;
\text{Bloch fiber}
\;\to\;
\text{shell truncation}
\;\to\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\to\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).

\section{Canonical decomposition of the triplet Bloch block}

Write the triplet Bloch block as
\begin{equation}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
=
H_{\mathrm{bare}}(k)
+
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}
+
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k),
\label{eq:Hpsipsi_decomp}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(H_{\mathrm{bare}}(k)\) is the translation-invariant bare symbol;
\item \(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}\) is the \(k\)-independent periodic Hessian induced by the background;
\item \(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)\) is the genuinely refined \(k\)-dependent internal/anisotropic part.
\end{enumerate}

Accordingly,
\begin{equation}
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}
+
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}},
\label{eq:Ki_PsiPsi_split}
\end{equation}
with
\[
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{bare}}(k)
\right]_{k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
\]
\[
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}
\right]_{k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
\]
\[
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

\section{Vanishing of the bare isotropic contribution}

For the minimal isotropic Brazovskii symbol,
\begin{equation}
h_0(q)=r_*+K\bigl(|q|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2,
\label{eq:h0_braz}
\end{equation}
one has
\begin{equation}
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)
=
4K\bigl(|q|^2-q_*^2\bigr)q_i.
\label{eq:dh0_general}
\end{equation}
At the selected shell,
\begin{equation}
|q|=q_*,
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)\big|_{|q|=q_*}=0.
}
\label{eq:dh0_shell_zero}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the slow-envelope operator language,
the first-order shell transport coefficient of
\[
Z\nabla^2-Y\nabla^4
\]
is proportional to
\[
2i(Z+2Yq_*^2)G\cdot\nabla,
\]
which vanishes exactly at
\[
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y}.
\]

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}=0.
}
\label{eq:Ki_bare_zero}
\end{equation}

This is not approximate.
It is an exact on-shell cancellation.

\section{Vanishing of the purely scalar periodic convolution contribution}

Now consider the background-induced periodic Hessian contribution
\[
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)},
\]
coming from scalar periodic terms such as the quartic Hessian background potential.
In the reciprocal-harmonic basis it has the generic form
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
U^{rs}_{G-G'}.
\label{eq:Hper0_template}
\end{equation}

If the periodic background term is scalar in the internal doublet and contains no explicit Bloch momentum dependence, then
\begin{equation}
\partial_{k_i}U^{rs}_{G-G'}=0.
\label{eq:dUdk_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}=0.
}
\label{eq:Ki_per0_zero}
\end{equation}

So a purely \(k\)-independent scalar periodic convolution can affect
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0),
\]
for example the constant Bragg block, but it cannot by itself generate the first-order shell derivative matrix \(K_i\).

\section{What can survive: refined internal / anisotropic pieces}

The only triplet-sector source that can survive inside \(K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}\) is therefore the genuinely \(k\)-dependent refined block
\[
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k).
\]

Write its harmonic matrix elements as
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
A^{rs}_{G,G'}(k).
\label{eq:A_GGprime_rs}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}A^{rs}_{G,G'}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_perint_formula}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full triplet contribution reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:Ki_PsiPsi_final_reduced}
\end{equation}

\section{Necessary condition for Branch A from the triplet sector}

Recall that Branch A requires a nonzero constant-leading longitudinal coefficient
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0.
\]
Inside the triplet sector, this can only happen if
\[
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\]
contains a shell-compatible \(k\)-linear term whose shell projection produces a \(\sigma_3\)-type longitudinal block.

In other words, a necessary condition for Branch A coming from the triplet block is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_\parallel}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}
\not\propto 0
}
\label{eq:BranchA_triplet_necessary}
\end{equation}
and, more specifically, its projected traceless internal part must have a nonzero \(\sigma_3\) component.

If this fails, then the triplet block does not realize Branch A, and one must pass either to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the projector/gauge-fixing transport sector, or
\item the Class II primitive longitudinal branch.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Term-by-term audit criterion}

The practical finite audit is therefore:

\begin{equation}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
=
\underbrace{H_{\mathrm{bare}}(k)}_{\text{dead in }K_i}
+
\underbrace{H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}}_{\text{dead in }K_i}
+
\underbrace{H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)}_{\text{only triplet-sector live source}}.
\label{eq:triplet_audit_table}
\end{equation}

Hence the triplet-sector Route B computation is reduced to the finite question:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{What are the explicit }k\text{-linear harmonic matrix elements of }
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\text{ at }k=k_*?
}
\label{eq:triplet_remaining_question}
\end{equation}

This is now the exact next subtask.

\section{Consequence for the full operator audit}

Combining the triplet result with the mediator Schur-complement formula,
the full first-derivative shell matrix satisfies
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
\underbrace{K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}}_{\text{triplet refined source}}
+
\underbrace{K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}}_{\text{Class II Schur source}}
+
O(M_X^{-4}).
\label{eq:Ki_two_live_sources}
\end{equation}

Thus the load-bearing microscopic sources are now sharply localized:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(I) refined }k\text{-dependent internal/anisotropic triplet block,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(II) Class II mediator Schur complement.}
}
\end{equation}

No other term in the currently explicit minimal/refined decomposition can produce
the required first-order shell witness by itself.

\section{Honest conclusion}

At this stage, the strongest honest statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}=0,
\qquad
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}=0,
}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the remaining triplet-sector microscopic frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit extraction of the \(k\)-linear refined internal harmonic block
\[
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\]
at the folded Bragg point \(k_*\).

\section{Final Summary}

The triplet Bloch block decomposes as
\[
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
=
H_{\mathrm{bare}}(k)
+
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)}
+
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k).
\]

Accordingly,
\[
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
\Pi_{S_*}\left[\partial_{k_i}H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\right]_{k_*}\Pi_{S_*}
=
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}
+
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}.
\]

For the minimal isotropic Brazovskii symbol,
\[
h_0(q)=r_*+K(|q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\]
one has
\[
\partial_{q_i}h_0(q)\big|_{|q|=q_*}=0,
\]
equivalently the slow-envelope first-order coefficient
\[
2i(Z+2Yq_*^2)G\cdot\nabla
\]
vanishes exactly at
\[
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y}.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}=0.
}
\]

If the periodic background Hessian is \(k\)-independent,
\[
(H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(0)})_{(G,r),(G',s)}=U^{rs}_{G-G'},
\qquad
\partial_{k_i}U^{rs}_{G-G'}=0,
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}=0.
}
\]

Therefore the only triplet-sector contribution that can survive in \(K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}\) is the refined \(k\)-dependent internal/anisotropic block:
\[
\boxed{
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\]

Thus the full first-derivative shell matrix is reduced to
\[
\boxed{
K_i
=
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
+
O(M_X^{-4}),
}
\]
where the only load-bearing microscopic sources are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(I) refined }k\text{-dependent internal/anisotropic triplet block,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(II) Class II mediator Schur complement.}
}
\]

Hence the next exact microscopic subtask is to write the explicit harmonic matrix elements of
\[
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\]
and extract their \(k\)-linear shell projection at \(k=k_*\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal \(k\)-linear harmonic tensor form of the refined internal block}

\section{Goal}

We now determine the minimal shell-compatible \(k\)-linear structure of the refined internal/anisotropic Bloch block
\[
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\]
that can generate the three reduced S2 witness coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta.
\]

The previous audit already established that
\[
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
\]
because both the bare isotropic part and the \(k\)-independent scalar periodic convolution are dead in the first shell derivative.

So the remaining triplet-sector question is purely finite:
what is the minimal \(k\)-linear tensor form of
\[
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\]
at the folded Bragg point \(k_*\)?

\section{Shell-adapted decomposition}

Fix the adapted frame
\[
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n+p_1e_1+p_2e_2,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]

After projection to the isolated shell doublet block \(H_*\), every Hermitian \(2\times2\) first-order symbol has a unique Pauli decomposition
\begin{equation}
P_*H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k_*+p)P_*
=
\mathcal E_0
+
p_i\Bigl(
u_i\,\mathbf 1_2
+
v_i^a\,\sigma_a
\Bigr)
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:general_projected_klinear}
\end{equation}
with real coefficients \(u_i,v_i^a\).

The scalar term \(u_i\mathbf 1_2\) is irrelevant for the local Weyl data.
Therefore the actual reduced transport content is carried by
\begin{equation}
p_i\,v_i^a\,\sigma_a.
\label{eq:traceless_klinear}
\end{equation}

\section{S2 symmetry reduction}

The worldvolume momentum representation splits as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\},
\]
while the traceless internal fiber splits as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]

Thus the most general symmetry-compatible intertwiner is exactly the natural S2 form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:S2_minimal_target_again}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the shell-derivative matrices must satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*(\hat n_iK_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
=
\lambda_\parallel\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:long_proj_target}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*(e_{1i}K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
=
\alpha\,\sigma_1-\beta\,\sigma_2,
}
\label{eq:e1_proj_target}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*(e_{2i}K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
=
\beta\,\sigma_1+\alpha\,\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:e2_proj_target}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal \(k\)-linear harmonic tensor ansatz}

The unique minimal shell-compatible ansatz for the refined internal block is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
=
H_0
+
(k-k_*)_i\,\mathcal N_i^a\,s^a
+
O(|k-k_*|^2),
}
\label{eq:minimal_internal_ansatz}
\end{equation}
where \(s^a\) denotes the internal Pauli basis before shell projection and
\(\mathcal N_i^a\) is a finite harmonic operator on the shell carrier space.

After shell projection, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a
:=
P_*\mathcal N_i^aP_*.
}
\label{eq:Ntilde_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
P_*H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k_*+p)P_*
=
P_*H_0P_*
+
p_i\,\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a\,\sigma_a
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:projected_minimal_ansatz}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
=
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a\,\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:Ki_from_Ntilde}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal shell tensor basis}

To realize the S2 target exactly, \(\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a\) must lie in the three-dimensional shell-adapted tensor span
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a
=
\lambda_\parallel\,\hat n_i\,\delta^{a3}
+
\alpha\,(e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2})
+
\beta\,(-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}).
}
\label{eq:minimal_shell_tensor_basis}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_\parallel^a
=
\lambda_\parallel\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_{1}^a
=
\alpha\,\delta^{a1}-\beta\,\delta^{a2},
\qquad
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_{2}^a
=
\beta\,\delta^{a1}+\alpha\,\delta^{a2}.
\label{eq:N_components_explicit}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:minimal_shell_tensor_basis} into \eqref{eq:Ki_from_Ntilde} gives
\begin{equation}
p_iK_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:S2_recovered_exactly}
\end{equation}
which is exactly the required reduced symbol.

\section{Microscopic interpretation of the three channels}

The ansatz \eqref{eq:minimal_shell_tensor_basis} separates the three physically distinct microscopic channels.

\subsection{Longitudinal singlet channel}

The coefficient \(\lambda_\parallel\) multiplies
\[
\hat n_i\,\sigma_3.
\]
This is the unique shell singlet-to-singlet intertwiner and therefore the only possible first-order longitudinal source inside the S2 branch.

In the local projector-defect geometry, the canonical microscopic realization of this channel is the commutator-square seed
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3,
\label{eq:commsq_sigma3_repeat}
\end{equation}
which leads to the primitive transport seed
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:primitive_long_seed_repeat}
\end{equation}

Therefore a triplet-sector Branch A realization requires that the projected \(k\)-linear refined block itself already produces a nonzero coefficient of \(\hat n_i\sigma_3\).
If not, the theory must fall back to the primitive Branch B channel.

\subsection{Transverse even doublet channel}

The coefficient \(\alpha\) multiplies
\[
e_{1i}\sigma_1+e_{2i}\sigma_2.
\]
This is the even transverse intertwiner and is the minimal source of the term
\[
p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2.
\]

\subsection{Transverse odd doublet channel}

The coefficient \(\beta\) multiplies
\[
-e_{1i}\sigma_2+e_{2i}\sigma_1.
\]
This is the odd transverse intertwiner and is the minimal source of the term
\[
-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2.
\]

\section{Direct projector formulas}

Because the projected first-order symbol is already in the Pauli basis, the coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\Bigl(
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_iK_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:lambda_from_internalblock}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac14\sum_{a=1}^2
\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\Bigl(
\sigma_a\,P_*(e_{a i}K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:alpha_from_internalblock}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac14\left[
\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\Bigl(
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{1i}K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
\Bigr)
-
\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\Bigl(
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{2i}K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
\Bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:beta_from_internalblock}
\end{equation}

\section{Necessary and sufficient tensor criterion}

Inside the triplet refined block, the S2 witnesses survive iff the projected \(k\)-linear tensor
\[
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a
\]
has nonzero overlap with the three shell target tensors
\[
\hat n_i\delta^{a3},
\qquad
e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2},
\qquad
-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}.
\]

Equivalently:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\iff
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a\not\perp \hat n_i\delta^{a3},
}
\label{eq:lambda_overlap_criterion}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\iff
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a\not\perp
\mathrm{span}\!\left\{
e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2},
\,-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:transverse_overlap_criterion}
\end{equation}

Thus the triplet-sector audit is reduced to one finite tensor-overlap question:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the actual }k\text{-linear refined internal block contain the shell tensor basis }
\{\hat n_i\delta^{a3},\,e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2},\,-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}\}?
}
\label{eq:final_triplet_tensor_question}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest conclusion}

At this stage the triplet refined block is no longer mysterious.

Its minimal shell-compatible \(k\)-linear form is exactly the three-parameter tensor ansatz
\eqref{eq:minimal_shell_tensor_basis}, and nothing else is needed at first order.

Therefore the only remaining microscopic question is not
whether some abstract S2 symbol might exist,
but whether the actual harmonic matrix elements of the final refined TECT linearization
produce nonzero coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
in that explicit shell tensor basis.

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining triplet-sector contribution to the first shell derivative is
\[
K_i^{(\Psi\Psi)}
=
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
=
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

After projection to the isolated shell doublet block \(H_*\), every Hermitian \(k\)-linear term has the form
\[
P_*H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k_*+p)P_*
=
\mathcal E_0
+
p_i\bigl(u_i\mathbf 1_2+v_i^a\sigma_a\bigr)
+
O(|p|^2).
\]
The scalar piece \(u_i\mathbf 1_2\) is irrelevant for the local Weyl data.

By S2 symmetry, the unique minimal shell-compatible traceless \(k\)-linear form is
\[
\boxed{
p_iK_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

Equivalently, the projected shell tensor must be
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde{\mathcal N}_i^a
=
\lambda_\parallel\,\hat n_i\,\delta^{a3}
+
\alpha\,(e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2})
+
\beta\,(-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}).
}
\]

Thus the three first-order microscopic channels are:

\[
\hat n_i\sigma_3
\quad\leftrightarrow\quad
\text{longitudinal singlet,}
\]
\[
e_{1i}\sigma_1+e_{2i}\sigma_2
\quad\leftrightarrow\quad
\text{transverse even doublet,}
\]
\[
-e_{1i}\sigma_2+e_{2i}\sigma_1
\quad\leftrightarrow\quad
\text{transverse odd doublet.}
\]

The coefficients are extracted by the projector traces
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(
\sigma_3P_*(\hat n_iK_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
\bigr),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac14\sum_{a=1}^2
\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(
\sigma_aP_*(e_{a i}K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
\bigr),
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac14\left[
\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(
\sigma_2P_*(e_{1i}K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
\bigr)
-
\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(
\sigma_1P_*(e_{2i}K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}})P_*
\bigr)
\right].
\]

Hence the remaining triplet-sector microscopic audit is finite and explicit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{compute the actual }k\text{-linear harmonic coefficients of }
H_{\mathrm{per}}^{(\mathrm{int})}(k)
\text{ at }k=k_*
\text{ and test their overlap with the shell tensor basis }
\{\hat n_i\delta^{a3},\,e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2},\,-e_{1i}\delta^{a2}+e_{2i}\delta^{a1}\}.
}
\]
