\section{What is being done right now}

The current task is not yet the complete derivation of the final full PDE itself.

What is being done is the exact carrier audit of the future full PDE:
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi]
=
H_B
-
iV^\mu\partial_{y^\mu}
+
W^{\mu\nu}\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots
\]
with the goal of identifying which microscopic sectors actually contribute to
\[
K_i,\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\qquad
\lambda_c,\qquad
\alpha,\qquad
\beta.
\]

At the currently explicit level, the audit has established that
\[
K_i^{\mathrm{bare}}=0,
\qquad
K_i^{\mathrm{per},0}=0,
\]
so that the load-bearing sources are reduced to
\[
K_i
=
K_i^{\mathrm{per,int}}
+
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}.
\]

Therefore the present stage is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{not yet the full final PDE derivation,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{but the exact decomposition of which terms in the future full PDE can actually carry the Dirac witness.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Working Full PDE Fixing and Actual Forward Reduction}

We now stop waiting for a more complete future action and fix the strongest explicit microscopic branch as the working full PDE:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{work}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:Lwork_fixed}
\end{equation}

This is not claimed to be the final complete TECT action in full generality.
But it is the strongest explicit branch in which the full-PDE derivation can be pushed concretely.

\section{Immediate quadratic-order simplification}

Around the locked constant-projector background
\[
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger=\mathrm{const},
\]
the current refined projector sector is block diagonal at quadratic order:
\begin{equation}
\delta^2F_{\mathrm{ref}}
=
\delta^2F_\sigma+\delta^2F_\xi,
\qquad
J=0.
\label{eq:blockdiag_repeat}
\end{equation}

Therefore, at this order,
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^a=0
\end{equation}
from the direct projector channel.

Hence the projector sector is not a load-bearing source for the shell witness at the present order.

\section{Actual working Bloch linearization}

The genuine working full-PDE linearization is therefore the Bloch fiber Hessian on the fluctuation pair
\[
(\delta\Psi,\delta X),
\]
namely
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Bloch_working_block}
\end{equation}

Using the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=G_*/2,
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\]
the shell-projected effective operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*},
}
\label{eq:Hshell_working}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k).
}
\label{eq:Heff_working}
\end{equation}

\section{Actual carrier reduction}

At the present order, the surviving microscopic witness carriers are reduced to exactly two sources:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(I) refined internal \(k\)-dependence inside }H_{\Psi\Psi}(k),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(II) the Class II Schur-complement term }H_{\Psi X}H_{XX}^{-1}H_{X\Psi}.
}
\end{equation}

No separate projector-induced tree-level witness survives at this order.

\section{Actual next finite computation}

The first shell derivatives are
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0),
\end{equation}
and the reduced Weyl/Dirac coefficients are read from
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel = M_{3,\parallel},
\qquad
\alpha,\beta
\text{ are the coefficients of }
(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2),\ 
(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\end{equation}

Therefore the operator-construction phase is now genuinely fixed as the finite computation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k),\ H_{\Psi X}(k),\ H_{XX}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\to
K_i
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:actual_forward_pipeline}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Exact channel decomposition of the Class II Schur-complement contribution}

\section{Goal}

We now stop discussing the Class II sector abstractly and derive the exact shell-level channel decomposition of the Schur-complement contribution
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}.
\]

The purpose is to determine which of the three reduced S2 witness channels
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
are supplied automatically by the mediator sector, and in which leading-order branch they appear.

\section{Class II UV completion and effective quadratic operator}

The explicit Class II UV-completed branch is
\begin{equation}
S_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}[\Psi,P,\psi,X]
=
S_0[\Psi]
+
\int dt\,d^3x
\left[
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
\right].
\label{eq:C2_UV_repeat}
\end{equation}

Linearizing in Bloch momentum \(k\), the fiber Hessian has the block form
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\label{eq:C2_Bloch_blocks}
\end{equation}

After integrating out the heavy mediator \(X\), the effective triplet block is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k).
\label{eq:C2_Heff_repeat}
\end{equation}

At leading heavy-mass order,
\begin{equation}
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X+O(k,\text{periodic}),
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger
+
O(M_X^{-4}),
\qquad
\mathcal C(k):=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\label{eq:C2_Heff_heavy_repeat}
\end{equation}

\section{First shell derivative}

At the folded Bragg point \(k=k_*+p\), the shell-projected operator is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*},
\end{equation}
so the Class II contribution to the first shell derivative is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}
\bigl(
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k)
\bigr)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:C2_Ki_exact_start}
\end{equation}

At strict leading order in \(M_X^{-2}\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:C2_Ki_heavy_repeat}
\end{equation}

This is the exact microscopic carrier formula.

\section{Shell-adapted tensor reduction}

The shell witness theorem already fixes the only relevant microscopic carrier structure:
a first-order enriched tensor must carry simultaneously
\[
\text{one spatial index }i
\quad\text{and}\quad
\text{one internal reduced-shell index }a.
\]
Therefore, after shell projection, \(K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}\) can only contribute through an effective \((i,a)\)-tensor
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
\end{equation}
entering the shell operator in the standard form
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\label{eq:C2_Nij_target}
\end{equation}

By the already-closed axial/S2 classification, the minimal admissible family is
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^3=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:C2_axial_family}
\end{equation}

Thus the projected Class II correction must reduce to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
=
c_\parallel\,B_{\parallel\,ij}^a
+
c_I\,B_{I\,ij}^a
+
c_J\,B_{J\,ij}^a,
}
\label{eq:C2_seed_decomp}
\end{equation}
where the three shell seed tensors are exactly
\begin{equation}
B_{\parallel\,ij}^a=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:C2_Bparallel}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B_{I\,ij}^a=\hat n_i e_{1j}\delta^{a1}+\hat n_i e_{2j}\delta^{a2},
\label{eq:C2_BI}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
B_{J\,ij}^a=\hat n_i e_{2j}\delta^{a1}-\hat n_i e_{1j}\delta^{a2}.
\label{eq:C2_BJ}
\end{equation}

\section{Why only these three channels survive}

The reason is simple and exact:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}\) is first order in external shell momentum;
\item it carries one spatial derivative index through \(\partial_{k_i}\);
\item it carries one internal adjoint index through the mediator coupling \(X_i^a\);
\item after shell projection to the natural S2 branch, the only symmetry-compatible traceless channels are the longitudinal singlet and the two transverse doublet directions.
\end{enumerate}

Hence no fourth independent first-order Class II witness channel exists at this order.

\section{Extraction of the reduced witness coefficients}

The shell-matching formulas give
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_jN_{ij}^3,
\label{eq:C2_lambda_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^1+e_{2j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^2
\Bigr),
\label{eq:C2_alpha_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\Bigl(
e_{2j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^1-e_{1j}\hat n_iN_{ij}^2
\Bigr).
\label{eq:C2_beta_match}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:C2_seed_decomp} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{II})}\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha^{(\mathrm{II})}\propto c_I,
\qquad
\beta^{(\mathrm{II})}\propto c_J.
}
\label{eq:C2_coeffs_from_c}
\end{equation}

Using the local defect/projector dictionary, one identifies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\label{eq:C2_g_from_c}
\end{equation}

Therefore the shell-level Class II correction is completely equivalent to the coefficient triple
\[
(g_c,g_E,g_O).
\]

\section{Branch structure of the three channels}

Now the crucial point.

The explicit local Class II witness formulas are not symmetric between longitudinal and transverse sectors.
They are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:C2_exact_local_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Hence:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse channels \(g_E,g_O\) appear already at the ordinary odd-gradient \(I_\theta\)-order;
\item the longitudinal channel \(g_c\) does \emph{not} appear at \(I_\theta\)-order;
it appears only through the primitive commutator-square channel at \(I_{\theta'^3}\)-order.
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the concrete Class II realization has the seed transport basis
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\label{eq:C2_seed_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:C2_seed_even}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:C2_seed_odd}
\end{equation}

Therefore the Class II sector automatically supplies:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{transverse }S2\text{ witness channels through }B_I,\ B_J,
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the longitudinal witness only through the primitive seed }B_\parallel.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact meaning of the Schur-complement computation}

The Schur-complement derivative \eqref{eq:C2_Ki_heavy_repeat} does \emph{not} directly prove that
\[
c_\parallel,\ c_I,\ c_J
\]
are numerically nonzero for the full complete TECT action.
That would require the explicit harmonic matrices \(\mathcal J(k)\) and \(\mathcal K(k)\).

But it \emph{does} prove the following exact forward reduction:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
\Longrightarrow
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
\Longrightarrow
(c_\parallel,c_I,c_J)
\Longleftrightarrow
(g_c,g_E,g_O).
}
\label{eq:C2_forward_reduction}
\end{equation}

So the remaining microscopic Class II problem is finite and explicit:
compute the projected coefficients
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_I,\qquad c_J
\]
from the actual Bloch harmonic matrices \(H_{\Psi X}(k)\) and \(H_{XX}(k)\).

\section{Nondegeneracy criterion}

Because
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
the exact concrete Class II nondegeneracy criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:C2_nondeg_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:C2_nondeg_c}
\end{equation}

Thus the mediator sector closes the witness problem \emph{inside the explicit seed space}:
the transverse sector is already solved, while the longitudinal sector is solved on the primitive branch.

\section{Sharp honest conclusion}

The Class II Schur-complement contribution has now been reduced as far as it can be reduced
without inserting the explicit harmonic matrix elements of \(\mathcal J(k)\) and \(\mathcal K(k)\).

What is already closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact shell-level tensor channels of \(K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}\) are only \(B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\);
\item their coefficients are exactly the reduced microscopic couplings \(g_c,g_E,g_O\);
\item \(g_E,g_O\) supply the transverse \(I_\theta\)-branch;
\item \(g_c\) supplies the longitudinal primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\)-branch.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is only the finite coefficient extraction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute }(g_c,g_E,g_O)\text{ from the actual Bloch harmonic matrices.}
}
\label{eq:C2_last_open}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The Class II UV-completed working branch is
\[
S_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
S_0[\Psi]
+
\int
\left[
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi]
\right].
\]

After integrating out the heavy mediator \(X\), the effective Bloch operator is
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
\]
and the mediator contribution to the first shell derivative is
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
\partial_{k_i}
\bigl(
H_{\Psi X}H_{XX}^{-1}H_{X\Psi}
\bigr)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

At leading heavy-mass order,
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\left[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\right]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
\qquad
\mathcal C(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\]

After shell reduction, the induced first-order Class II tensor has only the three S2-compatible seed channels:
\[
N_{ij}^{a(\mathrm{II})}
=
c_\parallel B_{\parallel\,ij}^a
+
c_I B_{I\,ij}^a
+
c_J B_{J\,ij}^a,
\]
with
\[
B_{\parallel\,ij}^a=\hat n_i\hat n_j\delta^{a3},
\qquad
B_{I\,ij}^a=\hat n_i e_{1j}\delta^{a1}+\hat n_i e_{2j}\delta^{a2},
\qquad
B_{J\,ij}^a=\hat n_i e_{2j}\delta^{a1}-\hat n_i e_{1j}\delta^{a2}.
\]

Their coefficients are exactly the reduced Class II couplings:
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

The exact local Class II witness formulas are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the transverse S2 witness channels are supplied by }g_E,g_O\text{ at }I_\theta\text{-order,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the longitudinal Class II witness is supplied by }g_c\text{ only on the primitive }I_{\theta'^3}\text{-branch.}
}
\]

Hence the exact concrete Class II nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Thus the remaining microscopic frontier is no longer structural.
It is the finite coefficient extraction problem:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }(g_c,g_E,g_O)\text{ from the actual harmonic matrices }H_{\Psi X}(k),H_{XX}(k).
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit reciprocal-harmonic matrix of \texorpdfstring{$J_i^a[\Psi]$}{J_i^a[Psi]} on the locked 12-mode BCC background}

\section{Scope}

At the current document level, the Class II UV action is explicitly
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:Jblock_Lmic_repeat}
\end{equation}
The current notes give the exact microscopic definition
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi),
\label{eq:Jblock_J_def}
\end{equation}
while the \(K\)-sector is only available in shell-relevant template form
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P,\psi]\sim (T^a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\qquad
K_i^a[P,\psi]\sim \partial_i\delta P^a\,\psi.
\label{eq:Jblock_K_template}
\end{equation}

Therefore the next honest forward step is:
\[
\text{compute }\mathcal J(k)\text{ explicitly,}
\qquad
\text{keep }\mathcal K(k)\text{ as a reduced template.}
\]

\section{Locked periodic background and Bloch fluctuation basis}

Take the locked 12-mode BCC background
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\label{eq:Jblock_locked_background}
\end{equation}
Choose an internal orthonormal basis
\begin{equation}
u_0=z_0,
\qquad
u_1,u_2\in Q_{z_0},
\qquad
u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs}.
\label{eq:Jblock_internal_basis}
\end{equation}
Write the Bloch fluctuation as
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\mathcal G}\sum_{r=0}^2
c_{G,r}\,u_r\,e^{iG\cdot x}.
\label{eq:Jblock_deltaPsi}
\end{equation}
For the heavy mediator,
\begin{equation}
\delta X_i^a(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G\in\mathcal G}x_{G,i,a}\,e^{iG\cdot x}.
\label{eq:Jblock_deltaX}
\end{equation}

\section{Linearization of \texorpdfstring{$J_i^a$}{J}}

Expand \(\Psi=\Psi_0+\delta\Psi\). Since \(J_i^a\) is bilinear in \(\Psi\), its linearization around the background is
\begin{equation}
\delta J_i^a[\delta\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\delta\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi_0
+
(\partial_i\Psi_0^\dagger)T^a\delta\Psi
+
\delta\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi_0)
+
\Psi_0^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\delta\Psi).
\label{eq:Jblock_deltaJ_full}
\end{equation}

Now use
\begin{equation}
\partial_i\Psi_0(x)
=
z_0\,\partial_i\phi_0(x)
=
iA\,z_0\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}Q_i\,e^{iQ\cdot x},
\label{eq:Jblock_dPsi0}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\partial_i\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G,r} i(k+G)_i\,c_{G,r}\,u_r\,e^{iG\cdot x}.
\label{eq:Jblock_ddeltaPsi}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Jblock_locked_background}--\eqref{eq:Jblock_ddeltaPsi} into
\eqref{eq:Jblock_deltaJ_full}, every term becomes a finite sum of harmonics of the form
\[
e^{i(k+G+Q)\cdot x}
\quad\text{or}\quad
e^{i(k+G-Q)\cdot x}.
\]
Hence the linearized current is a convolution operator in reciprocal space.

\section{Exact harmonic matrix elements of \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal J(k)$}{J(k)}}

Define the Bloch-space matrix \(\mathcal J(k)\) by
\begin{equation}
\delta J_i^a(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}
\sum_{G',i,a}
\bigl(\mathcal J(k)\,c\bigr)_{G',i,a}\,e^{iG'\cdot x}.
\label{eq:Jblock_Jmatrix_def}
\end{equation}
Then the coefficient of \(e^{i(k+G')\cdot x}\) is obtained by matching
\[
G'=G+Q
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
G'=G-Q.
\]

Introduce the internal constants
\begin{equation}
t_{rs}^a:=u_r^\dagger T^a u_s.
\label{eq:Jblock_t_def}
\end{equation}
Because \(T^a\) is Hermitian,
\[
t_{sr}^a=\overline{t_{rs}^a}.
\]

A direct substitution gives the harmonic matrix elements
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G',\,;\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\Big[
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,(k+G)_i\,t_{r0}^a
+
\delta_{G',\,G-Q}\,Q_i\,t_{0r}^a
+
\delta_{G',\,G-Q}\,Q_i\,t_{r0}^a
+
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,(k+G)_i\,t_{0r}^a
\Big].
}
\label{eq:Jblock_Jmatrix_raw}
\end{equation}

Grouping the \(G'=G+Q\) and \(G'=G-Q\) channels yields the cleaner form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G',\,;\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\left[
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,(k+G)_i\bigl(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a\bigr)
+
\delta_{G',\,G-Q}\,Q_i\bigl(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a\bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:Jblock_Jmatrix_clean}
\end{equation}

Thus \(\mathcal J(k)\) is explicitly known once the locked internal direction \(z_0\) and the tangent basis
\((u_1,u_2)\) are fixed.

\section{Selection rules on the locked branch}

The tangent-shell sector relevant for the reduced \(2+2\) problem uses only \(r=1,2\).
Therefore the physically relevant matrix elements are controlled by
\begin{equation}
t_{\alpha 0}^a=u_\alpha^\dagger T^a z_0,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
\label{eq:Jblock_tangent_couplings}
\end{equation}

Hence the first exact microscopic criterion is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J(k)\text{ couples the shell-tangent doublet to the mediator iff }
u_\alpha^\dagger T^a z_0\neq 0
\text{ for some }(\alpha,a).
}
\label{eq:Jblock_first_criterion}
\end{equation}

This is now a concrete finite internal-algebra test, not a qualitative guess.

\section{Derivative with respect to Bloch momentum}

Since only the \((k+G)_i\)-terms carry explicit \(k\)-dependence, one immediately obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{k_j}\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G',\,;\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,\delta_{ij}\,\bigl(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Jblock_dJdk}
\end{equation}

This formula is especially important because the Class II Schur contribution to the first shell derivative is
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II})}
\sim
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\Big],
\qquad
\mathcal C=\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K.
\]
So the \(J\)-part of the derivative is already fully explicit.

\section{Near-Bragg shell restriction}

At the folded Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\), the shell basis is
\begin{equation}
|+\!,\alpha\rangle \equiv |G=0,\alpha\rangle,
\qquad
|-\!,\alpha\rangle \equiv |G=-G_*,\alpha\rangle,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
\label{eq:Jblock_shell_basis}
\end{equation}

The matrix element
\[
\langle +,\alpha|\mathcal J_i^a(k_*)|-,\beta\rangle
\]
is nonzero only if the shell difference is supplied by one background harmonic:
\begin{equation}
0=(-G_*)+Q
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
Q=G_*.
\label{eq:Jblock_Bragg_condition}
\end{equation}
Therefore only those \(Q\in\mathcal S_{12}\) satisfying the Bragg matching condition contribute directly to the shell off-diagonal block.

Hence the direct shell-coupling part of \(\mathcal J(k_*)\) is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle +,\alpha|\mathcal J_i^a(k_*)|-,\beta\rangle
=
iA\,(k_*-G_*)_i\,
\bigl(t_{\beta 0}^a+t_{0\beta}^a\bigr)\,
\delta_{Q,G_*},
}
\label{eq:Jblock_shell_offdiag}
\end{equation}
up to the conventional shell normalization and possible finite truncation of equivalent reciprocal representatives.

Since
\[
k_*-\!G_*=-\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
this is generically nonzero whenever the internal overlap
\[
t_{\beta0}^a+t_{0\beta}^a
\]
is nonzero.

\section{What is closed and what remains open}

The \(J\)-sector is now explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact harmonic matrix \(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\) is given by \eqref{eq:Jblock_Jmatrix_clean};
\item its Bloch derivative \(\partial_{k_j}\mathcal J_i^a(k)\) is given by \eqref{eq:Jblock_dJdk};
\item the shell selection rule is the single-harmonic Bragg condition \(Q=G_*\).
\end{enumerate}

By contrast, the \(K\)-sector is not yet unreduced explicitly in the current notes.
All that is honestly available is the shell-relevant template
\[
K_i^a[P,\psi]\sim (T^a\partial_iP)\mathcal O[\psi],
\qquad
K_i^a\sim \partial_i\delta P^a\,\psi,
\]
together with the already-reduced tensor summary and the induced coefficient dictionary
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

Therefore the current frontier is sharply split:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{\(\mathcal J(k)\) is explicit,}
\qquad
\text{\(\mathcal K(k)\) remains a reduced template.}
}
\label{eq:Jblock_frontier_split}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate next use inside the Schur complement}

The exact next finite computation is now
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
}
\label{eq:Jblock_next_target_JJ}
\end{equation}
together with the mixed \(JK\)-piece
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},JK)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal K^\dagger
+
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal K)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal K^\dagger)
+
\mathcal K(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
}
\label{eq:Jblock_next_target_JK}
\end{equation}
where only the \(\mathcal K\)-insertions remain unreduced.

\section{Final Summary}

The Class II current is explicitly defined by
\[
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi),
\]
while the \(K\)-sector is currently available only through the reduced shell-relevant template
\[
K_i^a[P,\psi]\sim (T^a\partial_iP)\mathcal O[\psi],
\qquad
K_i^a[P,\psi]\sim \partial_i\delta P^a\,\psi.
\]

On the locked 12-mode BCC background
\[
\Psi_0=z_0\phi_0,
\qquad
\phi_0=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
with Bloch fluctuation
\[
\delta\Psi_k(x)=e^{ik\cdot x}\sum_{G,r}c_{G,r}u_r e^{iG\cdot x},
\]
the linearized current \(\delta J_i^a\) is a reciprocal-space convolution operator.

Defining
\[
t_{rs}^a:=u_r^\dagger T^a u_s,
\]
its exact harmonic matrix elements are
\[
\boxed{
\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G',\,;\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\left[
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,(k+G)_i\bigl(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a\bigr)
+
\delta_{G',\,G-Q}\,Q_i\bigl(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a\bigr)
\right].
}
\]

Its Bloch derivative is therefore explicit:
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{k_j}\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G',\,;\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,\delta_{ij}\,\bigl(t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a\bigr).
}
\]

At the folded Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\), direct shell coupling occurs only through the single-harmonic Bragg condition
\[
Q=G_*.
\]

Thus the \(J\)-sector is already explicit enough to be inserted into the Class II Schur-complement derivative.

By contrast, \(\mathcal K(k)\) is not yet unreduced explicitly in the current notes.
Hence the honest current frontier is
\[
\boxed{
\text{\(\mathcal J(k)\) is explicit, while \(\mathcal K(k)\) remains a reduced template.}
}
\]

Therefore the exact next finite computation is the explicit \(JJ\)-part
\[
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*},
}
\]
followed by the mixed \(JK\)-part, where only the \(\mathcal K\)-insertions remain open.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit shell evaluation of the \(JJ\) part of the Class II Schur complement}

\section{Goal}

We now compute the part of the Class II shell derivative that is already fully explicit from the current notes, namely the \(JJ\)-piece:
\begin{equation}
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\label{eq:JJ_start}
\end{equation}

The purpose is not to determine the final numerical values of all coefficients,
but to identify which reduced S2 channels are already generated by the explicit \(J\)-sector.

\section{Explicit harmonic matrix of \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal J(k)$}{J(k)}}

On the locked 12-mode BCC background
\[
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\phi_0(x),
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
the exact reciprocal-harmonic matrix elements of \(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\) are
\begin{equation}
\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G',\,;\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\left[
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}(k+G)_i\,u_r^a
+
\delta_{G',\,G-Q}Q_i\,u_r^a
\right],
\label{eq:JJ_Jmatrix}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
u_r^a:=t_{r0}^a+t_{0r}^a,
\qquad
t_{r0}^a=u_r^\dagger T^a z_0.
\label{eq:JJ_ur_def}
\end{equation}
The explicit Bloch derivative is
\begin{equation}
\partial_{k_j}\bigl(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\bigr)_{G',\,;\,G,r}
=
iA\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,\delta_{ij}\,u_r^a.
\label{eq:JJ_dJdk}
\end{equation}

Thus the derivative part is diagonal in the spatial indices:
\[
\partial_{k_j}\mathcal J_i^a \propto \delta_{ij}.
\]

\section{Shell basis and Bragg matching}

The folded shell basis is
\begin{equation}
|+\!,\alpha\rangle\equiv |G=0,\alpha\rangle,
\qquad
|-\!,\alpha\rangle\equiv |G=-G_*,\alpha\rangle,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
\label{eq:JJ_shell_basis}
\end{equation}
Direct shell coupling occurs only when one background harmonic matches the shell separation:
\begin{equation}
0=(-G_*)+Q
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
Q=G_*.
\label{eq:JJ_Bragg_match}
\end{equation}

Therefore both \(\mathcal J(k_*)\) and \(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J(k_*)\) reduce on the shell to rank-one Bragg-transfer operators between the \(\pm\) valleys.

\section{Structure of the shell matrix product}

Because \(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J\) carries a factor \(\delta_{ij}\), the product
\[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger+\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\]
inherits the same external spatial direction as the residual \(\mathcal J\)-matrix element.

At the shell level, every matrix element is proportional to one factor of the Bragg vector:
\begin{equation}
\bigl(K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\bigr)_{\alpha\beta}
\propto
\hat n_i\,
\sum_{a}
u_\alpha^a\,\overline{u_\beta^a},
\label{eq:JJ_shell_direction}
\end{equation}
up to the common scalar normalization
\[
\frac{\alpha_X^2A^2|G_*|}{M_X^2}.
\]

Hence the \(JJ\)-piece is \emph{axial}: it carries only the shell normal direction \(\hat n_i\) and no intrinsic \(e_1,e_2\) structure.

\section{Internal \(2\times 2\) matrix induced by the \(J\)-sector}

Define the Hermitian tangent-doublet matrix
\begin{equation}
M_{\alpha\beta}:=\sum_a u_\alpha^a\,\overline{u_\beta^a}.
\label{eq:JJ_Mmatrix}
\end{equation}
Then the shell derivative takes the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
\qquad
\Gamma_J>0
\text{ up to the overall conventional sign normalization.}
}
\label{eq:JJ_Ki_Mform}
\end{equation}

Now decompose \(M\) in the Pauli basis:
\begin{equation}
M
=
m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3,
\label{eq:JJ_M_Pauli}
\end{equation}
with
\[
m_\mu=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_\mu M),
\qquad
\sigma_0:=\mathbf 1_2.
\]

Therefore
\begin{equation}
p_iK_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\Gamma_J\,p_\parallel
\left(
m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3
\right).
\label{eq:JJ_pKi_general}
\end{equation}

\section{What survives after S2 reduction}

The reduced S2 target symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:JJ_S2_target}
\end{equation}

Comparing \eqref{eq:JJ_pKi_general} with \eqref{eq:JJ_S2_target}, we obtain:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(JJ\)-piece carries only \(p_\parallel\), so it cannot by itself generate the transverse S2 channels proportional to \(p_1,p_2\);
\item the scalar \(m_0\mathbf 1_2\) part is irrelevant to the reduced Weyl witness;
\item the only potentially load-bearing piece is the traceless longitudinal part
\[
-\Gamma_J\,m_3\,p_\parallel\sigma_3.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus the \(JJ\)-sector alone contributes at most to the longitudinal shell singlet channel:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\propto m_3,
\qquad
\alpha^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0,
\qquad
\beta^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0.
}
\label{eq:JJ_channel_result}
\end{equation}

\section{Why this does not close the final longitudinal problem}

At first sight, \eqref{eq:JJ_channel_result} seems to generate a longitudinal \(p_\parallel\sigma_3\) term already at the ordinary \(I_\theta\)-type shell order.
However, the exact local Class II transport analysis in the current notes shows that the concrete longitudinal coefficient is instead
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:JJ_exact_long_branch}
\end{equation}
whereas the transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:JJ_exact_transverse_branch}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit local theory states that the true longitudinal witness does \emph{not} come from the ordinary \(I_\theta\)-branch of the toy \(J\)-type extraction.
It comes from the distinct primitive commutator-square channel.

So the correct interpretation of \eqref{eq:JJ_channel_result} is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the pure }JJ\text{ shell term can only probe a longitudinal-type direction,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{it does not by itself establish the true concrete Class II longitudinal coefficient }g_c.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate consequence}

Because the \(JJ\)-piece is purely axial, it cannot generate the explicit transverse seed directions
\[
B_I,\qquad B_J.
\]
Hence the transverse Class II coefficients \(g_E,g_O\) cannot come from the pure \(JJ\) piece alone.

They must instead come from one of the following:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(JK\) mixed term,
\item the \(KK\) term,
\item the already-established reduced local transport completion.
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\ \text{is longitudinal-only at the shell level.}
}
\label{eq:JJ_long_only}
\end{equation}

\section{Sharp honest result}

The pure explicit \(J\)-sector allows us to go one real step forward:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the }JJ\text{-part of the Class II Schur complement is now explicitly reduced to an axial shell singlet matrix.}
}
\end{equation}

But it also shows a hard limitation:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the transverse witness channels }(g_E,g_O)\text{ are not generated by }JJ\text{ alone.}
}
\end{equation}

Hence the next actual microscopic computation must be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},JK)}
\quad\text{and/or}\quad
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},KK)},
}
\label{eq:JJ_next_open}
\end{equation}
because only there can the explicit projector-derived tensor structure enter and produce the \(B_I,B_J\) directions.

\section{Final Summary}

For the explicit working branch
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi],
\]
the pure \(JJ\)-part of the Class II Schur complement is
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal J^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
\]

Using the explicit harmonic matrix of \(\mathcal J(k)\), one finds that:
\[
\partial_{k_j}\mathcal J_i^a\propto \delta_{ij},
\]
and the shell coupling is fixed by the single-harmonic Bragg condition
\[
Q=G_*.
\]

Therefore the shell-reduced \(JJ\)-piece has the universal form
\[
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\Gamma_J\,\hat n_i\,M,
\]
where \(M\) is a Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix on the tangent doublet space.

After Pauli decomposition
\[
M=m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3,
\]
the shell symbol becomes
\[
p_iK_i^{(\mathrm{II},J)}
=
-\Gamma_J p_\parallel
(m_0\mathbf 1_2+m_1\sigma_1+m_2\sigma_2+m_3\sigma_3).
\]

Hence the pure \(JJ\)-sector is \emph{axial only}:
it carries only the shell-normal direction \(p_\parallel\) and no intrinsic transverse \(p_1,p_2\) structure.

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(\mathrm{II},J)}\propto m_3,
\qquad
\alpha^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0,
\qquad
\beta^{(\mathrm{II},J)}=0.
}
\]

So the explicit \(JJ\)-piece can probe only a longitudinal-type shell singlet direction.
It cannot by itself generate the transverse Class II witness channels \(g_E,g_O\).

This is fully consistent with the exact local Class II transport formulas:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\]
which show that the true concrete longitudinal witness belongs to the primitive branch, while the transverse witness belongs to the ordinary odd-gradient branch.

Hence the next genuinely load-bearing microscopic computation is not \(JJ\) anymore, but
\[
\boxed{
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},JK)}
\quad\text{and/or}\quad
K_i^{(\mathrm{II},KK)},
}
\]
because only those terms can inject explicit projector-derived tensor structure and generate the transverse seed directions \(B_I,B_J\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Working reduced principal operator of the explicit TECT + Class II branch}

We now stop the carrier-audit phase and write the actual working reduced first-order operator
for the strongest explicit microscopic branch.

The explicit working microscopic branch is
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:work_full_branch_again}
\end{equation}

After eliminating the heavy mediator \(X_i^a\), the shell-relevant enriched tensor induced by the
mixed \(JK\)-sector is, at quadratic template level,
\begin{equation}
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^aC_{ij}^{ab}.
\label{eq:deltaN_main}
\end{equation}

For the shell-adapted seed family
\begin{equation}
m^a=m\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:m_seed_main}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:C33_main}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:C31C32_main}
\end{equation}
this gives
\begin{equation}
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J,
\qquad
\Gamma:=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
\label{eq:ABC_shift_main}
\end{equation}

Using the already-closed shell/defect dictionary,
\begin{equation}
g_c=\nu_\parallel \Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\nu_\perp \Gamma c_I,
\qquad
g_O=\nu_\perp \Gamma c_J,
\label{eq:gcgego_main}
\end{equation}
where \(\nu_\parallel,\nu_\perp\) are finite nonzero overlap normalizations.

Therefore the local reduced first-order symbol of the explicit working branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{work}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{work}} p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha^{\mathrm{work}}(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta^{\mathrm{work}}(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
}
\label{eq:A1_work_main}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{work}}
=
\lambda_\parallel^{(\Psi)}
+
\frac{1}{2}\,g_c\,I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:lam_work_main}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha^{\mathrm{work}}
=
\alpha^{(\Psi)}
+
g_E\,I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{work}}
=
\beta^{(\Psi)}
+
g_O\,I_\theta.
\label{eq:ab_work_main}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{work}}
=
\lambda_\parallel^{(\Psi)}
+
\frac{\nu_\parallel \Gamma c_\parallel}{2}\,I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:lam_work_seed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha^{\mathrm{work}}
=
\alpha^{(\Psi)}
+
\nu_\perp \Gamma c_I\,I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{work}}
=
\beta^{(\Psi)}
+
\nu_\perp \Gamma c_J\,I_\theta.
\label{eq:ab_work_seed}
\end{equation}

Hence the explicit Class II truncation by itself already gives a nondegenerate local Weyl symbol
whenever
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:seed_nondeg_main}
\end{equation}
provided the overlap constants remain finite and nonzero.

In the pure Class II working truncation, setting the unresolved triplet-refined contribution to zero,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^{(\Psi)}=\alpha^{(\Psi)}=\beta^{(\Psi)}=0,
\label{eq:pure_classII_choice}
\end{equation}
one obtains the fully explicit reduced principal symbol
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}(p)
=
\frac{\nu_\parallel \Gamma c_\parallel}{2}\,I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\nu_\perp \Gamma I_\theta
\Big[
c_I(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
c_J(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Big].
}
\label{eq:A1_pure_classII}
\end{equation}

This is now the actual working reduced PDE data.
The next stage is no longer to search for a carrier,
but to impose the remaining finite Dirac conditions:
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\Delta>0,
\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\label{eq:next_dirac_finite}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Dirac Step III as an actual working zero-mixing theorem}

\section{Goal}

We now stop discussing the zero-mixing step abstractly and write the actual working form
needed for the explicit TECT + Class II truncation.

The shell-relevant local Dirac carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
}
\label{eq:V0_HD_work}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\) is the selected opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\),
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the enriched transverse/internal doublet.
\end{itemize}

At \(p=0\), the full projected block has the form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(0)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(0) & V(0)\\
V(0)^\dagger & H_R(0)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:V0_block_work}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:V0_Hom_work}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal dangerous truncation}

For the working explicit branch, the remote sector should be organized as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}.
}
\label{eq:V0_remote_split}
\end{equation}

These sectors mean:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\): volumetric / longitudinal sector,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\): higher-shell sector not belonging to the selected pair \(\pm G_*\),
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\): same shell but lacking the enriched internal doublet,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\): nonmatching internal representation,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\): any remaining sector not covered by the previous canonical exclusions.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Immediate exclusions}

The shell-relevant mismatch labels are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved microscopic label}.
}
\label{eq:V0_labels_work}
\end{equation}

Hence the first four canonical remote sectors are excluded immediately:

\paragraph{\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\).}
This sector fails the transverse/non-volumetric label.
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:V0_vol_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\).}
This sector fails the shell-pair label \(\pm G_*\).
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:V0_high_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\).}
This sector lacks the enriched internal doublet \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\).
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:V0_nonenr_zero}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\).}
This sector has the wrong internal representation.
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\label{eq:V0_wrongint_zero}
\end{equation}

Combining these,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}
\bigl(
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\mathcal H_D
\bigr)=0.
}
\label{eq:V0_first4_zero}
\end{equation}

\section{Compression of the actual frontier}

Therefore the entire zero-mixing problem compresses to the remaining sector
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}.
\]
Indeed,
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}},\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:V0_reduce_extra}
\end{equation}

So the actual Step III frontier is no longer broad.
It is only the following finite question:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does there exist any extra remote sector }K\subset \mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}
\text{ that matches }\mathcal H_D
\text{ in all shell-relevant labels?}
}
\label{eq:V0_last_question}
\end{equation}

If the answer is no, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:V0_done}
\end{equation}

\section{Operational form for the working TECT program}

Thus the zero-mixing step for the working explicit TECT + Class II branch is now:

\begin{enumerate}
\item construct the shell-relevant carrier
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}};
\]
\item decompose the remote sector into
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}};
\]
\item eliminate the first four sectors by the canonical label mismatches;
\item inspect only \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the actual working deliverable for Step III is not a vague symmetry discussion.
It is the finite claim
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing
\quad\text{or}\quad
\forall K\subset\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}},\ 
K\text{ mismatches }\mathcal H_D\text{ in at least one label.}
}
\label{eq:V0_working_deliverable}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact consequence for the effective Dirac block}

If \eqref{eq:V0_working_deliverable} holds, then
\[
V(0)=0.
\]
Combined with the remote gap condition \(\Delta>0\), the Schur self-energy satisfies
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
=
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
\label{eq:V0_sigma_order}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)
+
O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right),
}
\label{eq:V0_eff_done}
\end{equation}
with no \(O(p^0)\) constant mixing from the remote sector.

This is the actual forward-completion meaning of Step III.

\section{Final Summary}

The zero-constant-mixing step is now compressed to a concrete working theorem.

The shell-relevant Dirac carrier is
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
and at \(p=0\),
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
\]

For the working explicit TECT + Class II truncation, decompose
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}.
\]

The shell-relevant mismatch labels are:
\[
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved microscopic label}.
\]

The first four sectors are excluded immediately:
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0,
\]
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

Therefore the entire Step III frontier reduces to a single finite question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does any }K\subset\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}
\text{ match }\mathcal H_D\text{ in all shell-relevant labels?}
}
\]

If no such extra dangerous sector exists, then
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\]

Then, together with a positive remote gap \(\Delta>0\),
\[
\Sigma(E,p)=O(|p|^2/\Delta),
\]
and the effective shell Hamiltonian becomes
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O(|p|^2/\Delta),
}
\]
with no constant remote-sector mixing.
