\section{Working closure of Step III}

At the level of the explicit working TECT + Class II truncation, we now impose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{extra}}=\varnothing.
}
\label{eq:stepIII_working_closure}
\end{equation}

Since each of the four displayed remote sectors mismatches the Dirac carrier
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
in at least one shell-relevant label, it follows that
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:stepIII_done_working}
\end{equation}

Thus, for the working truncation, Step III is now closed by definition, and the actual next task is Step IV:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta:=\operatorname{dist}\bigl(\operatorname{spec}H_R(0),E_D(0)\bigr)>0.
}
\label{eq:stepIV_next}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Step IV in working form: explicit finite remote-gap inequality}

\section{Goal}

We now stop repeating the abstract spectral-isolation theorem and write the actual working form
of Step IV for the explicit TECT + Class II truncation.

The remote-gap problem is not solved by the shell determinant
\[
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)\neq 0.
\]
That determinant controls only the nondegeneracy of the local shell Dirac block.
The remote gap
\[
\Delta_\rho>0
\]
is an independent spectral property of the remote block \(H_R(p)\).

What is already closed at theorem level is that the full Step IV reduces to a finite matrix inequality
on the remote block.

\section{Remote-block decomposition}

For the working truncation, write
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\label{eq:step4_full_block}
\end{equation}

Decompose the remote block as
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\label{eq:step4_DR_RR}
\end{equation}
where \(D_R(p)\) is the diagonal benchmark part and \(R_R(p)\) is the residual Hermitian mixing.

Define the four sector-center energies
\begin{equation}
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p),
\label{eq:step4_sector_centers}
\end{equation}
and set
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p)
=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\label{eq:step4_delta0p}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\eta_R(p)=\|R_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:step4_etaRp}
\end{equation}

On the neighborhood
\[
N_\rho=\{|p|\le \rho\},
\]
define
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\label{eq:step4_delta0rho_etaRrho}
\end{equation}

\section{Working remote-gap theorem}

The exact theorem-level sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\quad(|p|\le \rho),
}
\label{eq:step4_main_criterion}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:step4_gap_formula}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, a Gershgorin sufficient bound is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_a
\left(
|(H_R)_{aa}(p)|-\sum_{b\neq a}|(H_R)_{ab}(p)|
\right)>0.
\label{eq:step4_gershgorin}
\end{equation}

Thus Step IV is no longer conceptual.
It is a finite lower-bound problem on \(H_R(p)\).

\section{Immediate explicit input already available}

Among the four sector centers, the current uploaded notes already provide an explicit formula
for the wrong-internal shell separation.

The longitudinal--transverse splitting is
\begin{equation}
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right].
\label{eq:step4_EL_minus_Estar}
\end{equation}
Hence the wrong-internal benchmark gap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
|E_L-E_*|
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
}
\label{eq:step4_wrongint_explicit}
\end{equation}

Therefore a sufficient condition for the wrong-internal sector to stay separated is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:step4_wrongint_nonzero}
\end{equation}
A stronger sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
>0,
}
\label{eq:step4_wrongint_positive}
\end{equation}
which implies \(E_L>E_*\) and hence \(m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}>0\).

Under a bounded perturbation of the wrong-internal block,
\begin{equation}
\|Q\,\delta H\,Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\end{equation}
one has the stable lower bound
\begin{equation}
m_{\mathrm{int}}\ge m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:step4_wrongint_stable}
\end{equation}

\section{Working closure strategy}

We now impose the following working Step IV strategy.

First, define the diagonal benchmark gap by
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
m_{\mathrm{int}}(p)
\}.
\label{eq:step4_bench_gap}
\end{equation}

Second, define the total remote mixing budget
\begin{equation}
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:step4_rem_budget}
\end{equation}

Then the actual working deliverable of Step IV is the single inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:step4_working_goal}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:step4_working_goal} holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
>0.
}
\label{eq:step4_full_gap}
\end{equation}

\section{Consequences for the Dirac block}

Once Step III and Step IV both hold, namely
\[
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\]
the Schur-complement resolvent bound gives
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|
\le
\frac{2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}}
\qquad
(|E|<\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}/2),
\label{eq:step4_resolvent}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}}|p|^2.
\label{eq:step4_selfenergy}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}}\right).
}
\label{eq:step4_Heff}
\end{equation}

\section{Sharp honest status}

What is closed now is the exact working form of Step IV:
the remote-gap problem has been reduced to the finite inequality
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

What is not yet fully evaluated in the uploaded material is the full set of explicit formulas for
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),
\]
and the final upper bound for
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

So the remaining Step IV frontier is now exactly this:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the three remaining benchmark sector centers and one remote mixing norm bound.}
}
\label{eq:step4_last_frontier}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The remote-gap condition
\[
\Delta_\rho>0
\]
is an independent spectral input.
It is not implied by the shell determinant
\[
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)\neq 0,
\]
which controls only the local Dirac-block nondegeneracy.

For the working truncation,
\[
\mathcal H_R
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
and
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p).
\]

Define the benchmark sector-center energies
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\quad
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\quad
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),\quad
\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p),
\]
together with
\[
\delta_0(p)
=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\]
\[
\eta_R(p)=\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

On \(|p|\le \rho\),
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\]

Then the exact working sufficient criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

Equivalently one may use the Gershgorin bound
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0.
\]

The currently uploaded notes already provide one explicit benchmark piece:
the wrong-internal gap
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
\]
Hence a sufficient condition for wrong-internal separation is
\[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\neq 0,
\]
and a stronger sufficient condition is positivity of the same quantity.

Therefore the remaining Step IV frontier is finite and explicit:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\ 
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\ 
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p),
\text{ and an upper bound for }\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Once
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}>0,\qquad \|V(p)\|\le c|p|
\]
all hold, the Schur complement gives
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O(|p|^2/\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}),
\]
so the remote sector only contributes subleading curvature corrections.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Working benchmark formulas for the remaining Step-IV sector centers}

\section{Goal}

We now stop repeating the abstract remote-gap theorem and write the actual working benchmark
formulas for the three remaining remote-sector centers:
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p).
\]

The remote-gap criterion is already fixed:
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\]
So the only forward task is to give explicit lower bounds for the sector centers.

\section{Volumetric sector benchmark}

The volumetric sector is controlled by the heavy scalar locking mode \(\sigma\), which couples
only to the longitudinal displacement and decouples from the transverse sector at quadratic order.
The coupled longitudinal--volumetric block is
\[
L_{L,\sigma}^{(2)}
=
\frac12 \rho |\dot u_L|^2
-\frac12 (\lambda+2\mu)k^2 |u_L|^2
+
\frac12 |\dot\sigma|^2
-\frac12 (M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 k^2)|\sigma|^2
+
g\,\sigma(-\mathbf k)\, i k\,u_L(\mathbf k).
\]

Therefore the natural remote benchmark energy of the volumetric sector is set by the heavy
volumetric mode:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)\simeq \sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2|p|^2}.
}
\label{eq:muvol_working}
\end{equation}

On \(|p|\le \rho\), a uniform lower bound is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_vol_working}
\end{equation}

In a weaker model-independent form one may simply use
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma>0
\end{equation}
for some finite \(c_{\mathrm{vol}}>0\).

\section{Higher-shell benchmark}

The higher-shell sector consists of harmonics not belonging to the selected pair \(\pm G_*\).
Hence it is separated radially from the selected shell by the Brazovskii penalty
\[
r_*+K\bigl(|q|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2.
\]

Accordingly, the working higher-shell sector center is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)
\simeq
r_*+K\bigl(|k_*+p+G|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2,
\qquad
G\notin\{0,-G_*\}.
}
\label{eq:muhigh_working}
\end{equation}

A sufficient benchmark lower bound is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|,
\label{eq:Delta_high_general}
\end{equation}
where \(\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}\) is the minimal radial separation from the selected shell.

In the current explicit benchmark notes, this is specialized to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
4K-|r_*|.
}
\label{eq:Delta_high_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{Non-enriched same-shell benchmark}

The non-enriched sector lies on the same shell, but it does not carry the enriched internal doublet
that defines the Dirac block.
Therefore its separation is not controlled by radial shell distance, but by the internal block
eigenvalue splitting inside the same-shell truncation.

Thus the correct working definition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)
=
\text{lowest eigenvalue of the same-shell non-enriched internal block.}
}
\label{eq:munonenr_working}
\end{equation}

At the finite truncation level, the notes already reduce this to the benchmark lower bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_nonenr_working}
\end{equation}

Therefore this is the only genuinely non-automatic same-shell piece that still requires an
actual finite matrix eigenvalue computation.

\section{Wrong-internal benchmark}

For completeness, the already-explicit wrong-internal gap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
}
\label{eq:mwrongint_repeat}
\end{equation}

\section{Final benchmark summary}

Combining the four sectorwise lower bounds, the final benchmark gap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_bench_final_working}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual Step-IV closure condition for the working truncation is the single finite inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:StepIV_single_ineq}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:StepIV_single_ineq} holds, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}
>0.
}
\label{eq:StepIV_done_working}
\end{equation}

\section{What is now genuinely left}

After this reduction, the remaining work is no longer structural.

Three of the four sector benchmarks are already fixed in usable working form:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)},\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}.
\]

The only genuinely model-specific unresolved benchmark is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\]
together with the residual remote mixing norm
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]

Thus the final Step-IV frontier has been compressed to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{one finite same-shell non-enriched eigenvalue computation}
\quad+\quad
\text{one remote-mixing norm bound.}
}
\label{eq:StepIV_last_frontier_reduced}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The Step-IV remote-gap criterion is already fixed:
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\]

The remaining forward task was to write explicit working benchmark formulas for
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p),\qquad
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p).
\]

These are now fixed as follows.

For the volumetric sector,
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)\simeq \sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2|p|^2},
\]
with uniform lower bound
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}.
\]

For the higher-shell sector,
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)
\simeq
r_*+K\bigl(|k_*+p+G|^2-q_*^2\bigr)^2,
\qquad
G\notin\{0,-G_*\},
\]
with explicit benchmark
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
4K-|r_*|.
\]

For the non-enriched same-shell sector,
\[
\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)
=
\text{lowest eigenvalue of the same-shell non-enriched internal block},
\]
with finite-truncation lower bound
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]

The wrong-internal sector is already explicit:
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|.
\]

Hence the final working benchmark gap is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\]

Therefore the actual Step-IV closure condition is the single finite inequality
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

After this reduction, the only genuinely unresolved Step-IV data are:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]

So the final frontier is no longer broad:
it is one same-shell non-enriched finite matrix eigenvalue computation plus one remote-mixing norm bound.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Working finite matrix for the same-shell non-enriched sector}

\section{Goal}

The only genuinely non-automatic Step-IV slot is the same-shell non-enriched sector.
Its correct benchmark is not a universal symbolic formula, but an actual finite truncated eigenvalue computation.

The exact definition is already fixed:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
:=
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
\,H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)\,
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)},
\label{eq:nonenr_block_def_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\Bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p))
\Bigr).
\label{eq:nonenr_gap_def_again}
\end{equation}

We now write the actual working matrix form that must be computed.

\section{Finite shell-truncated space}

Let the shell-truncated Bloch space be
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}
=
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{rest}}^{(N)}.
\label{eq:shell_split_N}
\end{equation}

Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\) is the enriched shell doublet sector producing the local Dirac block;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}\) is the complementary same-shell sector without the enriched internal doublet;
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{rest}}^{(N)}\) contains all other truncated states.
\end{itemize}

Choose an orthonormal basis of same-shell harmonics
\begin{equation}
\mathcal B_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}
=
\left\{
|G_a,\chi_\alpha\rangle
\right\},
\qquad
a=1,\dots,N_s,
\quad
\alpha=1,\dots,n_{\mathrm{int}},
\label{eq:shell_basis_general}
\end{equation}
with \(G_a\) restricted to the selected shell orbit and \(\chi_\alpha\) spanning the internal sector.

The enriched Dirac carrier occupies a distinguished \(4\)-dimensional subspace
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
so the same-shell non-enriched complement is the orthogonal remainder inside the same shell:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
=
\left(
\bigoplus_{a=1}^{N_s}\mathrm{span}\{|G_a,\chi_\alpha\rangle\}
\right)
\ominus
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}.
\label{eq:nonenr_complement}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal working basis}

For the minimal dangerous truncation, the smallest useful basis is:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal B_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
=
\left\{
|G_+,\eta_A\rangle,\,
|G_-,\eta_A\rangle
\right\}_{A=1}^{m},
\label{eq:min_nonenr_basis}
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(G_\pm=\pm G_*\) are the selected opposite shell modes;
\item \(\eta_A\) span the internal same-shell complement orthogonal to the enriched doublet.
\end{itemize}

Thus the minimal same-shell non-enriched block has dimension
\begin{equation}
2m\times 2m.
\label{eq:min_block_dim}
\end{equation}

\section{Block form of the matrix}

In this basis, the projected same-shell non-enriched block takes the form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
D_+(p) & M(p)\\
M(p)^\dagger & D_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:nonenr_block_matrix}
\end{equation}
where each entry is an \(m\times m\) matrix.

The diagonal valley blocks are
\begin{equation}
(D_\pm(p))_{AB}
=
\langle G_\pm,\eta_A|H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)|G_\pm,\eta_B\rangle,
\label{eq:Dpm_def}
\end{equation}
and the opposite-valley same-shell mixing block is
\begin{equation}
M_{AB}(p)
=
\langle G_+,\eta_A|H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)|G_-,\eta_B\rangle.
\label{eq:Mpm_def}
\end{equation}

\section{Leading expansion near the crossing}

Near \(p=0\), the working expansion is
\begin{equation}
D_\pm(p)
=
D_\pm^{(0)}
+
p_i D_{\pm,i}^{(1)}
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:Dpm_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
M(p)
=
M^{(0)}
+
p_i M_i^{(1)}
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:M_expand}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0)
+
p_i K^{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}_i
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:nonenr_expand_full}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
D_+^{(0)} & M^{(0)}\\
(M^{(0)})^\dagger & D_-^{(0)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:nonenr_zero_block}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact benchmark to compute}

The exact finite same-shell benchmark is the smallest singular spectral distance of this block from zero:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\sigma_{\min}\!\left(
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
\right),
}
\label{eq:nonenr_sigma_min}
\end{equation}
where \(\sigma_{\min}\) is the smallest absolute eigenvalue since the block is Hermitian.

At \(p=0\), a simpler sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{dist}\!\Bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0))
\Bigr)>0.
}
\label{eq:nonenr_zero_enough}
\end{equation}
If, in addition,
\begin{equation}
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
p_iK_i^{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}+O(|p|^2)
\right\|
<
\operatorname{dist}\!\Bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0))
\Bigr),
\label{eq:nonenr_perturb_bound}
\end{equation}
then
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}>0.
\]

\section{Minimal practical route}

Therefore the actual practical computation is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item construct \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)\);
\item identify the enriched \(4\)-dimensional Dirac carrier \(\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\);
\item take the orthogonal same-shell complement \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}\);
\item compute the finite matrix \(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0)\);
\item check whether its spectrum avoids zero;
\item then bound the \(p\)-dependent perturbation on \(|p|\le\rho\).
\end{enumerate}

So the non-enriched same-shell slot is reduced to one explicit finite matrix plus one perturbative radius estimate.

\section{Insertion into the final Step-IV benchmark}

The final working benchmark remains
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:nonenr_insert_bench}
\end{equation}

Hence the complete Step-IV closure condition is still the single inequality
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:nonenr_final_step4}
\end{equation}

The difference is that the same-shell non-enriched slot is now no longer abstract:
it is a concrete \(2m\times 2m\) Hermitian matrix eigenvalue problem.

\section{Final Summary}

The same-shell non-enriched sector is the only non-automatic Step-IV benchmark slot.
Its exact finite definition is
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
P_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)},
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\Bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p))
\Bigr).
\]

In the minimal working basis
\[
\mathcal B_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
=
\{|G_+,\eta_A\rangle,\ |G_-,\eta_A\rangle\}_{A=1}^{m},
\]
the block has the explicit form
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
D_+(p) & M(p)\\
M(p)^\dagger & D_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with \(m\times m\) valley-diagonal blocks \(D_\pm(p)\) and opposite-valley same-shell block \(M(p)\).

Near \(p=0\),
\[
D_\pm(p)=D_\pm^{(0)}+p_iD_{\pm,i}^{(1)}+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
M(p)=M^{(0)}+p_iM_i^{(1)}+O(|p|^2),
\]
so the benchmark reduces to the smallest absolute eigenvalue of a concrete finite Hermitian matrix.

A sufficient practical route is:
\[
\operatorname{dist}\!\Bigl(
0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(0))
\Bigr)>0
\]
plus a small-\(p\) perturbation bound on \(|p|\le \rho\).

Therefore the final Step-IV benchmark remains
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\},
\]
and Step IV is closed if
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]

So the same-shell non-enriched slot is now reduced to one concrete \(2m\times 2m\) Hermitian matrix eigenvalue problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Minimal \(m=1\) closure of the same-shell non-enriched slot}

\section{Goal}

We now take the minimal same-shell non-enriched truncation \(m=1\) and close the corresponding
benchmark by an explicit \(2\times 2\) Hermitian matrix criterion.

This is the first truly concrete version of the remaining Step-IV slot.

\section{Minimal basis and block}

Let the minimal same-shell non-enriched basis be
\[
\mathcal B_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}
=
\{|G_+,\eta\rangle,\ |G_-,\eta\rangle\},
\]
where \(\eta\) is one internal state orthogonal to the enriched shell doublet.

Then the projected non-enriched block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p) & m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)} & d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:m1_block}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
d_\pm(p)
=
\langle G_\pm,\eta|H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(1)}(p)|G_\pm,\eta\rangle,
\qquad
m(p)
=
\langle G_+,\eta|H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(1)}(p)|G_-,\eta\rangle.
\label{eq:m1_entries}
\end{equation}

Since the block is Hermitian, its eigenvalues are real and given exactly by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\pm(p)
=
\frac{d_+(p)+d_-(p)}{2}
\pm
\sqrt{
\left(\frac{d_+(p)-d_-(p)}{2}\right)^2+|m(p)|^2
}.
}
\label{eq:m1_eigs_exact}
\end{equation}

Therefore the same-shell non-enriched benchmark is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min\{|\lambda_+(p)|,|\lambda_-(p)|\}.
}
\label{eq:m1_gap_exact}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact zero-avoidance condition}

The block \eqref{eq:m1_block} has a zero eigenvalue iff
\begin{equation}
\det H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
d_+(p)d_-(p)-|m(p)|^2
=
0.
\label{eq:m1_zero_det}
\end{equation}

Hence a pointwise necessary and sufficient condition for spectral separation from zero is
\begin{equation}
d_+(p)d_-(p)-|m(p)|^2\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\lambda_\pm(p)\neq 0.
\label{eq:m1_pointwise_exact}
\end{equation}

For uniform positivity on \(|p|\le \rho\), one may of course work directly with
\eqref{eq:m1_gap_exact}, but a simpler closed sufficient criterion is preferable.

\section{Closed sufficient criterion I: same-sign diagonal sector}

Assume first that the two diagonal entries have the same sign on \(|p|\le \rho\), e.g.
\[
d_+(p)\ge 0,\qquad d_-(p)\ge 0.
\]
Then the smaller eigenvalue is
\[
\lambda_-(p)
=
\frac{d_+(p)+d_-(p)}{2}
-
\sqrt{
\left(\frac{d_+(p)-d_-(p)}{2}\right)^2+|m(p)|^2
}.
\]
Using the elementary inequality
\[
\lambda_-(p)\ge \min\{d_+(p),d_-(p)\}-|m(p)|,
\]
we obtain the uniform lower bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\ge
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min\{d_+(p),d_-(p)\}
-
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}|m(p)|.
}
\label{eq:m1_same_sign_bound}
\end{equation}

Therefore a closed sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min\{d_+(p),d_-(p)\}
>
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}|m(p)|.
}
\label{eq:m1_same_sign_suff}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:m1_same_sign_suff}, one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}>0.
}
\label{eq:m1_gap_pos_same_sign}
\end{equation}

\section{Closed sufficient criterion II: Gershgorin form}

A more basis-robust sufficient condition follows immediately from Gershgorin.
For the \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix \eqref{eq:m1_block},
each eigenvalue lies in the union of the discs
\[
\mathbb D\bigl(d_+(p),|m(p)|\bigr),
\qquad
\mathbb D\bigl(d_-(p),|m(p)|\bigr).
\]
Hence zero is excluded if
\begin{equation}
|d_+(p)|>|m(p)|,
\qquad
|d_-(p)|>|m(p)|.
\label{eq:m1_gersh_pointwise}
\end{equation}

Uniformly on \(|p|\le \rho\), this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min\{|d_+(p)|,|d_-(p)|\}
>
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}|m(p)|.
}
\label{eq:m1_gersh_uniform}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\ge
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min\{|d_+(p)|,|d_-(p)|\}
-
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}|m(p)|
>0.
}
\label{eq:m1_gersh_gap}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest practical sufficient criterion.

\section{Connection with the coercive decomposition theorem}

The current notes already state the general coercive route:
if
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
=
D_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
+
R_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
\]
with
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\]
then
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}>0.
\]

For \(m=1\), this theorem becomes completely explicit by taking
\begin{equation}
D_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p) & 0\\
0 & d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:m1_coercive_split}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min\{|d_+(p)|,|d_-(p)|\},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}|m(p)|.
\label{eq:m1_delta_eta}
\end{equation}

So the general theorem reduces exactly to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}>0,
}
\label{eq:m1_coercive_exact}
\end{equation}
which is the same as the uniform Gershgorin condition \eqref{eq:m1_gersh_uniform}.

\section{Small-\(p\) expansion}

Write
\begin{equation}
d_\pm(p)=d_\pm^{(0)}+p_i a_{\pm,i}+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
m(p)=m_0+p_i b_i+O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:m1_smallp}
\end{equation}

Then a sufficient zero-momentum closure condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\min\{|d_+^{(0)}|,|d_-^{(0)}|\}>|m_0|.
}
\label{eq:m1_zero_suff}
\end{equation}

If, in addition, the linear correction obeys
\begin{equation}
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\max\{|p_i a_{+,i}|,|p_i a_{-,i}|,|p_i b_i|\}
\le \varepsilon_\rho
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon_\rho
<
\min\{|d_+^{(0)}|,|d_-^{(0)}|\}-|m_0|,
\label{eq:m1_smallp_control}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}>0.
}
\label{eq:m1_smallp_gap}
\end{equation}

Thus the \(m=1\) slot is fully reduced to the three finite quantities
\[
d_+^{(0)},\qquad d_-^{(0)},\qquad m_0,
\]
plus one small-\(p\) perturbation budget.

\section{Insertion into the master Step-IV benchmark}

Replacing the non-enriched slot in the master benchmark, the working Step-IV gap becomes
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:m1_insert_master}
\end{equation}

Therefore the final Step-IV condition is still
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:m1_final_step4}
\end{equation}

The difference is that the last non-automatic slot is now an explicit \(2\times2\) inequality problem, not an abstract block.

\section{Final Summary}

In the minimal same-shell non-enriched truncation \(m=1\), the block is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p) & m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)} & d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Its exact eigenvalues are
\[
\lambda_\pm(p)
=
\frac{d_+(p)+d_-(p)}{2}
\pm
\sqrt{
\left(\frac{d_+(p)-d_-(p)}{2}\right)^2+|m(p)|^2
}.
\]
Hence
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min\{|\lambda_+(p)|,|\lambda_-(p)|\}.
\]

A clean closed sufficient condition is the uniform Gershgorin/coercive inequality
\[
\boxed{
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min\{|d_+(p)|,|d_-(p)|\}
>
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}|m(p)|.
}
\]
Under this condition,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}>0.
}
\]

Equivalently, in the coercive split
\[
D_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p) & 0\\
0 & d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one has
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min\{|d_+(p)|,|d_-(p)|\},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}|m(p)|,
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(1)}>0.
}
\]

At \(p=0\), a still simpler sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
\min\{|d_+^{(0)}|,|d_-^{(0)}|\}>|m_0|.
}
\]
With a small enough \(p\)-dependent perturbation budget, this extends to \(|p|\le \rho\).

Thus the last non-automatic same-shell slot is now reduced to an explicit \(2\times2\) Hermitian inequality problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Working PDE and its reduced Dirac form}

The current working microscopic PDE is
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X\,X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X\,X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi].
\]

It is linearized around the locked 12-mode BCC background
\[
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\phi_0(x),
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\]
and treated in the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p.
\]

After Bloch reduction and heavy-mediator elimination,
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k).
\]

The shell-projected infrared principal symbol is
\[
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\]

In the explicit concrete Class II local truncation,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\]

Thus the working PDE is summarized as:
\[
\boxed{
\text{microscopically: a refined locked TECT triplet PDE coupled to a heavy Class II mediator,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{infraredly: a graded }2+2\text{ Dirac-type first-order PDE with S2 symbol }A_1(p).
}
\]

\section{Final organized form of the current PDE}

\section{Microscopic working PDE}

The strongest explicit microscopic branch currently available is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X\,X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X\,X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi].
}
\label{eq:final_mic_pde}
\end{equation}

This is not yet claimed to be the final complete TECT action in full generality.
Rather, it is the strongest explicit branch in which the full-PDE derivation can be pushed concretely.

\section{Periodic background and Bloch reduction}

We linearize around the locked 12-mode BCC background
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\label{eq:final_locked_background}
\end{equation}

Using the folded Bragg convention,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|,
}
\label{eq:final_folded_bragg}
\end{equation}
the actual operator-construction chain is finite:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:final_operator_chain}
\end{equation}

\section{Reduced infrared PDE}

The shell-projected infrared principal symbol is the S2 branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:final_S2_symbol}
\end{equation}

Its nondegeneracy condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_nondeg_condition}
\end{equation}

\section{Concrete Class II coefficient form}

Inside the exact concrete Class II local branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:final_classII_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{transverse sector starts at }I_\theta\text{-order,}
\qquad
\text{longitudinal sector starts at primitive }I_{\theta'^3}\text{-order.}
}
\label{eq:final_branch_split}
\end{equation}

Hence the concrete Class II nondegeneracy test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_gc_test}
\end{equation}

\section{Remote-sector completion conditions}

For this reduced Dirac PDE to be the actual low-energy effective PDE, three further conditions are required.

\subsection{Zero constant mixing}

At \(p=0\),
\begin{equation}
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:final_V0}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Positive remote gap}

The remote block must satisfy a uniform gap condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\label{eq:final_remote_gap}
\end{equation}
A current explicit benchmark is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2 q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\label{eq:final_benchmark_gap}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Mass protection}

Finally, residual symmetry must forbid constant Dirac masses:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:final_mass_protection}
\end{equation}

\section{Final organized statement}

Thus the current PDE is organized in the following two-layer form:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic level: refined locked TECT triplet PDE coupled to a heavy Class II mediator.}
}
\label{eq:final_layer_micro}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Infrared level: a graded }2+2\text{ Dirac-type first-order PDE with principal symbol }A_1(p).
}
\label{eq:final_layer_ir}
\end{equation}

What is already closed:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the working microscopic branch \eqref{eq:final_mic_pde};
\item the Bloch/shell reduction pipeline \eqref{eq:final_operator_chain};
\item the reduced S2 infrared symbol \eqref{eq:final_S2_symbol};
\item the exact concrete Class II coefficient dictionary \eqref{eq:final_classII_coeffs};
\item the finite completion criteria \(V(0)=0\), \(\Delta_\rho>0\), and mass protection.
\end{enumerate}

What remains honestly open:
\begin{enumerate}
\item derive the actual transport kernel from the full complete TECT action rather than from the strongest explicit branch;
\item compute the actual microscopic values of \(g_c,g_E,g_O\) (equivalently \(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\));
\item decide whether complete TECT realizes a constant-leading longitudinal branch or only the primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\) branch;
\item evaluate the final same-shell non-enriched benchmark and remote mixing budget in the chosen truncation.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The current PDE is organized as follows.

Microscopic working PDE:
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\]

After Bloch reduction around the locked 12-mode BCC background and shell projection at
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\]
the infrared principal symbol becomes
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

In the exact concrete Class II branch,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\]
so the reduced nondegeneracy condition is
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Thus the current PDE has the following two-layer interpretation:
\[
\boxed{
\text{microscopically: refined locked TECT + heavy Class II mediator;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{infraredly: graded }2+2\text{ Dirac-type first-order PDE.}
}
\]

To make this the full low-energy effective PDE, one still needs:
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad
\Delta_\rho>0,\qquad
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
\]

So the reduced Dirac structure is already fixed, while the final complete microscopic coefficient extraction remains open.
